Daily, they adjust by day and night; monthly, they respond to the seasons, subtly aligning with celestial degrees, each movement following the Dipper’s alignment—hence the union with the Celestial Pivot. The Celestial Pivot is the Dipper’s pivot. The *Yimen Song* says: “Within the twelve gates, the lunar alignment shifts; the clepsydra’s flow follows time’s turning.” This is its moment.

The marvel of the supreme Dao lies herein: the ascent and descent of *Kan* and *Li* give birth to the numinous medicine, congealing the yellow sprout. For example, in the first month, aligned with *Yin*, *Lichun* occurs at the *Xu* hour, pointing to *Gen*; *Yushui* at the *Xu* hour, pointing to *Yin*—thus it is said: “Each month, always add the *Xu* hour; at each time, behold the Breaking Army.” The great medicine of the Golden Elixir is possessed by every household, yet not bound by marketplace or court. Alas! How many recognize the dragon when they see it, or the tiger? Few indeed reverse course to cultivate it.

In a fleeting moment, a precious pearl forms, large as a millet grain. An ancient poem says:
*“Brought forth, it gleams like rosy clouds upon the palm;
Swallowed, the palaces within the belly are renewed.”*
And again:
*“The great Dao thrives in court and market—
Those in the mountains know not, nor do they care.”*

The commentary says: The Golden Elixir, formed from the primordial *qi*, is completed through the postcelestial *qi* of the human body. The surging of wind and waves describes the body’s *qi* converging with the Golden Elixir. The birth of the dark pearl describes the body’s *qi* uniting with the elixir’s defense.

The *Zi* and *Wu* of the sun follow its passage; the *Zi* and *Wu* of the Dipper follow its initial alignment. These *Zi* and *Wu* are the cardinal directions of earth. Exhaustively applied, they move in tandem with sun and Dipper—this is the true master’s oral transmission. Where the sun aligns, spirit gathers—commonly called the “lunar general.” Where the Dipper points, *qi* stirs—commonly called the “lunar alignment.” Subtly aligning with celestial degrees, using the sun’s *Zi* and *Wu* while following the Dipper’s movement, the Dipper’s *Zi* and *Wu* divide day and night. The moon responds to the seasons, adjusting for waxing and waning. *Zi* generates, *Wu* wanes; south and north refer to *Zi* and *Wu*. Dawn and dusk likewise refer to *Zi* and *Wu*. From *Zi* to *Si* is dawn; from *Wu* to *Hai* is dusk—this is the immortals’ dawn and dusk, not the world’s sunrise and sunset.

Another method: at the solar term’s exchange, add the lunar alignment to *Hai*; at the mid-term’s exchange, add to *Xu*, to determine each time’s alignment. Master Peng, having divided the *Cantong Qi* into chapters and elucidated its true meaning, later read the four lines on the five phases’ inversion and disorderly movement, revealing the mechanism of heaven and earth’s mutual use and the Dao of yin and yang’s return. Thus he composed the *Black Lead and Fire Tiger Treatise* and the *Red Lead and Fire Dragon Formula*, naming them *The Inner Image of the Returned Elixir* and *The Golden Key*. His discussions of the tiger’s essence and the dragon’s function both concern the great elixir’s transformations. Now, the Nameless One borrows these to distinguish the inner and outer elixirs, adopting the titles but not the texts. Though not the work of the True Unity Master, the principles remain coherent.

All people inherently possess the medicine of long life, yet in delusion, they cast it away. When sweet dew descends, heaven and earth unite, and the yellow sprout is born where *Kan* and *Li* intersect. The well frog claims no dragon’s cave; the wren on the fence knows not the phoenix’s nest. When the elixir ripens, gold naturally fills the house—why seek herbs or burn thatch?

The commentary says: Sweet dew and yellow sprout are alternate names for the Golden Elixir. Heaven and earth, *Kan* and *Li*, are images of dragon and tiger. When the *qi* of heaven and earth intermingles, sweet dew descends; when the *qi* of *Kan* and *Li* intersects, the yellow sprout is born. The union of dragon and tiger’s paths, the true unity *qi*’s congealment—this supreme treasure is possessed by every household. Yet because it is too near, it is slighted and discarded, unaware that this is the numinous ladder to ascension.

Modern scholars often cling to side doors—non-dual solitary yin, solitary yang, methods where the center generates, where encounter is easy but completion difficult—and thus err in their own bodies. They know not that this Dao is simple and easily accomplished, like the well’s frog or the fence’s sparrow—how could they know of dragon caves or phoenix nests?

The millet-grain pearl, once suspended, is the gold of heaven and earth, ready to be scooped up. Formerly, Shao Gangzhong was skilled in the arts of the yellow and white; the world called him the Little Huainan Prince. Later, he met the immortal Han Zitao, the Dharma Master, by the water, and served him as a disciple. He presented a hundred *yi* of mercury and gold as tribute, but Tao merely smiled and paid no heed. Shao then swore a blood oath, and Tao finally transmitted the teaching.

Upon completion, Tao took a handful of mercury, rinsed his mouth with it, and spat it into a water basin. The water surged and boiled, then settled into a lump of purple gold—demonstrating the inner elixir’s great medicine, possessing such divine marvels. How could one see this through years of toiling with herbs or burning thatch?

The scripture does not say: “The earth’s treasury releases its form as gold and jade dew”—this is further proof.

The commentary says: Lü Chunyang turned mud, tiles, and stones into gold; the Southern Tang’s Geng Xian’gu molded snow into silver; Chen Niuwan dried mercury instantly. The *Transmission of the Dao Collection* says: “In the mouth, mercury can be dried”—all signs of the elixir’s ripening.

The Seventh: Know that the source of the elixir’s production lies solely in the southwest—this is its native land. When lead meets *gui*, it is born and must be swiftly gathered; when gold meets the full moon, it is too distant and unfit for tasting. Return it to the earthen crucible, seal it firmly, then introduce the flowing pearl to pair with it. The medicine weighs one *jin*, requiring the balance of two eights to harmonize. The firing times rely on yin and yang.

The *Western Florescence Scripture* says: “The medicine is born in the west and gathered in *wu-si*.” Harvest it at the proper time, and the work will proceed day by day. The southwest is the *kun* earth, the place where the tiger is born. The *kun* direction is also where the moon is born—thus it is called the native land. The moon is the essence of metal and water; when the upper and lower *kan* unite, the elixir is formed. Therefore, the true source of the golden elixir’s medicinal materials indeed arises from the *kun* earth.

When lead meets *gui*, the time is *chou*; when gold meets the full moon, the month is *wei*. The moon’s fullness resides in the mouth; the secret of the hour lies in the heart’s transmission. The breath of the celestial cycle is subtle, its count as faint as the dripping of a jade clepsydra—this is the true oral transmission, passed mouth to mouth in strictest secrecy.

Lu Sicheng, in his postscript to the *Awakening to Reality*, says: “Those who transmit these poems often err, mistaking *lead* for *if* and *gold* for *like*, greatly distorting the Elder Immortal’s intent. Lead and gold are the golden elixir itself.” Lu exposed the error to correct the misreading of “fish” for “ru,” yet guarded the source, fearing its spread through written records. We who receive the master’s oral teaching know this well. If not, even within the empty void five *zhang* from the earth, the millet-grain pearl is not easily obtained.

Alas, how many pursue side paths, taking mere facets for lead and gold, gathering at the *gui* hour in the sky—truly child’s play! There are also those who speak of *kun* receiving *gui*, like Ye Wenshu, who deserve only a laugh. The golden elixir requires work to begin at the *gui* day’s *zi* hour—no delay, no passing moment—thus the urgency of gathering. Once the full moon recedes, the *wei* qi wanes, making it unfit for tasting.

On the *gui* day, the hidden time is *ren-zi*, with *tian-ren* and *di-gui* converging in the north. Thus, the *Zhu Zhen Yi Commentary* says: “At the dark of the moon, at dawn, the *kan* moon and *li* sun unite at *ren-gui*. The *kan* moon is *wu*; the *li* sun is *si*. At dusk on the third day, the *zhen* image appears as the moon emerges at *geng*; on the eighth day, the *dui* image appears as the moon manifests at *ding*; on the fifteenth, the *qian* image appears as the moon waxes at *jia-ren*; at dawn on the sixteenth, the *xun* image appears as the moon wanes at *xin*; on the twenty-third, the *gen* image appears as the moon diminishes at *bing*; on the thirtieth, the *kun* image appears as the moon vanishes at *yi*, hiding *gui*. At the dark of the moon, at dawn, the *kan* water of the moon flows to *wu*; at noon, the *li* fire of the sun reaches *si*. This is the crucial celestial mechanism—it must be transmitted orally, for it cannot be conveyed in writing. Without a true master, one merely guesses and forces interpretations.

Ingest the elixir into the *dantian*, within the earthen crucible, sealing the embryo to prevent leakage. Circulate the fire-dragon’s flowing-pearl mercury to pair with it, and the sacred embryo will form. The raven’s liver weighs eight *liang*; the hare’s marrow, half a *jin*—together they make sixteen *liang*, hence “the medicine weighs one *jin*, requiring the balance of two eights.” The fire is not truly fire but borrows the harmonized operation of yin and yang’s two qi.

The commentary says: When people gather at the time of *gui*’s birth, some take *tian-gui*, others hide the *gui* hour—how can they know the secret of *Awakening to Reality*? “The time is *chou*” means the hour has passed; “the month is *wei*” means the day has passed. Once day and hour pass, the lead’s breath fades, the gold’s fullness wanes—gathering yields nothing, tasting brings no effect. The *Book of Changes* says: “Water flows to the damp; fire seeks the dry.” Flowing and seeking are the natures of water and fire. *Wu-si* is the earth between water and fire; water flows and fire seeks, both embracing *wu-si* to generate *ren-gui*. *Ren-gui* is where the sun and moon conceal their function; *wu-si* is where they display their brilliance. *Ren-gui* encircle *zi*; *xu* and *ji* encircle *wu*. *Zi* and *wu* are the new and full moons—this is the wondrous function of the moon’s soul and spirit, the golden elixir. For details, see the “Small Celestial Cycle” in the first month. Yang is fire; yin is also fire. There is no true fire—it is the essence of heaven, earth, sun, and moon, borrowed and operated.

The Eighth: Do not refine the Three Yellows or Four Spirits; seeking among myriad herbs is even less the true path. When yin and yang attain the proper phase and unite, the two eights balance, naturally merging in the deep pool. The sun at the bottom turns red, dispelling yin’s monstrosities; the moon atop the mountain shines white, sprouting new medicinal shoots. Let people recognize true lead and mercury—they are not common cinnabar or quicksilver.

The Three Yellows and Four Spirits—gold, stone, plants, and wood—are all post-heaven, earth-born dregs. How can they transform the formed into the formless? External things cannot form the embryo; grafting flowers cannot bear fruit. The true One’s *qi* arises before heaven and earth, vast and unfathomable. When the two eights in proper phase unite, they merge in the intimate, steaming union of attraction, stirring into manifestation. “Proper phase” means the emotionless emotion, the colorless color—precisely the raven’s liver of eight *liang* and the hare’s marrow of half a *jin*. When these two eights in proper phase unite and merge, the true One’s *qi* returns to the cavity of attraction, congealing into a millet-grain pearl—this is the marvel of the Dao.

The deep pool is yin; the sun is yang.

At the bottom of the deep pool, the sun glows crimson—this is the yang within yin. The yang within yin is pure yang, devoid of yin *qi*, hence it is called "the vanquishing of yin’s monstrosities." This is the *qi* of the tiger’s essence, termed "red lead," the yang of the mountain. The moon is yin; the moon atop the mountain gleams white—this is the yin within yang. It is the *qi* of the dragon’s essence, the initial stirring of *qi*, thus called "the tender sprout of medicine," termed "black mercury." An ancient song says: "Red lead and black mercury are the great elixir’s head. To merge red into black is true cultivation"—this is what it means.

The sage, using these two substances in a single moment, refines them into a grain of yang elixir within the Northern Sea, blazing like the sun piercing through a curtain. When ingested, it instantly enters the abdomen, and the yin mercury within the self—all the yin and malevolent *qi* of the body—vanishes entirely, just as the dawn sun rises from the Eastern Sea, blazing and illuminating, dispelling all yin’s monstrosities. The yin mercury, from the lower cinnabar field to the peak of the head, newly receives the *qi* of the yang elixir, gradually congealing and sprouting tender new shoots—hence "the tender sprout of medicine." It is like the new moon at dawn, exchanging *qi* with the sun; as the sun sets, it emits a faint glow in the west, at the *geng* earth, resembling the crescent moon—its light fresh and tender, like the tender sprout of medicine. This describes the symbolic forms of the inner and outer medicines.

The *Western Florescence Scripture* says: "The yin within yang is called the *nüwa* maiden; the yang within yin is called the *gong* metal lord." These are the husband and wife within the crucible, the steps to the Purple Palace. Those who awaken to this become immortals before their very eyes; those who remain deluded are separated by ten thousand miles of drifting sand. The true lead and true mercury of the outer medicine are the initial *qi* of the dragon and tiger. The true lead and true mercury within are the golden elixir and the self’s true *qi*. Those of this age who seek to recognize true lead and mercury—only these are real; all else falls short of the supreme Dao. These two true substances can transform the formed into the formless, becoming true immortals. How can ordinary cinnabar and common mercury compare?

A commentary says: The alchemical classics transmitted in the world often extract mercury from cinnabar, calling it "true mercury," or use cinnabar as the "golden body," refining it into an elixir. This wastes wealth and time, with few successes. Even if achieved, many who consume it perish—all because they fail to recognize true lead and true mercury.

Within yang lies yin essence, its substance not firm.
Cultivating this alone only weakens the body.
Breathing exercises and guiding *qi* are not the Way;
Absorbing mist and dining on dawn are but madness.
The world blindly seeks lead and mercury—
When will they witness the dragon and tiger descend?
I urge you to exhaustively seek the source of life,
Return to the root, restore the origin—this is the King of Medicines.

A note says: The yin essence within yang is the self’s true essence. Essence generates *qi*, *qi* generates spirit—nothing is greater for nourishing and defending the body. When the oil is exhausted, the lamp goes out; when the marrow is depleted, the person dies. This shows that essence and *qi* are the root of the body. Yet this substance belongs to yin, its nature not firm—like cinnabar containing mercury, or fire born within wood, its nature prone to flight. Day by day, it is lost through urine, sweat, tears, and saliva, difficult to capture and unwilling to be refined. Thus, the sage called it the "flowing pearl of the great yang," its nature fierce and violent. Without the true One’s yang elixir to restrain it, and the yang fire within yin to nurture it, it cannot congeal and transform. Cultivating this alone only leads to emaciation; guiding *qi* and laboring the body are not the true Way. Absorbing mist and dining on dawn are the acts of madmen. Even if one ingests the essence of the sun and moon, fills the five viscera with light, circulates the twin passes at the spine, replenishes the brain, and returns essence—even if one achieves corpse liberation, womb entry, spirit departure, or deep meditation—all these thousands of methods amount to nothing more than cultivating this single yin essence within yang. A solitary yin without yang is like a hen trying to hatch an egg alone—how can it succeed?

Master Zhongli said: Tears, saliva, fluids, essence, *qi*, blood, and humor—these seven numinous substances are all yin. If one takes these as the basis of the elixir, how can one ascend to the Jade Capital? From this, it is clear that within the body, not only is true essence yin—all five viscera and six bowels are yin, not yang. How can one take the heart and kidneys as *kan* and *li*, the liver and lungs as dragon and tiger? How can one use spirit and *qi* as mother and child, or fluids and saliva as lead and mercury? If one clings to these in cultivating the body, seeking the proof of pure yang, it is like trying to dispel cold by adding ice, or cure dampness with hot water—like making a flying phoenix dance with a snake, only increasing the disorder.

The *Unity of the Three* says:
"Make two maidens dwell together,
Their beauty most fair.
Su Qin’s persuasive words,
Zhang Yi’s matchmaking,
Unbound hair and sharp tongues,
Striving to craft fine speech,
Opening their hearts to harmony,
Becoming husband and wife—
Yet in the end, hair rots and teeth decay,
Never truly knowing one another."

This metaphor speaks of marrying a woman to a woman, refining yin with yin—how can there be a way of generation through attraction? The true dragon and true tiger are the two eights.

The true lead and true mercury are the qi of the dragon and tiger’s two essences. This Dao is most simple, not complex; most near, not distant. Yet scholars cling to perverse obstinacy, taking the medicines of side paths and heterodox ways as lead and mercury, while dismissing the true formulas of the Great Dao as false—deeply lamentable indeed. Thus Master Zhongli said:

*"Seeking immortality without knowing true lead and mercury,
One may read ten thousand volumes of alchemical classics in vain.
Failing to grasp the subtle meaning within,
One slanders true words as empty speech."*

Therefore, the Immortal Elder directly points to the source where lead and mercury arise, where the body is born, where life is established—returning to this root, reverting to this origin. By inverting the practice, the true dragon and true tiger will naturally descend; true lead and true mercury will naturally submit. Apart from the king among medicines, who could attain this?

In recent times, many take sixteen-year-old boys and girls, have them unite and emit essence to form an embryo, calling it "Primordial Embryo Elixir" or "Purple River Vehicle," regarding this as the golden elixir and great medicine. This is like grafting bamboo to the moon—how much farther from the truth could one stray? All that is born of post-heaven, possessing form and substance, is not the supreme medicine. For what lies below form is not the Dao of pre-heaven.

The *Commentary* says: The *Unity of the Three* originally used "flowing pearl of the great yang" as a metaphor for the difficulty of subduing numinous mercury. Now the Nameless One borrows it to illustrate the mercury within the human body—this interpretation also holds. The *Laozi* states: "All things bear yin and embrace yang," for all are formed through yin and yang. Humans and the myriad things are never without yang; why then is the human body regarded entirely as yin? Because it is born of post-heaven, possessing substance. Once substance exists, it is constrained by yin, yang, and the Five Phases, thus becoming yin. Therefore, it cannot transform.

The *Unity of the Three* says: "Things without yin and yang violate heaven and oppose the origin." Master Peng says: "Solitary yin or solitary yang cannot generate on their own." The marvel of external medicine is not without yin. Why then is it called pure yang? Because its qi is obtained from pre-heaven, born without substance. Born without substance, it can transform the formed into the formless, thus converting post-heaven qi into pre-heaven qi, making it pure yang—hence it is called yang.

Someone may ask: "Within yang lies yin essence; if its substance is not firm, it cannot be used. Yet now you speak of nurturing it with yang fire within yin—why?" This is the true fire within the great and small crucibles. The human body, being purely yin, has only the true fire of the primordial sea. If one obtains the yang elixir to restrain it, it will no longer flee. Then, nurturing it with yang fire within yin, the returning elixir can congeal. Thus, yin essence cannot be cultivated alone; it must be cultivated in tandem. Through breath and nurturance, following the fire of the great and small crucibles, returning it to the body, the returning elixir naturally coagulates and transforms.

In the great and small crucibles, it is called "yang fire within yin"; in the human body, it is called "yang essence within yin"; in immortal formulas, it is called "Purple River Vehicle." Not only does it replenish and heal the ailing body, but it truly transforms form and spirit.

---

*Ten*
Diligently seek the true lead,
Lest time slip by in vain.
Capture the earthly po with cinnabar mercury,
And the heavenly hun will naturally restrain water-metal.
This may be called the Dao’s height—dragons and tigers submit;
One may speak of virtue’s weight—spirits and gods revere.
Already knowing longevity equals heaven and earth,
Afflictions have no cause to arise in the heart.

*Annotation*: True lead is the golden elixir. The earthly po, in external medicine, is the White Tiger; in internal medicine, it is the golden elixir. The heavenly hun, in external medicine, is the Green Dragon; in internal medicine, it is one’s own body. Cinnabar mercury, externally, is the qi of the dragon’s essence; internally, it is one’s own true fluid. Water-metal, externally, is the qi of the tiger’s essence; internally, it is the golden elixir. It is also called "mercury within cinnabar" and "silver within water"—these metaphors illustrate internal and external matters.

The Immortal Elder exhorts practitioners of the true to cultivate the golden elixir to transcend life and death, not to waste their days in vain. Capture the White Tiger to subdue the dragon, and the Green Dragon will naturally restrain the tiger. The two qi intermingle to produce the golden elixir. Once the golden elixir is obtained, swallow it into the abdomen to capture one’s own true qi. One’s own true fluid, longing for the golden elixir, congeals into the sacred embryo. When the true dragon and true tiger within have descended, the dragons and tigers beyond the world will naturally submit. When the internal refinement of spirit and soul, gods and demons, attains sageliness, the gods beyond the world will naturally revere. Apart from those of lofty Dao and profound virtue, who could attain this? The body transforms into pure yang, longevity equals heaven and earth, and one roams carefree beyond the world, at ease among humans. All myriad thoughts dissolve—what afflictions could remain?

---

*Eleven*
Yellow sprout and white snow are not hard to find,
But the adept must rely on deep virtue and conduct.
The Four Symbols and Five Phases fully depend on earth;
The Three Origins and Eight Trigrams—how could they leave ren?
Refined into numinous substance, few recognize it;
Dissolving yin demons, gods dare not invade.
Wishing to leave secret formulas among humans,
Yet not meeting a single true kindred spirit.

*Annotation*: The qi of the dragon is called "yellow sprout"; the fluid of the tiger is called "white snow." The root of the great medicine truly lies here. The Dao is most simple; the matter is not difficult. Yet without grand merit and great conduct, one cannot encounter a true teacher to transmit the profound mysteries.

The Great Dao originates from emptiness and nothingness, giving birth to the One Qi. The One Qi generates yin and yang—called dragon and tiger. The dragon, wood, generates fire; the tiger, metal, generates water. Wood, fire, metal, and water combine to form the Four Symbols. The Four Symbols unite to form the elixir, whose foundation lies in earth. Earth has no fixed position but flourishes in the four seasons. Without earth in the four seasons, the four sequences cannot proceed, and the myriad things cannot be born. Thus, the Four Symbols and Five Phases fully depend on earth.

*Ren* is water—it is the qi of the true one, called "True One Water." Existing before heaven and earth, it transforms into the yang dragon and yin tiger. Dragon and tiger unite to form the elixir—elixir is earth. Dragon is wood; tiger is metal.

The Three Natures and Three Origins do not depart from the transformations of True One Water. The Eight Trigrams are the qi of the True One—its first transformation becomes Heaven, called *Qian*, the Father; its second transformation becomes Earth, called *Kun*, the Mother. *Qian*, with its yang qi, seeks *Kun*’s yin qi: the first seeking gives birth to the eldest son, *Zhen*; the second seeking gives birth to the middle son, *Kan*; the third seeking gives birth to the youngest son, *Gen*—this is *Qian*’s qi intermingling with *Kun*’s qi to produce the three yang. Then *Kun*, with its yin qi, seeks *Qian*’s yang qi: the first seeking gives birth to the eldest daughter, *Xun*; the second seeking gives birth to the middle daughter, *Li*; the third seeking gives birth to the youngest daughter, *Dui*—this is *Kun*’s qi intermingling with *Qian*’s qi to produce the three yin. These, too, do not depart from the transformations of True One Water. Thus, the Three Origins and Eight Trigrams—how could they depart from *ren*?

Not only the Three Origins and Eight Trigrams do not depart from the essence of the True One. Since the beginning of creation, all that has form and name arises from this and is transformed by it. The True One Master says: The essence of the True One is the Mother of Heaven and Earth, the Root of Yin and Yang, the Origin of Water and Fire, the Ancestor of Sun and Moon, the Source of the Three Powers, the Progenitor of the Five Phases. All things rely upon it to be born and completed; the thousand spirits receive it to manifest joy and sorrow. Even the vast heavens, the deep earth, the grotto-heavens, the sacred mountains, the numinous images, the divine officials, the immortals, the sages, the hosts of wind and rain, darkness and light, spring, summer, autumn, and winter—before any sign appears, none does not arise from this lead qi and undergo transformation.

For the cultivator of the elixir, obtaining True One Water completes all matters. Swallowing the millet of the True One into the five viscera and circulating the fire for ten months refines away all yin, transmuting it into pure yang—the True One Immortal. The yin demons and corpse-worms flee, finding no escape. The Immortal Elder wished to preserve this secret for the world, yet none have been found worthy of its transmission—so vast is the gulf, so far removed from human sentiment.

For those whose good roots are planted and whose numinous bones are endowed, immortality may be hoped for. The endowment of numinous bones and the planting of good roots—these are not merely "one gives birth to two, two gives birth to three," but among the countless billions of births, only those who plant myriad good roots may, upon emerging, drift lightly with the bearing of one who has transcended the dust. Alas! The walking corpses and moving cadavers, with but a single bottle and bowl, would ascend as immortals—yet those who attain immortality are not easily found.

Why not examine your own heart and ask: does it differ from the hearts of the ordinary? Or does it not differ at all?

My immortal arts, too, know no bounds. Yet one must take upon oneself the task of vast transformation and adaptability, standing alone above the age like a crane among chickens. Though others may laugh at me as impractical, I know I am no common mortal. The Red Lord and Red Pine are my friends; Penglai and Fangzhang, my home. Naturally, I have encountered extraordinary men and received the transmission of the supreme Dao, forming bonds with kindred spirits. Once the elixir of a single grain of millet is complete, the immortal elder wishes to leave this untransmitted secret in the world—yet blame not the rarity of those who meet its conditions. How might one find such a person?

The *Shu* says: "Earth" speaks of the ultimate realm of defense. "Ren" speaks of the inception of life. The true and unified water is the qi before form; the true and unified grain of millet is the qi after form. The four images each contain one true earth, and four make five; two and three make five—thus the four images are all earth. Ren is water, born of Heaven’s One. Ren stands at the head of the first yang in the *zi* hour (that is, the end of *hai* and the beginning of *zi*), the origin of generative qi and the forerunner of the five phases. Thus all begins with Ren.

The True One said: The essence of the true and unified alone accomplishes transformation. As stated in the *Golden Key*, all lead and mercury arise from this—it is the numinous water of the true and unified. The twelve [months]: In grasses and trees, yin and yang are equally matched. If either is lacking, no fragrance blooms. First the green leaves, yang, take the lead; then the red flowers, yin, follow. This is the constant Way of daily use, the true source. Yet who knows to return to it?

I say to those who study the Dao: If you do not recognize yin and yang, do not act recklessly.

The *Zhu* says: Before grasses and trees sprout, they contain the purest simplicity. When their shells split, they receive the one qi to germinate. Thus they first send forth a single shoot to symbolize the one qi, then divide into two leaves to symbolize yin and yang. Between the two leaves, a bud emerges to correspond to the Three Powers. Beyond this, they gradually branch out: flowers and leaves flourish, spring brings forth growth and the opening of green leaves, summer fosters expansion and the blooming of red flowers—all driven by yang’s urging. Autumn brings solemnity and fruition, winter brings decay and returns to the soil—all driven by yin’s urging. Yin and yang, equally matched, give rise to endless generation. If either is lacking, the myriad things do not come to be.

Thus the True One said: Solitary yin does not produce; solitary yang does not complete. Therefore, when heaven and earth intermingle in misty union, the myriad things are transformed and harmonized; when male and female unite in essence, the myriad things are generated. The common people take this as their daily constant, yet do not know the true source, the wondrous principle of the reversal and interplay of yin and yang. One who can refine this may transcend life and death. If scholars do not understand this and instead mock me, it is they who are self-deluded.

Not recognizing the reversal within the mysterious, how can one know how to plant lotuses in fire? Leading the White Tiger home to nurture it, one gives birth to a luminous pearl like the full moon. Do not merely guard the elixir furnace and defend the firing times; simply settle the spirit and rest in naturalness. When the host of yin is exhausted, the elixir matures, and one leaps free from the cage to live ten thousand years.

The *Zhu* says: By human affairs, a man cannot become pregnant, nor can lotuses be planted in fire. Yet the wondrous and mysterious Dao of immortals possesses the art of reversal. Thus it can make a man pregnant, just as it can plant lotuses in fire. Why? The sun, *li*, is male but becomes female when reversed; the moon, *kan*, is female but becomes male when reversed—this is the meaning of reversal. When the two are reversed, they can generate the elixir. Refining one’s own yin mercury to form the sacred embryo and nurturing the infant—this is a man becoming pregnant, just as planting lotuses in fire. Is this not reversal?

Thus the immortal elder, reading the *Cantong Qi*, said: "The five phases move in reverse, and the elixir body remains numinous and ever-present." Water reverses to earth, earth to wood, wood to metal, metal to fire, fire to water—this is the subtlety of reversal. The meaning of reversal is clear.

The Green Dragon and White Tiger are originally the essence of the true and unified, transformed into two things, positioned east and west. In reality, they emerge from the same source but bear different names. The essence of the true and unified belongs to mercury, and mercury is the dragon in the east—thus the essence of the true and unified resides in the east. The White Tiger is originally the child of the true and unified’s essence, lodging its body in the west, though its home is in the east. Thus the immortal elder said: "The Metal Duke is originally the son of the eastern family, sent to lodge in the western neighbor. Recognize him, call him home to nurture, and match him with the Alchemical Maiden as kin." The Metal Duke is lead; the Alchemical Maiden is mercury. Using lead to refine one’s own mercury and form the sacred embryo—this is leading the White Tiger home to nurture, matching it with the Green Dragon as husband and wife, giving birth to a luminous pearl like the full moon.

The "full moon" refers to the adept of elixir refinement first obtaining the upper *kan* at the western edge, a half-moon of eight ounces of yang metal, then obtaining the lower *li* at the eastern edge, a half-moon of half a catty of yin water. Combining these two half-moons generates the elixir, yielding a single grain of golden elixir like the full moon. This is akin to Master Daoguang’s Chan saying: "A single grain of numinous elixir weighs one catty"—for it is formed by two eight-ounce measures combining into one catty. This analogy pertains to the external medicine’s symbolic form.

After obtaining this elixir and swallowing it into one’s abdomen, the golden elixir becomes the White Tiger. One then leads this White Tiger into one’s abdomen to match it with one’s own mercury. Thereafter, one circulates the yin tally and yang fire through the sixty-four hexagrams, refining it into a single grain of golden liquid return elixir, also weighing one catty and resembling the full moon. This analogy pertains to the internal medicine’s symbolic form.

The internal elixir resembles the full moon because the firing hexagrams—each with six lines, sixty-four hexagrams totaling three hundred eighty-four lines—symbolize one catty and three hundred eighty-four *zhu*. The external elixir resembles the full moon because one catty comprises the two half-moons of the upper and lower *kan*, the number eight, hence its resemblance to the full moon.

The *Cantong Qi* states: "The upper *kan*’s number is eight; the lower *gen*’s is also eight. When the two *kan* unite their essence, the body of *qian* and *kun* is complete. Two eights correspond to one catty." The Dao of the *Yi* is perfectly balanced. Thus the True One said: The upper and lower *kan*’s one-catty measure is divided into three hundred eighty-four *zhu* to operate the fire tally and line numbers.

The immortal elder’s indication of the full moon’s meaning is to enable scholars to thoroughly understand the workings of creation, distinguishing the internal and external two eights’ numbers, which cannot be discussed indiscriminately.

The fire is not the common fire of the human realm—it is the primordial ancestral qi, the qi of yin and yang that makes no sound. Nor is there any elixir to guard; such talk is mere idle chatter. Master Qingxia said: "The crucible is no metal crucible; the furnace is no jade furnace. Fire arises from below *li*; water moves toward the center of *kan*. When the Three Essences are securely joined, the Two Substances naturally bind and solidify. The embryo is sealed, no leakage occurs, and transformation happens in an instant."

Gao Xiangxian said: "Heaven and earth intermingle; male and female unite. The Four Images and Five Phases gather like spokes to a hub. Day and night alternate through *zhun* and *meng*, following nature’s pattern. Diligently tend the fire phases—this is no mundane crucible or furnace, but the fire within the crucible of nature itself. Simply settle the spirit, regulate the breath, and let it unfold naturally. Refine with civil and martial measures, and the tally of time will not err by even a fraction. Within half a watch, the elixir is attained. Then, following this method, advance and retreat with yin tally and yang fire, applying withdrawal and addition to guard against danger and avert peril. After ten months, the work is complete: all yin is stripped away, the body transmutes into pure yang, and one leaps free from the cage of dust, attaining ten thousand years of life. This is the method of the Golden Liquor Returned Elixir.

Yet this is not yet the ultimate mystery. One must further embrace the One for nine years, returning the essence to spirit, to achieve the Nine-Turn Golden Liquor Great Returned Elixir. At that time, form and spirit are both wondrous, and one merges with the Dao in truth."

The Commentary states: Mercury is the Flowing Pearl of Grand Yang. When it obtains the Golden Flower, it congeals into the Golden Elixir. The Golden Elixir arises fundamentally from the Flowing Pearl of Grand Yang, and the Flowing Pearl of Grand Yang, in turn, arises from the Azure Dragon of the East—thus it is the son of the East. The Metal Duke is none other than the Golden Elixir, originally the son of the Eastern House. The Flowing Pearl of Grand Yang lodges its form within the Golden Flower of the West to take birth.

Zhang and Sui’s annotations to the *Triple Concordance Canon* say: A month has thirty days and three hundred sixty hours, which mirror the small crucible and furnace. A year has twelve months, and the hexagrams, qi, seasonal nodes, and fire phases of advance and retreat mirror the great crucible and furnace. Through calculation and agitation, six hundred chapters are composed—this is not the fire of the mundane world. The immortals sigh that common people do not recognize true fire, so they establish the images of hexagrams and lines. Yet the hexagrams are but the trap and snare of fire; once the function of fire is seen, the hexagrams and lines may be forgotten. Master Wu Ming’s commentary is based on this.

Fourteen, three-five-one—these three characters together: truly enlightened ones have been rare through the ages. East three and south two together make five; north one and west four together make five. Wu and Ji naturally return to the generative number five. When the three families meet, the infant is formed. Thus we know that the Great One contains true essence, and after ten months, the embryo is complete, laying the foundation for sagehood.

The commentary states: The "three-five-one" cannot be separated from dragon and tiger. The dragon pertains to wood; wood’s number is three and resides in the east. Wood can generate fire, thus the dragon’s essence pertains to fire. Fire’s number is two and resides in the south. These two things share the same source, so three and two combine to form the singular five. The tiger pertains to metal; metal’s number is four and resides in the west. Metal can generate water, thus the tiger’s lead-qi pertains to water. Water’s number is one and resides in the north. These two things share the same palace, so four and one combine to form the second five. The two fives of these two things meet in the central palace of *wu* and *ji*. The central palace pertains to earth, and earth’s generative number is five—this is the "three-five." When the three and five unite, the elixir is formed; the elixir is the one. Thus it is called "three-five-one." From ancient times to the present, those who can unite the three-five-one to form the elixir and fully comprehend the infant are truly rare. The "one" is the golden elixir; the "infant" is the elixir itself. The elixir is the one, the one is the true qi of the primordial unity, the mother-qi of heaven and earth. One’s true qi is the child-essence of heaven and earth. Drawing the mother-qi inward to the five viscera to subdue the child-essence is like a cat crouching over a mouse to prevent its escape. The qi of mother and child long for each other within the womb, coalescing into the singular infant. Thus it is said: "The Great One contains the true qi," meaning it holds the true essence of the one, just as a person carries a child for ten months before giving birth. The sacred embryo is the same: after ten months of work, it naturally becomes spiritually perfected. Thus it is said: "After ten months, the embryo is complete, laying the foundation for sagehood." Later generations take the kidneys to be the infant—how could they possess such efficacy?

The commentary further states: The numbers one, two, three, four, and five are generative numbers; they are the beginnings of form, yet remain formless. These are not the five phases of the mundane world with tangible qualities, but the qi of heaven and earth in their primordial emptiness. The numbers six, seven, eight, nine, and ten are completion numbers; they possess form and are not the formless five phases of the primordial. These are the five phases of the later heaven. Heaven-one and earth-four combine to make five, and the central five completes ten. Heaven-three and earth-two combine to make five, and the central five completes ten. The two fives pair together, also combining into the celestial number twenty-five. The golden elixir is formed from the five phases of the primordial, so only the generative numbers of the five phases are taken. To regard the kidneys as the infant or the heart as the maiden, to focus on the inner and outer landscapes, or to practice visualization of spirits and deities—these are all yin methods and thus devoid of efficacy.

Fifteen.
Not recognizing true lead as the true ancestor,
A thousand efforts are wasted in vain.
Resting wives and recklessly severing yin and yang,
The grains are merely left to empty the intestines.
Herbs, trees, gold, and silver—all are mere dregs;
Clouds, mist, sun, and moon—all are but illusions.
Even with breath-work and visualization,
None align with the work of the golden elixir.

The commentary states: The essential point of true lead lies in taking the qi of the two eights as its foundation; all else is not the supreme Dao and wastes effort. The *Breaking Delusion Song* of Yimen says:
*"Solitary yin is not the Way;
Yin and yang lose their proper place."*
Master Wang Zhenren says: "Disciples must first part from wives and concubines, for without non-action, there is nothing that cannot be done." Gao Xiangxian says:
*"Sometimes yang, solitary and roosting;
Sometimes yin, dwelling alone."*
These words all refer to the meaning of solitary yin and widowed yang, the cultivation of a single thing. Some, not understanding, cling to this saying and practice the bedchamber arts of controlling women, slandering the immortal Dao. Who shall bear the blame? They do not know that this speaks of the metaphor of yang as husband and yin as wife—it is not the husband and wife of the human world. The *Breaking Delusion Song* says:
*"Abandoning grains is not the Way;
After death, one becomes a hungry ghost."*
All the above—post-heavenly, earth-born, impure dregs—are easily encountered yet difficult to perfect. How can they be mentioned in the same breath as the great medicine of the golden elixir?

The commentary further states: Methods such as abandoning grains, breath-work, and visualization are all side doors followed by vulgar scholars. Many, seeing the phrase "not abandoning wives," mistakenly take the arts of gathering yin as the golden elixir. Why do they not thoroughly investigate the *Breaking Delusion Song* of the Great White Immortal?
*"Practicing qi is not the Way;
Saliva is not divine water.
Visualization is not the Way;
A painted cake cannot be eaten.
Gathering yin is not the Way;
Essence exhausted, life follows in death.
Cutting salt is not the Way;
Food and drink lose their savor.
Abandoning grains is not the Way;
Hunger and weakness harm the spleen and stomach.
Resting wives is not the Way;
Yin and yang lose their proper place."*
What, then, *is* the Way? The Great One contains the true qi. Qi interacts yet does not interact; its ascent and descent emulate heaven and earth. The two things pair and unite, arising from the primordial. The maiden and the infant match, completing the *jiji*. This is the true yin and yang, husband and wife sharing a single principle. Thus, there is no need to abandon them. How can solitary yang accomplish the task of transcending the world to become a golden immortal? The golden elixir is not easily attained. Noble scholars do not speak of the true and profound meaning of the Great Cavern. The five phases do not follow their usual course: the tiger is born from water, the five phases are inverted, and the dragon emerges from fire. These words are truly wondrous, for they are the power of the Great One. The rhymed verses of the Immortal Elder are ultimately based on this.

The *Breaking Delusion Song* of Yimen says:
*"The Great One contains the true qi;
The dragon is born from fire,
The tiger arises from water.
Knowing the inversion of yin and yang,
It originates from the primordial.
The five phases do not follow their course,
Yet return to be one with heaven and earth."*
The meaning of "resting wives" does not approach the clarity of the *Song of the Great One*. Since people do not understand the inversion of the five phases, how can they know that true yin and yang require no abandonment? Those who study immortality, unable to fully comprehend the titles and terms in the books of immortals, how can they thoroughly ponder the entire text and merge it into a single principle? Thus, the great Way of the golden elixir has faded with the ages, and the Dao has become obscured as human nature dims. How could it be due to the mistaken interpretation of "resting wives" and "recklessly severing yin and yang" as referring to the bedchamber arts of human couples? What a pity! When the elixir is complete and qi is full, one naturally abstains from grains—not like consuming black beans, sesame seeds, or other medicinal foods to survive famine. Some use medicinal elixirs to practice grain avoidance, spreading their methods in the world, but how can they become immortals of pure yang? There are those who rely solely on herbs and plants; even if they attain longevity, they are not of the pure yang substance.

Sixteen.
The myriad scrolls of immortal scriptures,
Their words all converge on the golden elixir—
This alone is the root and origin.
Follow the Kun position to give birth to the body,
Plant the seed in the Qian household, the palace of intercourse.
Do not blame the celestial mechanism for being fully revealed;
It is only because scholars are foolish and guarded.
If one understands the meaning within this poem,
They will immediately behold the Three Pure Ones.

The commentary states: The myriad scrolls of immortal scriptures, though vast, ultimately return to one truth—none do not take the initial qi of the dragon and tiger, the two eights, as the substance of the elixir. However, by following the principle of the Kun mother giving birth and reversing the process to cultivate it, after obtaining the elixir, the seed is planted in the Qian father’s palace of intercourse to circulate the fire. The essentials of elixir refinement do not extend beyond the two words: lead and fire. Lead and fire are the foundation of the great elixir. The Immortal Elder has revealed the celestial mechanism in its entirety. Scholars, even with hoary heads, remain confused and guarded. Why do they not draw near and seek it within themselves to illuminate the supreme Dao? When a single grain of millet is formed, it becomes the guest of heaven.

The Commentary states: Master Cui’s *Mirror for Taking Medicines* says, “Born in Kun, planted in Qian”—this is it. Born in Kun is the precelestial external medicine; planted in Qian is the postcelestial qi internal medicine. The principle of the Kun mother’s generation: the Kun position is the southwest, where the moon emerges from Geng, and metal and water give birth to the two eights’ wondrous workings—this is “born in Kun.” The Qian father’s palace of intercourse is the Central Palace, the Northern Sea, just as Qian lies in the northwest. Ingesting the elixir within, lead and mercury interact to transform and evolve—this is “planted in Qian.” Lead is the White Tiger; fire is the Green Dragon. The White Tiger’s qi is lead, which is also water. The Green Dragon’s qi is fire, yet not ordinary fire. Lead is the essence of the moon, born of water and completed in metal, possessing both substance and qi—the root of heaven and earth’s wondrous transformations. Fire is the essence of the sun, born of wood and restrained by metal, possessing qi but no substance—the origin of heaven and earth’s generation. Thus it is said: the essentials of elixir refinement, the foundation of the great elixir, do not extend beyond lead and fire.

**Five-character quatrain (to emulate the oddness of the Great One):**
The maiden dons azure robes,
The young lord wraps in white silk.
Seen, it cannot be used;
Used, it cannot be seen.
In the midst of vagueness they meet,
Within the obscure, change occurs.
In a flash, flames soar—
The true person naturally appears.

The Commentary states: The maiden is the qi and essence of the Dragon.

Within yang there is yin—thus she is called the maiden, also named Wood Maiden, born of the Azure Dragon, hence her azure robes. Within yin there is yang—thus he is called the young lord, also named Metal Lord, born of the White Tiger, hence his white silk. That which possesses substance and can be seen belongs to the turbid things of post-heavenly earthly generation; because it has substance, it can be seen but cannot be used. That which has no form to behold is the primordial qi of the Dragon and Tiger’s first dual eight; because it has qi but no substance, it cannot be seen but can be used—this is the pivotal mechanism of lead refinement.

The vague and indistinct, the obscure and subtle, are the true unified qi of the Primordial Origin, born before heaven and earth, beyond all measure. Within the vague there is something: the Dragon’s qi. Within the obscure there is essence: the Tiger’s qi. The two qi reside in the midst of vagueness and obscurity, intermingling and embracing, thus obtaining the true unified qi, which first manifests as a spirit-like transformation and becomes a grain-like pearl—this is the wonder of something arising from nothing.

The true person is the golden elixir. When the sage gathers a year’s fire timing into a single hour, and further divides that hour into six intervals, first applying the fire in the two intervals to forge and refine, the true unified qi coalesces into a single pearl, appearing in the Northern Sea, as large as a millet grain. Is this not the true person emerging naturally in a flash of fire?

This Dao is most wondrous and profound. Without encountering a true master to transmit the oral instructions and true method, who could attain this?

The Commentary states: The immortal elder composed this five-character quatrain to represent the five phases and four images forming a single millet-like pearl. Though the elixir is transformed from the true unified qi, without the Dragon and Tiger’s two qi intermingling, it could not be formed. This is because the Dragon and Tiger together with the two qi make the four images. The four images interact within the Central Palace to form the elixir—earth, the true five phases. As the Old Master said: “The five phases are the medicine; the four images cannot be lacking.” Thus, the five phases and four images combine to form the elixir, which is why the immortal elder said: “A five-character quatrain to emulate the oddness of the Great One.”

The *Imperially Commissioned Siku Quanshu*: *Annotations and Subcommentaries on the Wuzhen Pian*, Scroll Middle

By Zhang Boduan of the Song Dynasty
Annotated by Weng Baoguang
Subcommentary by Dai Qizong of the Yuan Dynasty

Sixty-four seven-character quatrains to emulate the sixty-four hexagrams of the eight eights. First, take Qian and Kun as the crucible and vessel; next, employ the Crow and Hare as the medicine for refinement. Once the two substances are driven into the Yellow Path, how could the golden elixir fail to take form?

**Annotation:** The sun and moon are fundamentally the essence of Qian and Kun, hence the sage uses Qian and Kun as metaphors for the crucible and vessel, and the sun and moon as metaphors for the medicinal substances. Qian and Kun are the true Dragon and true Tiger; the medicinal substances are the crescent qi of the Dragon and Tiger. The Perfected Wei said: “The crucible is fundamentally no crucible; the medicine is fundamentally no medicine.” The sage borrows names and relies on images as metaphors. In essence, it is only through the intermingling of the true Dragon and true Tiger’s initial crescent qi, congealing the essence of the true One within the Central Palace of the Northern Sea, that the two substances are driven into the Yellow Path, and the golden elixir takes form without fail. The Yellow Path is the Central Palace, the place where the golden elixir congeals and takes shape.

**Subcommentary:** The immortal classics compare Qian and Kun to the crucible and vessel, and Kan and Li to the medicinal substances. Qian, Kun, Kan, and Li as crucible, vessel, and medicinal substances are ultimately formless and nameless. They are but the true Dragon and true Tiger of Qian and Kun—this refers to the external Dragon and Tiger of the golden elixir. The *Cantong Qi* annotated by Perfected Peng states: “Kan’s wu is the essence of the moon, resembling metal born in water—the Tiger. Li’s si is the radiance of the sun, resembling wood born in fire—the Dragon.” These are the internal Dragon and Tiger of the golden elixir. Though their names and forms differ, all are metaphors. If the two substances can return to the Yellow Path, they will naturally intermingle and form the elixir. If one stubbornly insists on distinguishing which is the fixed form of the Dragon or Tiger, the only concern is failing to recognize the Yellow Path’s role as the mediator.

**II. Establishing the Crucible and Setting the Vessel**
The method of forging Qian and Kun refines the essence and brilliance, restraining the po and hun. Gathering and dispersing, the qi intermingles to transform—how dare one idly discuss such profound wonders?

**Annotation:** Accumulating all yang qi forms Heaven, which remains above without descending to moisten below; accumulating all yin qi forms Earth, which remains below without rising to scorch above—this is the non-interaction of Heaven and Earth. If they do not interact, how could they generate the myriad things?

For though Heaven is the utmost yang entity, it contains within it a single strand of yin qi—thus it can descend to Earth; though Earth is the utmost yin entity, it contains within it a single strand of yang qi—thus it can ascend to Heaven. The intermingling of these two qi gives rise to the myriad things, transforming them to purity. This is how the interaction of the two qi brings about transformation. The Dao of the golden elixir, in establishing the crucible and setting the vessel to refine essence and brilliance and restrain the hun and po, takes no model other than Heaven and Earth.

The *Mother-Child Song* says:
*"When essence meets, no medicine is needed;
When qi conjoins, no words are spoken."*
The golden elixir is formed by the union of qi and mercury—thus it is said: *"Only when medicine encounters qi and mercury does it take shape."*

It begins with nothing giving rise to something, then returns to something giving rise to nothing. Though formless, it can transform—hence its transformations are inexhaustible. This is the celestial mechanism; how dare one idly prattle and risk the transgression of careless leakage?

**Annotation:** *"It begins with nothing giving rise to something"* refers to the external medicine, which relies on the true unity of the formless qi—from no substance, substance is born. It is not a case of *"something giving rise to something,"* where a material object is used as the basis. *"Then returns to something giving rise to nothing"* refers to the internal medicine, which, once the external medicine has taken shape, is swallowed into the five viscera, where the tangible forms of the four limbs and hundred bones are transmuted into qi. *"Though formless, it can transform"* means that once the internal and external have completed their transmutation, qi is refined into spirit, and embracing the origin for nine years, one enters the formless and undergoes unfathomable transformation. If one can comprehend the supreme Dao within nothingness, then gradual transmutation becomes possible.

**III.**
Do not cling to the elixir furnace and waste effort—
To refine the medicine, seek the recumbent-moon crucible.
Within it lies the true fire of Nature;
Why need kindling or breath to fan it?

**Commentary:**
Master Ye Wenshu designates the space between the two kidneys as the "recumbent-moon crucible"—how mistaken! Others point to the two eyes, yet none reflect on their own errors, instead leading others further astray. Why such extreme misguidance? The mouth of this crucible opens upward like a recumbent moon, hence its name. It is the Northern Sea, where the primordial ancestor of the original beginning abides. Within it lies the true fire of Nature; why rely on kindling or breath to fan it?

**Exegesis:**
The jade bud grows within the recumbent-moon crucible—this is the external medicine of the yin crucible. Here, it is the internal medicine of the Northern Sea. Both are metaphors, repeatedly inverted and reversed. Without a luminous teacher, one may cling to these names and fail to grasp their coherence, making the profound Dao difficult to attain. The true fire of Nature is seized from the great and small crucibles and returned to the body to produce the golden liquid and reverted elixir, which is not the yin within the body.

**IV.**
Within the recumbent-moon crucible, the jade bud grows;
In the cinnabar tripod, mercury lies level.
Only when fire and force harmonize
Does the yellow sprout take root and gradually flourish.

**Commentary:**
The recumbent-moon crucible is the yin crucible, containing the yang of the jade bud—the *qi* of the tiger. The cinnabar tripod is the yang crucible, containing the yin *qi* of mercury—the *qi* of the dragon. The golden elixir arises solely from the harmonizing and unifying power of these two *qi*. The true sprout of the One is planted, growing within the yellow household to form the millet pearl.

**V.**
Swallowing saliva and absorbing *qi*—only when one acts with substance
Can the myriad things be born.
If the crucible lacks the true seed,
Boiling water and fire is like cooking an empty pot.

**Commentary:**
What the world calls "swallowing saliva and absorbing *qi*" refers to the postnatal, earth-born, utmost-yin substances—this is not true *qi*-absorption. True *qi*-absorption first subdues and then absorbs. As the classic states: *"Subdue the *qi* before absorbing it; to absorb *qi*, one must first subdue it. Absorbing *qi* does not lead to longevity; longevity requires subduing *qi*."* The true *qi* of the One blends into the dim and indistinct, difficult to seek and see. The sage employs methods to subdue it, thus obtaining essence within the dim and substance within the indistinct. Through transformation and refinement, the elixir is formed and ingested into the cinnabar field, where the myriad things are transmuted and born. Hence, *"only with substance can the myriad things be born."* For it possesses the true seed. Without the true seed, all efforts are labor in vain, like boiling an empty pot with water and fire—what can be achieved? The true seed is true lead.

**Exegesis:**
Directing the golden liquid into the brain, descending from the upper palate to the cinnabar field, is also swallowing saliva. Directing the true *qi* of external yin and yang is also absorbing *qi*. This is not to say that swallowing saliva and absorbing *qi* are wrong, but without the true seed, efforts are futile. Without the true seed, what is swallowed is pure yin essence, and what is absorbed is postnatal *qi*. Lacking the mother *qi* of the postnatal, the true *qi* of heaven and earth’s yin and yang will not cling to and congeal with the child *qi* of the body. *"To subdue"* is like a cat stalking a mouse—restraining and subduing it so it does not move. *"To absorb"* is like a fish swallowing water—what enters cannot be retained. Furthermore: *"To subdue"* is to subdue the *qi* of heaven and earth, congealing it into the elixir. Subduing the *qi* of heaven and earth to form the elixir and swallowing it into the cinnabar field, the postnatal yin and yang, heaven and earth, all return to nurture the golden liquid and reverted elixir, forming the sacred embryo.

**VI.**
To harmonize lead and mercury and form the elixir,
Great and small cause no harm—both realms are preserved.
If you ask what true lead is:
The toad’s light shines all day upon the Western River.

**Commentary:**
Driving the dragon causes the fiery mercury to fly; riding the tiger makes the watery lead flicker. In the midst of their intermingling, transformation occurs—a grain of millet, the *qi* of the prior heaven, is formed. What harm is there? Hence, *"great and small cause no harm—both realms are preserved."* The dragon is great, the tiger small—this is the principle of yang’s nobility and yin’s humility. The golden elixir is formed from the upper and lower crescents of gold and water, called true lead. The toad’s light is the essence of gold and water, belonging to yin. *"Shines all day"* signifies the mutual illumination of the moon and sun, symbolizing the union of yin and yang. The west is the direction of metal; the river is water. On the fifteenth day of the eighth month, the sage combines the *qi* of gold and water to form the essence of the golden liquid—this is the meaning. The moon’s upper crescent belongs to water, its lower crescent to metal. Thus, the immortal elder takes the west as the direction of metal and the river as the body of water. Yet the moon does not truly shine all day. When the lower crescent moon first appears at dawn on the eastern side, half of its golden light is visible in the south (bing). By noon, it sets in the west (geng). When the upper crescent moon appears at noon on the western side, half of its watery light emerges in the east (jia). By sunset, it ascends to the south (ding). The two half-moons combine to form the full, round light of gold and water, creating the appearance of all-day illumination. This metaphorically represents the union of the *qi* of dragon and tiger to generate the elixir. Hence, *"if you ask what true lead is: the toad’s light shines all day upon the Western River."*

**Exegesis:**
The upper and lower crescents of the moon illuminate the sun by day, taking the utmost purity of gold and water. On the full moon, the moon faces the sun by night, taking the utmost abundance of gold and water. *"Pure"* means having *qi* but no form; *"abundant"* means having form but no form. When pure, the two eights mutually manifest; when abundant, the two eights become one body—thus, the golden elixir is instantly formed. The upper classic states: *"The upper crescent is half a catty of gold."* Here, it says the upper crescent belongs to water. The upper classic states: *"The lower crescent is half a catty of water."* Here, it says the lower crescent belongs to gold. Thus, the upper crescent’s half-catty of gold is the white half without the moon, while the upper crescent’s water is the black half with the moon. White is metal, black is water—hence the alternating terms to reveal that the two *qi* of gold and water each weigh half a catty, forming the wonder of the two eights. The lower crescent is the same. Those who do not understand this wonder may doubt it.

**VII.**
Before refining the reverted elixir, do not retreat to the mountains—
Within those mountains, both inside and out, lead is absent.
This supreme treasure exists in every household,
Yet people of this age fail to recognize it entirely.

**Annotation:**
The dragon does not dwell in the eastern sea, nor the tiger in the western mountains—every household possesses the means to reverse and cultivate it, and the reverted elixir may be hoped for.

**VIII.**
When bamboo splits, one must use bamboo to mend it;
To hatch a chick, one must use an egg.
All else is not of the same kind—vain labor,
Like contending for true lead to match the sage’s mechanism.

**Annotation:**
When a bamboo vessel breaks, can one mend it with metal or wood? It must be mended with bamboo before the vessel is whole again. When a chick is to be hatched, can one use earth or stone to brood it? It must be hatched with an egg before the fledgling is born. Master Tao says: *"When bamboo breaks, bamboo must mend it; when wood splits, wood must repair it. A leaking roof is covered with tiles. When a person declines, the same kind must preside over their cultivation."* If one does not employ the same kind, their efforts are in vain. The *Cantong Qi* states: *"When the same kind is employed, work is easily done; without the proper seed, skill is difficult to apply."* Those who wish to refine and consume the elixir must use the same kind. For humans receive the essence *qi* of Heaven and Earth to gain life. True lead is the mother *qi* of Heaven and Earth, entrusted to things of the same kind to conceive and nurture it. Thus, true lead is the mother *qi*, and one’s true *qi* is the child *qi*—is this not the supreme wonder of the same kind? Therefore, it accords with the profound mechanism of the utmost sage and the great Dao of spontaneity.

**Commentary:**
Master Tao, named Zhi, has a separate record. His *Three Grades of Supreme Medicines* was secretly transmitted to the world. In the first year of Baoli during the reign of Emperor Jingzong of Tang, on the fifteenth day of the eighth month, at Siming Mountain’s Damei Peak in Yin County, Mingzhou, Zhejiang, he ascended in broad daylight at the Immortal’s Terrace of Mei Fu. A stele inscription remains below the terrace.

**IX.**
Use lead, yet do not use common lead—
What is used is true lead.
Discard this, for it is the wondrous secret of using lead.
To use lead is not to use it—this is the truth.

**Annotation:**
Common lead is a substance born of the postcelestial world, a turbid and material thing. True lead is the *qi* of the primordial Unity that precedes Heaven and Earth. Now, man’s original yang and true essence scatter and disperse daily, never congealing to form the sacred embryo. Thus, the sage refines true lead, seizes it, and subdues it, causing it to coagulate into cinnabar. Day by day, fire is applied, and mercury is gradually added; as mercury increases, the *qi* of lead gradually dissipates. Lead is drawn out, and mercury is replenished—such is its wonder. After ten months, the fire is complete, and the sixty-four hexagrams conclude. The *qi* of lead ascends and floats away like dust motes in a sunlit window, scattering in fragments. After nine years of embracing the One, the primordial *qi* is exhausted, leaving only a single taste of dry mercury. When lead is spent and mercury desiccated, they transform into the golden liquid of the Great Return Elixir. The body, now purely yang, attains the same lifespan as Heaven. Thus it is said: "Use true lead, then discard it; to use lead is not to use it." Are these words empty?

Hearing the Dao to this point, one should pledge before Heaven, saying: "The grace of the teacher is hard to repay; I shall attain the Dao to requite it. To betray the teacher’s words is to betray Heaven and Earth."

**X.**
Empty the heart and fill the belly—both meanings run deep.
Yet to empty the heart, one must first know the heart.
Better to refine lead and fill the belly first,
Then guard the hall brimming with gold.

**Annotation:**
Mercury is essence. Guarding mercury to fill the belly brings a hall overflowing with gold and jade. The One is the Elixir. Embracing the One to empty the heart leaves not a speck of dust. When the heart is empty, the form cannot long endure—one must refine lead to restrain it. When the belly is full, the heart must not cling—one must embrace the One to empty it. To fill the belly, first refine lead to control mercury; when mercury is desiccated and form transformed, then embrace the One to empty the heart. With the heart empty and form wondrous, one merges with the Dao, becoming one with the formless.

Both principles are marvelous, though their paths differ, they converge as one. None but the utmost sage can comprehend this. The "hall brimming with gold" is the essence and *qi* of the entire body. The cultivator of truth, desiring to refine lead to fill the belly, must not disturb their essence. If essence is scant, the Return Elixir cannot be completed.

**Commentary:**
"When the heart is empty" refers to one who has completed *xing* (nature) yet cannot stabilize form—thus, they must refine lead to restrain it. "When the belly is full" refers to one who has completed *ming* (life-destiny) yet cannot empty the heart—thus, they must embrace the One to empty it. *Xing* and *ming* are cultivated in sequence; only when both are complete can they fuse, merging with the Dao in truth. How could one confuse *xing* and *ming* as one, clinging to partial views through the Chan of hearsay or the arts of side doors?

**XI.**
In a dream, I paid homage to Xihua,
And the Perfected of the Nine Heavens bestowed upon me the *Zhigao* Scroll.
Its words were few and simple,
Only teaching men to refine mercury and lead.

**Annotation:**
Gao Xiangxian said: Suddenly, my soul ascended to the Jade Capital, where the Emperor took pity on me and commanded the Perfected of Xihua to instruct me in the elixir’s secrets. The scroll’s gist reads: "Shutong followed Wei Boyang, laughing as they entered the land of nothingness. They composed the *Cantong Qi*, leaving it as the king of elixirs for ten thousand ages. Its opening says: ‘Qian and Kun are the gates of the *Yi*; the Dao of Qian becomes male, the Dao of Kun becomes female.’ Yet people do not recognize true yin and yang, blindly seeking dragon and tiger across the world. Its words are many, but it only teaches men to clarify true dragon and true tiger, refining lead and mercury."

Shutong’s surname was Chunyu.

**Commentary:**
The *Zhigao* Scroll is written in elegant and ancient script, focusing solely on lead and mercury. The passage quoted here is from Gao Xiangxian’s song. Its marvels are distilled below, revealing the path to enlightenment, akin to the *Zhigao* Scroll and the song itself. The song says:

The Yellow Emperor sought the Dao in Kongtong’s chamber,
First obtaining the *Gang* of the Mysterious.
Yet still incomplete, he turned to Shu,
Visiting Emei to seek the Heavenly Perfected.
The August Person and True Unity—none surpass
Knocking at the gate of Wuji.
Within Wuji’s gate lies metal and water;
Metal and water are the root of the Yellow Sprout.
The Yellow Sprout, mother of all things,
With child, becomes the cauldron and furnace.
When the sun’s soul and moon’s essence intertwine,
One floats, one sinks—pearls take flight.
The pearl flies to Kunlun’s peak;
To obtain it, rely on Wangxiang.
Wangxiang gains it and returns to the Crimson Palace,
Where it steams into the flesh, reddening the skin.
Reddened skin, blackened hair—
The Northern Dipper falls, death’s register erased.
Great indeed! Ninety days to completion,
Echoing the traces left at Mount Fang.
Have you not seen Shutong follow Wei Boyang,
Laughing as they entered the land of nothingness?
They composed the *Cantong Qi*,
Leaving it as the king of elixirs for ten thousand ages.
Its opening says: "Qian and Kun are the gates of the *Yi*;
The Dao of Qian is male, the Dao of Kun is female."
Yet people do not recognize true yin and yang,
Blindly seeking dragon and tiger across the world.
The sun is *Li*, the moon is *Kan*;
Sun and moon, yin and yang, devour each other.
When the golden crow dies, the jade hare is born—
All things arise from Heaven and Earth’s interaction,
The two *qi* in harmonious union.
Male and female unite, the four images and five phases
Rely on the hub’s convergence.
Day and night, *Zhun* and *Meng*—such is Nature’s law.
Diligently tend the fire’s timing;
Harvest at the appointed hour, gather at the destined day.
Harvest and gather—be ever discreet.
**[The above quotes the *Zhigao* Scroll to clarify mercury and lead.]**

**XII.**
The Dao arises from emptiness and nothingness,
Giving birth to the One *qi*.
From the One *qi* emerge yin and yang;
Yin and yang unite to form the Three Bodies.
The Three Bodies give rise to the flourishing of all things.

**Annotation:**
The Dao is fundamentally empty, yet it produces the *qi* of form. *Qi* is fundamentally substantial, yet it manifests as the formless form. Form and formlessness restrain each other, and the One arises therefrom.

Thus, the One gives birth to the Two, the Two gives birth to the Three, and the Three gives birth to the ten thousand things. The ten thousand things bear yin and embrace yang, harmonizing through the *qi* of the center. Before form emerges, the harmonious *qi* is invisible.

Once formed, the light and pure *qi* belongs to yang, while the heavy and turbid *qi* belongs to yin. Thus, yang Heaven is the father, and yin Earth is the mother. The two *qi* intertwine, their passions uniting—this is called Heaven, Earth, and Man, together forming the Three Bodies, known as the Three Powers. From these, the Three Things are born.

Therefore, the *Yi* says: "Heaven and Earth intertwine, and the ten thousand things are transformed into purity; male and female unite in essence, and the ten thousand things are transformed into life." The utmost person delves into this nourishment to know its source, probes its spirit to know its transformations. Thus, they can return to the root and restore the source, inverting the smelting process to reverse creation, plundering the mother *qi* of Heaven and Earth to forge the Elixir, and stealing the essence of yin and yang to fuel the fire. Refining form returns it to the One *qi*; refining *qi* restores it to emptiness and nothingness. Thus, spirit merges with the Dao, attaining the wondrous formless, boundless transformations, unfathomable and profound—this is called the Perfected.

**Commentary:**
The Elixir is the mother *qi*; fire is the essence. The mother *qi* is the undifferentiated essence, while the essence is the already-differentiated mother *qi*. Fire and medicine are one.

The mother *qi* of True Unity is concealed within the yin-yang spirit-essence, invisible and unattainable. Yet by stealing the true essence of yin and yang to seek it, the *qi* of True Unity may be obtained. Shi Xinglin said: "The medicine is the primordial *qi*; the fire seeks the essence of Great Yang. To know the medicine and take the fire is to see the Elixir form within." Wang Dao further said: "Fire is the father and mother of the medicine; the medicine is the child and grandchild of the fire."

**Thirteen**
The thunder of Kan roars, refining with fire;
Golden Water meets the square flame, igniting Kunlun.
Yin and yang, these two things—
When harmonized, the Elixir ripens naturally,
Fragrance perfusing the entire body.

**Commentary:**
This chapter describes the symbolic method of the inner and outer Elixirs.
The "thunder of Kan" is the fire within water, called yin fire—the *qi* of the Black Tiger at the Mysterious Gate. Here, the Tiger refines with the fire within yin, while the Dragon responds by igniting the fire of Kunlun. When the two fires merge, the essence of True Unity naturally congeals. At once ingested, the hundred bones are ordered, and a wondrous fragrance arises.

The *Cantong Qi* says:
When golden sand enters the five viscera,
Mist scatters like wind and rain,
Steaming and permeating the four limbs.
The complexion becomes radiant,
Gray hair returns to black,
Fallen teeth regrow in their old places.
The old man regains youth,
The aged woman becomes a maiden—
Is this not the true fragrance filling the body?

After ingesting the Elixir, one further circulates the fire of the yin-yang tally.
The Tiger, with the fire within yin, smelts the Mysterious Gate,
While the Dragon, igniting fire at Kunlun, responds.
When the two things harmonize,
The golden essence naturally revolves,
Ascending from the Tail Gate with a resonant sound,
Passing through the spine’s twin passes,
Straight up to the Mud Pill,
Then descending through the Double Towers,
Its flavor sweet and fragrant beyond compare,
Naturally illuminating the entire body.

**Commentary:**
The earlier passage—"the Tiger refines with the fire within yin; the Dragon responds by igniting fire"—refers to the two fires of the inner and outer medicines. Later, "the Tiger refines with the fire within yin" speaks of the fire of the outer medicine, while "the Dragon ignites fire in response" speaks of the fire of the inner medicine. Though the inner and outer Dragon-Tiger fires share the same name, their forms differ. When the two fires merge, the true essence congeals; when the two medicines harmonize, the golden essence revolves. The congealing of true essence forms the outer Golden Elixir; the revolving of golden essence forms the inner Return Elixir. Thus, "fire ignites Kunlun" refers to the Dragon’s fire, further divided into the inner and outer yin and yang.

**Fourteen**
If Li and Kan lack Wu and Ji,
Though they contain the Four Images,
No Elixir forms.
Only because each holds the true Earth,
Does the Golden Elixir achieve return.

**Commentary:**
The *Cantong Qi* states: "Li contains *ji* as the sun’s light; Kan holds *wu* as the moon’s essence." Thus, *ji* in Li resembles the Dragon’s bowstring qi, while *wu* in Kan resembles the Tiger’s bowstring qi. Now, *wu* and *ji* are the true Earth in substance, each residing within the Dragon and Tiger’s bodies—hence the saying, "each holds the true Earth." If Dragon and Tiger lacked Earth, how could the Four Images merge? Only by guarding Earth does the Elixir form. Precisely because each contains the qi of Earth, the two Earths unite to become the *daogui*. Thus, when Dragon and Tiger interact, *wu* and *ji* merge; when *wu* and *ji* unite as one, the Four Images combine to form the Elixir. This is why the Golden Elixir achieves return. As Master Lü said: "When the two things guard each other, they become the root of the Dao; when the Five Phases are complete in their guarding, it is called the Elixir."

**Exegesis:**
