Li is yang, *ji* is yin. Fire, with Earth as two, generates Heaven as seven, containing five in the center—fire is dark within yet bright without. The Li trigram is hollow within, all yang containing yin. Kan is yin, *wu* is yang. Water, with Heaven as one, generates Earth as six, containing five in the center—water is dark without yet bright within. The Kan trigram is solid within, all yin containing yang. Kan holds metal, Li holds wood, forming the Four Images. Kan flows with *wu*, Li gathers *ji*; each harbors true Earth. When the Four Images merge, *wu* and *ji*—the yin and yang Earths—guard each other to become one, and the Five Phases are complete. Returning to the root and restoring the origin, seven returns and nine reverts, and the Golden Elixir is achieved.

**Fifteen**
The sun resides in Li’s position yet becomes female;
The moon matches Kan’s palace yet turns male.
Do not dismiss the inverted meaning within—
Cease your lofty discourse on mere surface matters.

**Commentary:**
The crow in the sun belongs to yin, hence Li is female; the rabbit in the moon belongs to yang, hence Kan is male. If one does not grasp the marvel of inversion but merely engages in high talk, it is like gazing at the heavens through a tube.

**Exegesis:**
Inversion means not taking yin as yang—this is extracting yang from within yin; not taking yang as yin—this is extracting yin from within yang. Yin as yin and yang as yang is the common course of the world’s constant Dao. Extracting yang from yin and yin from yang is the reverse movement—the Heavenly mechanism of theft. The Five Phases invert, yin and yang interchange, yet the world rarely understands this. Thus it is said: "When the Five Phases reverse, the Elixir’s body is eternally numinous and enduring." And again: "All is because the child gives birth to the mother." Among all the world’s rabbits, only the moon’s rabbit is male; gazing at the moon, it conceives—hence the moon’s rabbit belongs to yang.

**Sixteen**
Take the solid center from Kan’s position,
Transform the yin within Li’s palace.
From this, the dry and vigorous body arises—
Hidden potential and soaring leaps all stem from the heart.

**Commentary:**
The Li trigram is yang without and yin within; the Kan trigram is yin without and yang within. Taking the inner yang to replace the inner yin forms the *Qian* trigram. For example, the Golden Elixir is the utmost yang’s essence, called the Yang Elixir, congealed within the Northern Sea. When taken to refine *ji*’s yin mercury, it becomes pure *Qian*, transforming into a purely yang body. Thereafter, the firing process—withdrawing and adding, advancing and retreating—is all governed by my heart’s operation. Some consider the *guidan* to be the yang within Kan, but this is a post-Heaven, Earth-born turbid substance, not the pre-Heaven, Earth-born qi. To equate heart and kidneys with Kan and Li is to stray far from Heaven and Earth.

**Exegesis:**
"Hidden potential and soaring leaps" describe the six lines of *Qian*, illustrating the firing process—withdrawing and adding, advancing and retreating—suddenly swift, like the *Cantong Qi*’s forty-seventh chapter, where the six lines of *Qian* are distributed among the six trigrams as symbols for the six stages. The *guidan* involves absorbing the wife’s *gui*, plucking the maiden’s flower, or extracting the qi of boys and girls—all post-Heaven, Earth-born turbid substances. Though human qi may be pure, it is still yin vapor; how can it refine a purely yin body into a purely yang immortal? Those who claim "using humans to supplement humans" as the same qi do not understand that Heaven and Earth’s commander is our nature, Heaven and Earth’s blockage is our body. At the moment of receiving qi at birth, was it from between the two kidneys or the birth gate? The Heavenly-Earthly numinous root, the yin-yang sagely mother, is the foundation of transformation—this is the same qi.

**Seventeen**
The Thunder Dragon’s mercury emerges from Li’s homeland;
The Marsh Tiger’s metal is born in Kan’s domain.
Both things arise because the child gives birth to the mother—
The Five Phases complete, they must enter the center.

**Commentary:**
Mercury is the Thunder Dragon, belonging to wood; wood generates fire, wood is fire’s mother, fire is wood’s child—this is the common course of the constant Dao. Yet cinnabar belongs to fire, and mercury emerges from cinnabar—this is fire returning to generate wood, hence "the child gives birth to the mother." As the *Taibai Immortal*’s song says: "The Five Phases’ inverted art—Dragon emerges from within fire." The Immortal Elder thus speaks of mercury being born in Li, not of mercury born from cinnabar, for mercury within cinnabar is called true mercury, also called fire’s mercury. Thus, he speaks of mercury without mentioning cinnabar. Lead is the Marsh Tiger, belonging to metal; metal generates water, metal is water’s mother, water is metal’s child—this is the common course of the constant Dao. Yet black lead belongs to water, and silver is born from lead—this is water returning to generate metal, hence "the child gives birth to the mother." As the *Taibai Immortal*’s song says: "The Five Phases do not follow the common course—Tiger is born within water." The Immortal Elder thus speaks of lead being born in Kan, not of silver being born, for silver within lead is called true lead, also called water’s lead. Thus, he speaks of lead without mentioning silver. The two things mutually give birth, forming the Four Images; guarding the center, they complete the Five Phases. When the Five Phases unite, the Golden Elixir congeals. Thus it is said: "The Five Phases complete, they must enter the center." The center is the Central Palace, the Supreme Ultimate. Later generations take the heart’s and kidneys’ qi and fluids as Dragon and Tiger, lead and mercury—claiming the Tiger is the kidneys’ qi, and since kidneys belong to water, the Tiger is born within water; the Dragon is the heart’s fluid, and since the heart belongs to fire, the Dragon emerges from within fire. Such words are child’s play. How can one hope to refine the Great Medicine without going astray?

**Exegesis:**
Someone asked me: "Those who cultivate life all take the heart and kidneys as Dragon and Tiger, lead and mercury, and the qi and fluids as water and fire, hoping for their ascent and descent, union and mating, to form the embryo. Even the *Zhong-Lü Transmission of the Dao*, compiled by Shi Jianwu, states: 'Within the kidneys, qi is born; within qi, the true one’s water. Within the heart, fluid is born; within fluid, the correct yang’s qi. The Inner Elixir’s medicinal materials emerge from the heart and kidneys, uniting and mating daily to obtain the millet grain, called the Golden Elixir, the Great Medicine.' Yet the preface to the *Wuzhen Pian* says: 'Dividing heart and kidneys as Kan and Li, hoping to congeal the Return Elixir—is this not far off?'"

---

The Master of No-Name, in his commentary on the poem on extracting Kan and Li, states: "To take heart and kidneys as Kan and Li is to place Heaven and Earth far apart." Yet another annotation to this poem says: "To regard the qi and fluids of heart and kidneys as Dragon and Tiger, lead and mercury, is child’s play." If so, are the qi and fluids of heart and kidneys not the Great Medicine of the Golden Elixir?

I respond: Zhengyang said, "Heart and kidneys are not water and fire"—then what *are* water and fire? Shi Xinglin said, "Qi is born not from the kidneys; the spirit dwells not in the heart." Daoguang said, "Cease your stubborn reliance on heart and kidneys." Chen Niniwan said, "Heart and kidneys are not originally Kan and Li." Yet the *Zhong-Lü Transmission of the Dao* passes down the teaching of heart and kidneys, qi and fluids, as mother and child, husband and wife, lead and mercury, Dragon and Tiger, Kan and Li—this is but a borrowed metaphor from the human body’s qi and fluids to obliquely illustrate yin and yang and clarify their wondrous function.

The benighted, failing to receive the true transmission, take this as literal speech and thus stray far from the Great Dao. Why not investigate the *Transmission of the Dao*, which states: "Substance and function do not transcend yin and yang; all transformations arise from their union." How profound are these words!

*"When the moon at heaven’s edge shows half its wheel,*
*At early dawn, Dragon’s roar and Tiger’s cry—*
*Then is the time to refine your work.*
*Within the two eights’ single hour, the Elixir is assured."*

The annotation explains: "The moon’s half-wheel is the number of one eight. The Immortal Elder points to Dragon and Tiger as the numbers of one eight each, which together form two eights. At this time, the water’s source is utterly pure, possessing qi but no substance."

Within a year, there is but one day; within a day, but one hour; within an hour, six *hou*—yet the work is accomplished in no more than two *hou*, yielding a single grain of Golden Elixir. The remaining four *hou* serve other wondrous purposes. These are all celestial secrets, not recorded on bamboo or silk, transmitted only orally and mind-to-mind. The Immortal Elder dared not commit them to writing or reveal them openly, but embedded their meaning in poems, speaking obliquely of "the Elixir assured within a single hour."

Ye Wenshu, failing to grasp this principle, misunderstood that the Medicine is completed in one hour—not that one hour alone is used. Bewildered, he lost the true pointer and indulged in private conjecture, which is truly laughable. If one claims it is *not* accomplished in one hour, then the process would drag on indefinitely—how could it remain the simplest and easiest of paths?

Profound and wondrous! This Dao is not something one may hear of in the world of men.

Carefully examining the *Fire Record of the Great Elixir*, it states: "I have observed that when the Sage begins the initial work of crafting the Lead, at the very outset of stealing the primordial qi of the Great Celestial Cycle, they seize the correct tally of thirty-six thousand, gathering it within the cauldron of Qian and Kun, guarding it in the chamber of generation and destruction. They plunder the tally of Heaven and Earth, the tally of the Sun and Moon, the tally of Dragon and Tiger, the tally of generation and completion, the tally of yin and yang, and the tally of the Five Phases—all captured within a single *hou* to refine a single grain of Golden Elixir. Its size is like a millet seed, its weight one *jin*; most numinous, most noble, most sagely, most spiritually efficacious, simplest, and easiest. It becomes the primordial essence of Heaven and Earth, the master governing the body. Truly, it may be called the thief of Heaven, the thief of Earth, the thief of yin, the thief of yang. The cosmos lies within the palm, the myriad transformations arise from the body, and one becomes a perfected immortal, a guest of the Supreme Emperor. Thus, our Immortal Elder said, 'Within a single *hou*, the Elixir is assured'—how could this be empty words? This is its proof."

The commentary states: "The half-wheel is one eight. The upper *cun*’s eight is the yang of Metal; the lower *cun*’s eight is the yin of Wood."

Within a single *hou*, the union of the two eights yields a single grain of Golden Elixir—this is the esoteric transmission of immortals, the profound mechanism of Heaven and Earth, not something mundane scholars may idly speculate upon. Those in the world who employ a single *hou* may follow virtue to unite, or follow the cycles of *wu-ji*, or follow *gui-jia*, or take the lunar establishment, or use the lunar general, or take the direction of the Celestial Dipper, or take the winter solstice, or take the rising of yang, or take the descent of *gui*, or rely on intention reaching the Central Palace, or gather the seven luminaries, or assemble the five phases, or take the five phases’ generative, flourishing, declining, and storing positions, or take *jia-geng* and *bing-ren*, or take the three days and four seasons, or use the living *zi* hour, or use one’s natal hour, or reverse generation, or use the exact center of the sun and moon, or use the sun and moon in mutual opposition, or use the sun and moon in conjunction, or use the hour of heart-kidney union, or take the interval between *hai* and *zi*, or take the earthly *qi* of the three origins, or take the upper and lower *cun*, or take the Eastern Star forming the chamber, or the lunar lodgings on duty, or the establishment of the seven origins—all claim to begin with the *hou* of union. Yet those who practice thus have never attained immortality, for they do not know that within a single *hou* the Elixir is assured. If the Elixir is formed within that single *hou*, why delay its ingestion by extending the timeline?

Nineteen:
On the peak of Mount Hua, the male tiger roars;
In the depths of Fusang Sea, the female dragon hums.
The Yellow Dame daily dissolves their matchmaking,
Sending them to become husband and wife with one heart.

A Commentary states: Mount Hua is the place in the western mountains where the moon emerges, symbolizing the tiger. The male tiger is the *cun* and *qi* of the tiger—yang within yin, hence it is called the male tiger. Fusang is the place in the east where the sun rises, symbolizing the dragon. The female dragon is the *cun* and *qi* of the dragon—yin within yang, hence it is called the female dragon. These two beings are separated, one in the east and one in the west. The matchmaker, the Yellow Dame, causes them to unite and become husband and wife, producing the *xuan* pearl and the yellow sprout.

A Subcommentary states: The *Cantong Qi* says, "The dragon exhales, the tiger inhales"—here, the tiger is the husband and the dragon the wife, their original natures clashing to form male and female. The *Wuzhen Pian* says, "The male tiger and female dragon"—here, the yin and yang of the two beings merge to form male and female. Thus, dragon and tiger alternate as male and female, and this cannot be settled in a single phrase.

Twenty:
On the western mountain, the white tiger rages uncontrollably;
In the eastern sea, the azure dragon cannot be withstood.
Seize them with both hands and make them fight to the death,
Transforming into a sheet of purple-gold frost.

A Commentary states: This speaks of external imagery, as explained in the previous *lüshi* poem. Where the five phases are complete, the tiger and dragon coil within. The purple-gold frost is the golden elixir. Master Haichan said: "With the left hand seize the azure dragon’s head, with the right drag the white tiger’s tail, and in one moment bring them into the mouth to swallow. Reflecting on this, the substance is most sweet—realizing it is merely gold within water." Those who have not heard the supreme Dao may wildly guess, interpreting the two hands as two beasts—how laughable! They stray ever farther from the truth.

Twenty-One:
The red dragon and black tiger, each in west and east,
The four images intertwine; in *wu-si*, union is restored.
From this, one can circulate the golden elixir—
How could the Dao not succeed?

A Commentary states: The east is the azure dragon, wood; wood generates fire, so the dragon’s *xian-qi* belongs to fire. Fire resides in the south and is red, hence it is called the red dragon. The west is the white tiger, metal; metal generates water, so the tiger’s *xian-qi* belongs to water. Water resides in the north and is black, hence it is called the black tiger. The red dragon is also called the "maiden of cinnabar," and the black tiger is also named "Lord Metal." These two are like mercury within cinnabar and silver within lead. When the red dragon and black tiger unite their *xian-qi*, it is the convergence of east, west, south, and north. The four images intertwine within *wu-si*, the true earth, forming a grain of true elixir. Swallowing it into the five viscera, its fragrance steams through the four limbs, entering Kunlun Mountain where the eight waters all come to pay homage. Thereafter, advance the yang fire at *fu*, retreat the yin tally at *gou*, and naturally, in circulation and refinement, every step aligns with the measure. The golden elixir and supreme Dao will be achieved in days.

A Subcommentary states: The dragon’s *cun-qi* is fire; the tiger’s *cun-qi* is water. It is also said: the metal tripod has fire, becoming the white tiger; the jade pool has water, becoming the azure dragon. This is the principle that yin and yang have no fixed position, water and fire no fixed substance—mutually employed, their wondrous transformations are endless.

Twenty-Two:
First observe the heavens to clarify the five thieves;
Next examine the earth to pacify the people.
When the people are at peace and the state is prosperous,
Then seek war—when war ceases, only then can the sage be seen.

A Commentary states: The five thieves in heaven are the five planets; on earth, the five peaks; in humans, the five constants. I say: the five directions in humans are the five viscera; in *qi*, the five natures; in things, the five notes, five phases, five colors, five metals, five grains, five fruits, and five flavors. The *Yinfu Jing* says: "Heaven has five thieves; those who see them prosper. If one can perceive this reversal and cultivate it, then the cosmos is in hand, and the myriad transformations arise from the body."

Observing the earth’s advantages lies in pacifying the people; the people are the root of the state. When the root is firm, the state is at peace, and the nation prospers. Thus, the sage takes the body as the state, cinnabar as the sovereign, fire as the minister, and essence-*qi* as the people. The cultivator of the Elixir, if able to observe the heavens and capture the Five Thieves, reversing their course to refine them, seizing *yin-yang* to return it to transformation, may then wrest the true Unity’s essence and establish one’s own *yin*-mercury as the stem. When essence is firm and *qi* secure, perpetual victory in battle is assured. Thus, in deploying fire without error, after ten months the work is complete, the embryo is shed, and the spirit is transformed into a perfected one—a transcendent. Hence it is said: only after victory in battle can the sage be seen.

Twenty-Three:
In deploying generals, one must divide left and right armies;
Let the other be host, I the guest.
I urge you: when facing battle, do not treat the enemy lightly,
Lest you lose our priceless treasure of the household.

A Commentary states: This chapter clarifies the operation of fire-timing. The "generals" are fire. The left is civil fire, the right martial fire. The sage condenses a year’s fire-timing into a single month, a month’s fire-timing into a single day. From *zi* to *si*, the six double-hours belong to *yang*, resembling the virtue of spring and summer’s generation—thus civil fire, residing on the left, is called *yang*-fire. From *wu* to *hai*, the six double-hours belong to *yin*, resembling the punishment of autumn and winter’s austerity—thus martial fire, residing on the right, is called the *yin*-tally. "Let the other be host, I the guest": the host is *yang* and male, fond of contention; the guest is *yin* and female, fond of stillness. This means guarding the female without contending, maintaining stillness without strife—this is the intent of caution against peril and vigilance against danger, the utmost reverence. The *Art of War* says: "Rest to await the weary," and "Draw the enemy without being drawn"—this is the meaning. The application of the Dao lies in fire; the application of fire lies in the person. Those who deploy fire are like guests before a host: advancing and retreating with reverence, never daring to act recklessly. The adept of fire-deployment must not be ignorant of this.

First, fix the water-clock to divide *zi* and *wu*; next, arrange *yin-yang* to establish the foundation of transformation. Transpose the sixty-four hexagrams onto the *yin*-tally, drum the twenty-four *qi* with *yang*-fire. The celestial gate is in hand, the earth’s axis turns by the heart. The seventy-two seasonal nodes’ crucial passages converge within the crucible, seizing the three thousand six hundred *zheng-qi* to gather like spokes around the embryo. Deployment is methodical, extraction and addition follow sequence. In movement, guard against peril and contemplate danger—no deviation by a hair’s breadth is permitted. Thus, externally, one connects with the tally of *yin-yang*; internally, the body of true Unity is born. If, however, the mind is deployed carelessly and the timing of the nodes is amiss, causing the Maiden to flee and the numinous embryo within the crucible to fail in formation, then the priceless treasure of the Returned Elixir is lost. When facing battle, can the cultivator of the Elixir fail to guard the female and dare to treat the enemy lightly?

An Exegesis states: From *zi* to *si*, the left is civil fire; from *wu* to *hai*, the right is martial fire. The virtue of generation is civil, the punishment of austerity is martial. The *Cantong Qi*’s "Crucible and Vessel Song" says: "Martial at head and tail, civil in the middle." Yet civil and martial are further determined by the waxing and waning of fire-timing. Master Wuming said: "The crucible and vessel are the marrow of the Elixir," hence the simultaneous mention of the "Crucible and Vessel Song" and the civil and martial fire-timing—each has its proper use. This poem clarifies the fire-timing of the inner medicine, not the outer medicine. The marvel of the outer medicine lies in a single moment; the marvel of the inner medicine lies in a day. The fire-timing of a day may seem identical, yet its application differs. From transposing the sixty-four hexagrams to the embryo’s attainment of true Unity, this follows the *Cantong Qi*’s text. The sixty-four hexagrams are not entirely the *yin*-tally, nor are the twenty-four *qi* entirely *yang*-fire—this merely cites the year’s fire-count to complete the text.

Twenty-Four:
Fire is born of wood, its essence conceals its edge—
Do not forcefully drill or recklessly attack.
Disaster arises inevitably from this;
To protect oneself, one must seek restraint and find the Metal Elder.

**Commentary:**
Fire is born of wood, and disaster arises when it overcomes [the wood]. Essence is born of the body, and when emotions stir, it inevitably dissipates. Without restraint in drilling and reckless attack, calamity will harm the self. To protect oneself, one must seek restraint and find the Metal Elder. Lü [Dongbin] said: "When fire erupts from the seven apertures, tightly seal the gates—do not let it burn through the River Chariot’s path."

**Exegesis:**
Fire is born of wood; if one drills excessively, the wood will surely be consumed, reduced to ashes by fire. This is an analogy for the body: fire represents primordial *qi*. If one conceals true *qi* to nourish the body but lightly depletes it, the body will inevitably perish. To restrain the *qi* of the "child" within the body, one must obtain the "mother" of heaven and earth—the Metal Elder—to subdue it. Only then can the root be cultivated, the sacred embryo congealed, and longevity attained, gazing upon the distant ages.

---

**Twenty-Five**
The Metal Elder is originally the Eastern House’s child,
Sent to dwell in the Western Neighbor’s abode.
Once recognized, call him home to nurture,
Then pair him with the Maiden to wed in affection.

**Commentary:**
This meaning has already been explained in the regulated verse, "Leading the White Tiger home to nurture." The commentary therein reveals that the great elixir of golden cinnabar encompasses all operations. Its symbolic patterns include *yang* within *yin*, and *yang* that is yet *yin*; *yin* within *yang*, and *yin* that is yet *yang*. There are also the *yin-yang* waters and fires of the inner medicine, the *yin-yang* waters and fires of the outer medicine, the three inner natures and three outer natures, the four inner images and five phases, the four outer images and five phases. Furthermore, there are the mutual applications of inner and outer *yin-yang*, their symbolic patterns reversing and repeating in ways beyond description. We disciples, having received the profound transmission in silence and heart-to-heart communion, may grasp it. Without encountering a true master, none can thoroughly comprehend it. The immortal elder composed this poem to elucidate it—having presented one corner, one should attain the rest.

**Exegesis:**
The reversals and repetitions of *yin* and *yang* have been thoroughly detailed in the symbolic patterns of the golden elixir’s methods.

---

**Twenty-Six**
The Maiden wanders, each with her own direction:
The forward path must be short, the return long.
When she comes back, she enters the Yellow Dame’s abode,
Marrying the Metal Elder as her old lord.

**Commentary:**
The Maiden is mercury. It is called "mercury fire," and her wanderings follow a direction. The forward path pertains to the outer medicine’s operation; the return pertains to the inner medicine’s operation. These two uses are why it is said, "each with her own direction." When the sage begins the work of refining the elixir, moving the mercury fire does not exceed half an hour before obtaining the essence of true Unity, refining it into a millet grain to swallow. Thus, it is said, "the forward path must be short." After ingesting the elixir, the movement of mercury fire requires ten months of effort—this is what is meant by "the return must be long." The Yellow Dame in the inner image is the golden embryo’s divine chamber. The Metal Elder is true lead; the old lord is the image of pure *yang*. True mercury, driven by the outer fire, flies into the divine chamber to unite with true lead, lovingly merging to transform into a pure *yang* body. Thus, it is said, "marrying the Metal Elder as her old lord." "Coming back" signifies drawing it into the Central Palace.

**Exegesis:**
The fire of the outer medicine is called mercury fire; the fire of the inner medicine is also called mercury fire. In the outer medicine, true lead is born when mercury fire congeals. In the inner medicine, the sacred embryo is born when one’s own mercury fire unites with the outer mercury fire and true lead. Thus, it is collectively called the Maiden, whose wanderings each have their own direction. It is originally a single taste of mercury, circulating throughout the body—mercury is mercury fire.

---

**Twenty-Seven**
Though you recognize cinnabar and black lead,
Without knowing the fire-timing, it is as idle as a great city.
All depends on the power of cultivation—
A hair’s breadth of error, and the elixir will not form.

**Commentary:**
The creation of the golden elixir entirely depends on Ding Gong. A hair’s breadth of error leads to a thousand *li* of deviation. Thus, the sage transmits the medicine but not the fire—it must be discussed in detail with an immortal.

**Exegesis:**
Cinnabar and black lead are not material substances—they are true dragon and true fire. Recognizing them but failing to grasp the fire-timing still does not yield the elixir. The *Daoguang Ci* states: "Three of like mind, be cautious of reckless fire-advancement; the work of fire must be meticulously explained." The *Nihe Poem* says: "Without like-minded companions to correct you, you may fear the fire-timing in the furnace is amiss." Thus, cultivation greatly relies on true friends. If there is even a slight deviation, the elixir cannot form. One must encounter a true master to clarify the great Dao, for the heart-transmission of fire-timing is not recorded in texts. Profound and mysterious, it is a celestial secret—only those with predestined affinity may encounter it and swiftly cultivate it.

---

**Twenty-Eight**
The *Cantong Qi* and scriptural songs speak of the true,
Yet they do not commit the fire-timing to writing.
To know the oral secrets and penetrate the profound,
You must discuss them in detail with the divine.

**Commentary:**
The fire-timing spans six hundred chapters, each resembling the others, interconnected and aligned with heaven’s measure. What heaven conceals, the sage does not transmit in writing. If you encounter a true master, do not act rashly.

**Exegesis:**
The six hundred chapters of fire-timing use sixty hexagrams for one month, making sixty chapters. Ten months complete six hundred chapters, each resembling the others—day after day, they are the same. Reading the *Cantong Qi* once will make this clear.

---

**Twenty-Nine**
On the fifteenth of the eighth month, admire the toad’s radiance—
This is precisely when metal’s essence is robust.
When the first *yang* arrives at *Fu*,
It is time to advance the fire—do not delay.

**Commentary:**
The fifteenth of the eighth month is when the *qi* of metal and water is flourishing. The *zi* hour is when the first *yang* returns at *Fu*. The fire-work of both outer and inner elixirs must advance simultaneously—do not delay and miss the seasonal node.

**Exegesis:**
The fifteenth is the full moon, the mean. The fourteenth is excessive; the sixteenth is insufficient. Only the full moon attains the mean, which is harmony.

---

**Thirty**
When the first *yang* stirs, it is time to make the elixir—
The lead cauldron warms, illuminating the curtains.
At the inception of receiving *qi*, it is easily obtained;
In the fire’s withdrawal and addition, beware of danger.

**Commentary:**
The sage, having exhausted spirit and searched the profound, silently knows when the metal essence’s *qi* is flourishing and the first *yang* stirs. Capturing the dragon and seizing the tiger, deploying civil and martial arts, he lures the true *qi* of Great Unity into the lead cauldron’s chamber of mutual resonance. Warmly, it nurtures a millet pearl, its radiance brilliantly piercing the curtains. In less than half an hour, the elixir is obtained—truly, at the inception of receiving *qi*, it is easily gained.

After ingesting the elixir, the movement of *yin* tally and *yang* fire requires ten months of effort. It begins with *Kun*’s thunder, transforms into *Feng*’s layering, rises from dawn, and does not end until dusk. The operations of withdrawal and addition circulate without cease. At this time, one’s emotions are like withered wood, the heart like dead ashes—guarding against danger, fearing peril, and never acting recklessly. Thus, externally, one harmonizes with the *yin-yang* tally and fire; internally, one generates the substance of golden liquid. The circulation never stops: ascending from the *weilü*, reversing to the *niwan*, descending through the *chonglou*, and returning to the Central Palace’s earthen cauldron—this is the golden liquid’s return as the elixir.

The numinous efficacy defies description—how, then, in the operations of withdrawal and addition, could one fail to be vigilant against peril and mindful of danger?

**Commentary:** The *Ruyao Jing* states, "Receiving *qi* is auspicious; guarding the city is inauspicious." This is the caution required. The subsequent return to *Kun* marks the beginning and end of *yin*’s waning and *yang*’s waxing over twelve months. Thunder and wind correspond to the moon’s birth in *Zhen* and its culmination in *Kun*, the six phases of waxing and waning that define its cycle. The hexagrams *Zhun* and *Meng* span the twelve hours of a day and the thirty days of a month, concluding the progression of hexagrams and lines—thus, the work of circulating fire aligns with celestial measure.

When the *mysterious pearl* takes form, it follows *yang*’s ascent: as *yang* reaches its peak, *yin* recedes, gradually stripping away the body. By the tenth month, frost descends, and the elixir ripens. At this time, even the spirits must marvel.

**Note:** The *golden liquid returning as elixir* assumes form because, from the Winter Solstice onward, a single *yang* advances, and *yang* fire pursues *yang*’s growth to generate the substance of golden liquid. By the time a single *yin* advances, the stripping away culminates in the tenth month’s frost, when the returning elixir matures, shedding its mortal coil to transform into a being of pure *yang*—how could the spirits not be astonished and submit in awe?

Before the *upper crescent* and after the *lower crescent*, the medicinal flavor is balanced, its *qi*-aspect complete—gather it and return to the furnace for refinement, where gentle nurturing and intense firing proceed.

**Note:** By the thirtieth day of the lunar month, the *yang* soul’s gold is exhausted, and the *yin* spirit’s water fills the wheel, rendering it utterly dark and lightless. This mirrors the hexagram *Kun*, hence the term "darkness." At this time, the moon conjoins the sun during the two days of darkness and new moon, moving in unison, rising and setting together. By the second day, it borrows the sun’s light to conceive, gradually separating until, at sunset on the third day, a crescent appears in the west, *geng* emerging within pure *yin*—a single *yang* light born within the spirit, a soul within the spirit, mirroring the hexagram *Zhen*. At this moment, the *yang* soul’s gold is newly sprouted, the medicinal seedling fresh.

By the eighth day, two *yang* lines appear, mirroring the hexagram *Dui*. Here, the soul within the spirit reaches half, its balance as straight as a plumb line—hence the term *upper crescent*. Before this crescent belongs to *yin*, after it to *yang*; within *yin*, half yields eight ounces of water’s gold, its flavor balanced, its *qi*-aspect complete.

By the fifteenth day, three *yang* lines are complete, mirroring the hexagram *Qian*. Now, the *yin* spirit’s water is exhausted, and the *yang* soul’s gold fills the wheel, forming a perfect circle of pure *yang* without *yin*—hence the term "full moon." As *yang* reaches its peak, *yin* is born: on the sixteenth day, a single *yin* emerges within the pure *yang* wheel, a spirit within the soul, mirroring the hexagram *Xun*. Gradually waning, by the twenty-third day, two *yin* lines appear, mirroring the hexagram *Gen*. Here, the spirit within the soul reaches half, its balance as straight as a plumb line—hence the term *lower crescent*. Before this crescent belongs to *yang*, after it to *yin*; within *yang*, half yields eight ounces of gold’s water, its flavor balanced, its *qi*-aspect complete.

Thus, the sage gathers the essence of this *gold and water of the two eights*, seizing it to return to the furnace of creation, where the true *qi* of the One is refined. Transforming it into a millet grain, it is swallowed into the five viscera, then circulated with fire, gently nurtured and intensely fired to complete the *golden liquid returning as elixir*. This entirely depends on the advance and retreat of *yin* tally and *yang* fire, the withdrawal and addition—if even a hair’s breadth errs, no elixir forms.

The immortal master, in this chapter, repeatedly exhorts those who refine themselves, and not without reason.

**Commentary:** The *two eights* take their form from the moon’s gold and water; the six phases take their form from the moon’s waxing and waning—gold is *yang*, water is *yin*. The *qi* of the two crescents is the fire of *yin* and *yang*. Five days make one phase, completing the number of the Five Agents. "Before the *upper crescent* and after" refers to the period before the *upper crescent* (yin) and after (yang), where gold and water each weigh half a catty—this is the *two eights*. "After the *lower crescent* and before" refers to the period after the *lower crescent* (yang) and before (yin), where gold and water also each weigh half a catty—this, too, is the *two eights*. The *upper* and *lower crescents* are both *two eights*. The sage, using the essence of the *gold and water of the two eights*, gathers from the *upper* and *lower crescents* to obtain the balanced flavor and complete *qi*-aspect of the *two eights*—thus the elixir coalesces.

Many mistakenly fixate on the full moon, but on the full-moon day, the moon is full in *gan-jia*, a full catty of *yang* gold—this subtlety of the *two eights* is known only to those who encounter a true master. The correct method lies in taking eight ounces of gold and water from the *upper* and *lower crescents*, the proper *two eights* for each crescent. Every crescent contains the *mysterious two eights* of gold and water.

The eldest son suddenly drinks the wine of the western quarter,
The youngest daughter first blooms the flower of the northern garden.
If the Azure Maiden and the Alchemical Maiden meet thereafter,
At once the lock is sealed within the Yellow House.

Annotation:
*Zhen* is the eldest son, the Azure Dragon; wine is a yin substance, storing yin *qi*—this is called *yin fire*. *Dui* is the youngest daughter, the White Tiger; the flower is a yang substance, storing yang *qi*—this is called *yang fire*. The Azure Maiden and the Alchemical Maiden are called *mercury fire*. These are all terms used by adepts of the elixir: they drive the Dragon to approach the Tiger, and the Tiger, blooming the flower of the northern garden, comes to the Dragon. The Dragon drinks the wine of the western quarter to approach the Tiger. When Dragon and Tiger devour and intertwine, the image begins to form—then the *mercury fire* of the Azure Maiden is set in motion to meet with the three fires of Dragon and Tiger. After their mutual longing, at once it is sealed within the Yellow House of the Central Palace, producing the true unity of essence and forming the *Golden Liquor Returned Elixir*. The Yellow House is the crucible and the *mysterious barrier*.

Exegesis:
The first two lines speak of the *outer medicine*: the Azure Dragon stores yin *qi*, the White Tiger stores yang *qi*. The latter two lines speak of the *inner medicine*: the Azure Maiden is one’s own true *qi*, meeting the two *qi* of Dragon and Tiger in mutual longing, sealed within the Central Palace. Another version’s annotation takes the Azure Maiden as the *qi* of the Dragon’s crescent—this would again be outer, but since the first two lines have already spoken of the eldest son, it should not be repeated, and thus it is deleted. The Immortal Elder’s poem says, *"To bind the Alchemical Maiden in kinship,"* where *Alchemical Maiden* is the same as here. *"The Alchemical Maiden roams, each to their own direction"* further clarifies the inner and outer. Each poem points to different meanings—one must not cling to the names.

---

In the months of the Hare and the Rooster, when their time arrives,
Punishment and virtue descend at the gate—this is the arrival of the medicine’s image.
Here, the Golden Elixir should be bathed.
If fire is added instead, peril and ruin will surely follow.

**Annotation states:** The second month is governed by virtue, the eighth by punishment—these two months mark the season for bathing. Here, one should cease the fire; if fire is added instead, peril will surely follow, and the Returned Elixir will scatter and be lost.

**Exegesis states:** The present annotation says the second month is for virtue and the eighth for punishment, yet in the *Pi* and *Tai* hexagrams, just as they intersect, the myriad things flourish. Another annotation reverses this, calling the second month punishment and the eighth virtue. For in the second month, virtue lies in generation, yet the elm’s pods fall—within virtue, punishment resides. In the eighth month, punishment lies in withering, yet wheat sprouts—within punishment, virtue resides. Thus, punishment and virtue are spoken of interchangeably.

---

**Thirty-Five**
Sun and moon meet once every thirty days,
Their encounter timed, the day’s method shifts.
Divine work guards the city, battles in the wild—
Know fortune and misfortune, and the numinous cinnabar fills the crucible red.

**Annotation states:** The sun and moon conjoin once each month. The sage, understanding this, adjusts the cycle—one month becomes a day, one day an hour. Guarding the city means bathing and ceasing work; battling in the wild means the dragon and tiger engage in struggle. *Divine work* refers to the measure of advancing fire. If yin and yang are disordered, sun and moon discordant, though the outer fire moves, the inner tally remains still and unresponsive. The adept, advancing or retreating water and fire, knows fortune and misfortune, revolving the Dipper and traversing the Winnowing Basket, darkly harmonizing with celestial degrees. Naturally, the numinous embryo silently moves, and the divine crucible glows ever brighter.

**Exegesis states:** "Shifting the day by the hour" means that within each hour, there is a *zi* and *wu*, its yin and yang beginning and end all aligned with heaven, earth, sun, and moon. The handle of the Winnowing Basket and Dipper lies in the *gen* and *yin* positions. Yang fire resides in *zi*, fire in *chou* and *wei* flourishing in the northeast’s *gen* region, not far from *yin*. The moon’s essence also hides in *gen*. The lodging of the Winnowing Basket and Dipper is the position where fire is born—all aligned with celestial degrees. The *Cantong Qi* says, "It begins in the northeast, the region of the Winnowing Basket and Dipper." Revolving rightward forms the third day, the moon born in *zhen* and *geng*. Revolving leftward forms the first month, fire born in *yin*. The hexagram of the month is *Tai*.

---

**Thirty-Six**
As *Pi* and *Tai* just intersect, the myriad things flourish.
*Tun* guards against receiving the hexagram’s mandate of generation and completion.
Within this, grasp the meaning—do not seek images.
If you exhaust the lines, your spirit will be vainly taxed.

**Annotation states:** The winter and summer solstices mark the beginning of one yin and one yang. The *zi* and *wu* hours are the origin of one day and one night. The sage moves yin tally and yang fire, harmonizing with heaven and earth’s ascending and descending Dao, the sun and moon’s coming and going. Gathering the four seasons, eight nodes, twenty-four qi, and seventy-two hou, they array them within the crucible to generate the true unity of the body. This principle is simple, its work not cumbersome—nothing can be said of its action. Thus, it is entrusted to hexagrams, divided within a month’s thirty days, to unfold the mysterious mechanism and clarify the fire times. The use of line images is but a net and trap.

*Tun* and *Meng* are the first of the many hexagrams, symbolizing the beginning of fire’s movement, generation, and completion, the source of creation’s endowment. Thus, *Tun* is used at dawn, *Meng* at dusk.

*Pi* and *Tai* represent yin ascending and yang descending within the four seasons. By the second month’s spring equinox, yang qi rises to the center of heaven and earth, yin and yang equally balanced—neither cold nor warm, hence the *Tai* hexagram. This is like the moon’s waxing phase. At this time, yin and yang qi naturally intersect, so the sage does not advance fire—this is called bathing.

By the eighth month’s autumn equinox, yin qi descends to the center of heaven and earth, yin and yang again equally balanced—neither warm nor cold, hence the *Pi* hexagram. This is like the moon’s waning phase. At this time, yin and yang qi naturally intersect, so the sage does not advance water—this too is called bathing. Thus, the Immortal Elder said, *"In the months of the Hare and the Rooster, when their time arrives, punishment and virtue descend at the gate—this is the arrival of the medicine’s image."* The second month is punishment, the eighth virtue.

If the cultivator of the Elixir can grasp the meaning within these four hexagrams, why cling to the many lines and weary the heart with labored thought? The Immortal Elder, in his compassion, directly points to this shortcut.

**Exegesis states:** *Pi* and *Tai* are the bathing months. A year has twelve months; ten are used to gestate the embryo, excluding the two bathing months. *Tun* and *Meng* are the sun and moon’s two hexagrams. The two hexagrams together have twelve lines, symbolizing a day’s twelve hours. Of the sixty-four hexagrams, excluding *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, *Li*, and the four of the female and male, only sixty are used, corresponding to a month’s thirty days. This reflects the principle of heaven and earth’s 84,000 *li* of ascent and descent. At the spring and autumn equinoxes, exactly 24,000 *li* are traversed, precisely at the center of heaven and earth. Thus, the *Pi* and *Tai* hexagrams, with yin and yang evenly balanced above and below, are borrowed as metaphors.

The day’s hours at the second and eighth months are also evenly balanced. The moon’s waxing and waning phases likewise have gold and water each at half a *jin*. If discussing the monthly hexagrams, *Tai* is the first month, *Pi* the seventh—not the hexagrams of the second and eighth months. The *Cantong Qi* says, *"Great Strength at the *mao* gate, observe in mid-autumn the tally’s rest."* The second and eighth months are the *Dazhuang* and *Guan* hexagrams.

Master Peng’s annotation on *Tai* says, *"Yin and yang qi are balanced, husband and wife unite."* On *Pi*, *"Heaven and earth both rest, yin and yang do not intersect."* For when balanced, they do not intersect; when one is more or less, they do. When yang is above and yin below, they do not intersect; when yin is above and yang below, they do—this is the principle of things.

Once this principle is understood, there is no need to cling to hexagrams and lines to tax the spirit.

---

**Thirty-Seven**

Within the hexagrams, the method is established through forms to obtain images—words may be forgotten, yet meaning becomes self-evident. Yet the deluded of the world cling only to images, practicing *gua qi* in hopes of ascension.

The annotation states: The hexagrams are but the trap and snare of fire. The Perfected Wei Boyang, upon reading the *Yi*, awakened to the workings of the Golden Elixir, seeing its Dao as one with the *Yi*. Thus he composed the *Cantong Qi*, expounding the hexagrams of the *Great Yi* to clarify the alchemy’s safeguards, offering guidance to later generations. He likened *Qian* and *Kun* to the cauldron and vessel, the numinous embryo and spirit-chamber within our cinnabar field. He further compared *Kan* and *Li* to the medicinal substances, lead and mercury within the numinous embryo and spirit-chamber. For *Qian* and *Kun* are the parents of all hexagrams, and *Kan* and *Li* the true essence of *Qian* and *Kun*. Thus these four hexagrams reside in the central palace, just as the numinous embryo, lead, and mercury dwell within the cinnabar field. The inner regulates the outer, so these four hexagrams are not bound to the fire-manipulation sequence. The remaining hexagrams are distributed across a single month, circulating the tally-fire, beginning with *Zhun* and ending with *Jiwei*, cycling without cease like a wheel’s turning. Each day, two hexagrams govern affairs; thirty days account for sixty hexagrams. Together with *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, and *Li*—the cauldron, vessel, and medicinal substances—this totals sixty-four hexagrams and three hundred eighty-four lines, mirroring a year’s three hundred eighty-four days, including intercalary months. It further reflects the two times eight ounces of the Golden Elixir, one *jin* equaling three hundred eighty-four *zhu*. All these are metaphors and established images. The adept who grasps this may perceive the workings of fire-manipulation through these hexagrams. Once the use of fire is understood, the hexagrams and their words may be forgotten as no longer needed.

Yet today’s scholars, failing to comprehend this safeguard, cling instead to these images to practice *gua qi*, exhausting their forms and tormenting their minds in hopes of ascension—is this not folly? One catches the fish and forgets the trap, snares the hare and forgets the snare. Now they cling to the trap and snare as if they were the fish and hare, drifting ever farther from the Dao.

Master Zhongli said: "How can the Great Dao be conveyed through words? Boyang borrowed the *Yi* to compose the *Cantong Qi*. Later generations, failing to recognize the immortals’ metaphors, cling to the trap and snare and set to work—this is the proof." The commentary states: The transmitted *gua qi* diagrams divide the sixty hexagrams, each line aligned with the breath-count to model the principles of water and fire, yin and yang. Clinging to images, they practice thus—how could they know the Great Dao of the Golden Elixir, which uses hexagrams as mere traps and snares? The sixty hexagrams all derive from the pure yin and yang of *Qian* and *Kun*, yet only *Kan* and *Li* obtain the central qi of *Qian* and *Kun* and are thus correct. Excluding these four hexagrams as the female and male, *Qian* and *Kun* serve as the body, *Kan* and *Li* as the function. The sixty-four hexagrams serve as tally-signs, divided into cauldron, vessel, and medicinal substances, altogether forming the fire-phases of the celestial cycle. The alchemical Dao accords with heaven and earth, the *Yi*’s images harmonize with heaven and earth—thus the *Yi* is borrowed to illuminate the Dao.

**Thirty-Eight**

Heaven and earth’s fullness and emptiness have their appointed times. Only by discerning their waxing and waning can one know the mechanism’s origin. When *geng* and *jia* are made clear and the command is executed, the Three Worms are annihilated, and the Dao may be attained.

The annotation states: Heaven and earth’s fullness and emptiness have their appointed times. Heaven and earth are separated by eighty-four thousand *li*. On the winter solstice, a single yang qi stirs within the earth, ascending daily by four hundred sixty *li* and two hundred forty *bu*. After five days, it forms one *hou*; three *hou* make one *qi*; two *qi* make one *jie*; two *jie* make one season—this is the spring equinox. Over ninety days, the yang qi ascends forty-two thousand *li*, precisely to the midpoint between heaven and earth. At this time, yin contains half yang, forming the *Tai* hexagram. Its qi transforms from cold to warm, the time of the myriad things’ arising—thus it is spring.

From this point onward, the yang qi ascends into the yang position, gradually rising as before until the summer solstice. Counting from the winter solstice, one hundred eighty days have passed, and it has ascended eighty-four thousand *li*, reaching heaven. At this time, yang contains yet more yang, forming the pure yang *Qian* hexagram. Its qi transforms from warm to hot—this is summer, the time of the myriad things’ flourishing, thus called "fullness."

When heat reaches its extreme, yin arises. On the summer solstice, a single yin descends from heaven, also descending daily by four hundred sixty *li* and two hundred forty *bu*. Five days form one *hou*; three *hou* make one *qi*; two *qi* make one *jie*; two *jie* make one season—this is the autumn equinox. Over ninety days, the yin qi descends forty-two thousand *li*, precisely to the midpoint between heaven and earth. At this time, yang contains half yin, forming the *Pi* hexagram. Its qi transforms from hot to cool, the time of the myriad things’ fruiting—thus it is autumn.

From this point onward, the yin qi descends into the yin position, gradually descending as before until the winter solstice. Counting from the summer solstice, one hundred eighty days have passed, and it has descended eighty-four thousand *li*, reaching earth. At this time, yin contains yet more yin, forming the pure yin *Kun* hexagram. Its qi transforms from cool to cold—this is winter, the time of the myriad things’ withdrawal, thus called "emptiness."

The sage discerns the waxing and waning of heaven and earth’s fullness and emptiness, observing it through the months, which arise from the days. On the third day, *Zhen* *geng* takes form; on the eighth day, *Dui* *ding* completes form; on the fifteenth day, *Qian* *jia* reaches fullness—this is the time of heaven and earth’s fullness. On the sixteenth day, *Xun* *xin* receives governance; on the twenty-third day, *Gen* *bing* guards the tally; on the thirtieth day, *Kun* *yi* dissolves—this is the time of heaven and earth’s emptiness.

The sage, able to discern the mechanism of heaven and earth’s waxing and waning, condenses a year’s seasonal qi into a single month. The first day, the arising of the single yang, corresponds to the winter solstice. Dividing two and a half days into thirty hours accounts for thirty days, matching a month’s seasonal qi. The upper tally day, when yin contains half yang, corresponds to the spring equinox. By the fifteenth day, the four months’ seasonal qi are obtained, forming pure yang—thus it is called "fullness," the yang qi’s completion, hence "fullness." By the sixteenth day, yin arises, corresponding to the summer solstice. The lower tally day, when yang contains half yin, mirrors the autumn equinox. By the thirtieth day, the ten months’ seasonal qi are obtained, forming pure yin—the yin qi’s completion, hence "emptiness." Ending and beginning anew, it cycles without cease.

The sage manipulates the yang fire and yin tally, following precisely heaven and earth’s waxing and waning, ascending and descending, the sixty-four hexagrams’ progression from *geng* to *jia*, and the principle of the moon’s waxing and waning. Just as the sovereign issues commands to annihilate the yin demons, so too may the Dao be attained.

The commentary states: There is the fullness and emptiness of heaven and earth, and the fullness and emptiness of the sun and moon. The sage models and aligns with heaven and earth, sun and moon’s fullness and emptiness. *Geng* and *jia* are the degrees of fire-progression, thus modeled on the moon. The moon arises in *Zhen* *geng*, the beginning of the moon’s fullness, where the yin tally retreats and the yang fire advances. The moon is full in *Qian* *jia*, the beginning of the moon’s emptiness, where the yang fire retreats and the yin tally advances—this too is the principle of fullness and emptiness. Moreover, *jia* wood is the dragon, *geng* metal the tiger—this is also the image of the dragon and tiger.

Thirty-Nine
To ensure the Valley Spirit never dies,
One must rely on the Mysterious Female to establish the root.
Once true essence returns,
A golden house arises—
A single luminous pearl never departs.

The commentary states: That which is unfathomable in yin and yang is called *shen*. *Shen* has no form; it responds and thus communicates, like an echo answering a valley—hence "Valley Spirit." *Shen* is established through *qi*, *qi* is born from essence, and essence can generate *qi*, while *qi* can generate *shen*. Thus, *qi* is the master of the body, and the body is the abode of *shen* and *qi*. Without *shen* and *qi*, the form cannot live; without form, *shen* and *qi* cannot stand. These three depend on one another to give rise to life. If one desires longevity, the root must first be established in the Mysterious Female—only then can long life be attained. All spirits are born from these two and die through them. They are truly the root of heaven and earth, the ancestor of the Five Phases, the stem of yin and yang, and the foundation of the myriad transformations. The sage relies on them to achieve the external elixir and uses them to transform the inner cinnabar. Thus, when true essence is set in motion without cease, it returns to the golden crucible of earth, transmuting into a single luminous pearl whose radiance never flees. Gradually, form is refined into *qi*, *qi* into *shen*, until both form and *shen* attain wondrous subtlety, becoming as profound as the dragon’s manifestation.

Forty
The Gate of the Mysterious Female—few in the world know it.
Do not mistakenly apply effort to mouth and nose,
For even if you practice breathwork for a thousand years,
How could you seize the Golden Crow and grasp the Hare?

The commentary states: The Gate of the Mysterious Female is called the root of heaven and earth. How wondrous this saying! Yet none in the world can comprehend it—without a true teacher’s guidance, who could understand? Some, like Ye Wenshu, point to the space between the two kidneys as the "Mixed Primordial Cavity," but how could they glimpse the celestial mechanism and presume to dismiss other teachings? The Mysterious Female consists of two things—how could it be reduced to a single cavity? Since the beginning of creation, without these two, how could the myriad things exist? Thus, both the inner and outer elixirs are established through them. The sage conceals this, naming it the "Crescent Moon Furnace" and the "Suspended Embryo Crucible." The Golden Crow is the golden elixir; the Hare is one’s true *qi*. The golden elixir restrains one’s mercury, like a cat catching a rat or a hawk seizing a hare, allowing no escape. If one mistakes mouth and nose for the Mysterious Female, even after a thousand years of breathwork, one will only grow frail—how could one seize the Golden Crow, grasp the Hare, and form the sacred embryo?

The sub-commentary states: *Xuan* is yang; *pin* is yin. The *Book of Changes* says, "Heaven is *xuan* and earth is yellow; the hexagram *Kun* benefits the steadfastness of the mare." Here, *xuan* is borrowed to signify yang, and *pin* to signify yin. It is called a "gate" because the myriad things are born and die through this gate, and the Mysterious Female enters and exits through it. The terms "furnace" and "crucible" are also borrowed names. Master Bao’s *Song of the Mysterious Female* says, "Between the two kidneys, a radiant barrier shines." Later generations thus point to the space between the kidneys as the "Mixed Primordial Cavity," unaware that the two kidneys are merely metaphors for the wondrous workings of the body—two things emerging from the same source yet bearing different names. If one can unite them, a single luminous millet-pearl may be obtained in an instant—this is the true Gate of the Mysterious Female. Those who do not understand the metaphor cling to the *Song of the Mysterious Female* as literal truth, mistaking the space between the kidneys for the gate, or even misidentifying mouth and nose as the Mysterious Female—such are the errors of superficial understanding.

Forty-One
Different names, same origin—few know this.
These two, profoundly mysterious, are the crucial mechanism.
Preserve life, complete the form,
Understand gain and loss—
The Purple Gold Elixir is most wondrous.

The commentary states: The Most High said, "Nameless, it is the beginning of heaven and earth; named, it is the mother of the myriad things." He also said, "These two emerge from the same source yet bear different names." When it is formless, the true unity of *qi* is invisible—hence it is the beginning of heaven and earth. When it takes form, the true unity of *qi* transforms into a millet-grain, appearing within the empty mystery—hence it is the mother of the myriad things. In heaven, it is *Li* as mercury; on earth, it is *Kan* as lead. Their root is the same, but their emergence differs. This sameness is called "mysterious within the mysterious." In the practice of the Dao, grasping these two mysterious mechanisms to understand gain and loss and cultivate the body allows one to preserve form and safeguard life. These two are simply the yin and yang *qi*. As for "loss," it refers to the Five Phases following their natural course—this is the ordinary path of birth and extinction. Alas! The Purple Gold Elixir of pure yang is established as the beginning of heaven and earth and emerges as the mother of the myriad things. When it is said that the Purple Gold Elixir is most wondrous, know that the immortal sages’ admiration is boundless.

The sub-commentary states: In heaven, it is *Li* as mercury—fire flames upward as *Li*, rooted in heaven, which is yang above. Wood generates fire within, producing cinnabar; the yang of heaven contains yin, and the solemn yin descends from heaven. On earth, it is *Kan* as lead—water moistens downward as *Kan*, rooted in earth, which is yin below. Water generates metal within, producing lead; the yin of earth contains yang, and the blazing yang ascends from earth. Once heaven and earth are established in their positions and the sun and moon take form, all are transformations of the two *qi*—water as yin and fire as yang. Fire flames upward, light and clear, bright without and dark within; water moistens downward, heavy and turbid, dark within and bright without. After heaven, earth, sun, and moon take form, the Five Phases each assume their forms within heaven and earth. Metal, when struck, produces fire; when smelted, it becomes water. Wood, when drilled, produces fire; when pressed, it yields water. Earth is born from fire and moistened by water. Metal and wood are not the union of fire; rather, the two *qi* of water and fire pervade metal, wood, and earth. Water and fire cannot generate themselves—humans must act upon them. As for metal, wood, and earth, they cannot act on their own but must await human use—thus, the water and fire of the Five Phases are those that retain the fullness of *qi*. Heaven and earth, the myriad things—none exist beyond the Five Phases; the Five Phases, in turn, do not depart from yin and yang; and yin and yang emerge together from the Supreme Ultimate. This is the meaning of "emerging from the same source yet bearing different names." Their root is the same—the root of the Mysterious Female emerges from the true unity of the Supreme Ultimate. Their emergence differs—the true unity of *qi* divides into the yin and yang of the Mysterious Female. This is the sameness of their root and the difference of their emergence. The two of the Mysterious Female emerge from the undifferentiated *qi* of the Supreme Ultimate. Once formed, they receive their nature in purity and reside in their proper places. By inverting the practice, the Purple Gold Elixir can be achieved.

Forty-Two
At first, one acts—people rush to notice.
Only when one reaches non-action do the many begin to understand.
They see non-action as the wonder of the Dao,
Yet do not know that action is the root.

The commentary states: Some study the Buddha’s path of cultivating nature, clinging to the notion that all action is illusory and false, and thus disparage the Daoist path of cultivating life. These are those who know one aspect but not the other—those who glimpse the gate but have not entered the hall or the inner chamber.

Forty-Three
Within the black lies white—this is the Elixir Mother;
Within the male hides female—this is the Sacred Embryo.
The Supreme One resides in the crucible—guard it well,
Treasure gathered in the Three Fields aligns with the Three Terraces.

The commentary states: Extracting silver from lead becomes the Elixir Mother;
Drawing mercury from cinnabar forms the Sacred Embryo.
These two stir and transform the *qi* of the True One,
Coalescing within the crucible of the Supreme One.
Only by refining the fire’s timing and serenely upholding the method,
Without the slightest deviation,
Do the Three Natures merge to crystallize the Elixir Treasure,
Its radiance ascending to match the Three Terraces.
The Supreme One holds the true *qi*—thus it is said:
“The Supreme One embraces the true *qi*.”

The annotation states: Extracting silver from lead and drawing mercury from cinnabar
Are but borrowed external substances to embody the principle of yin-yang mutual engagement.
Yet people, unaware, mistakenly pursue refinement and ingestion,
Or misguidedly compose commentaries—leading many astray.
In the *Golden Crucible*, the Nameless Master sought to preserve the mercury within cinnabar,
With poems on the Azure Dragon and Black Tiger, each to east and west.
All these are but analogies—like silver in lead, mercury in cinnabar.
By studying the three poems deeply,
One discerns the marvel of these two substances,
For only they can stir and transform the *qi* of the True One—
How could common lead or mercury ever suffice?

Forty-Four
Within the dim and indistinct, seek the image;
Amid the profound and obscure, find the true essence.
From being and non-being, each enters the other—
How could mere thought ever grasp their formation?

The commentary states: Within the dim and indistinct lies the image—this is the dragon’s *qi*;
Amid the profound and obscure dwells the essence—this is the tiger’s *qi*.
Both are present as *qi* yet lack form.
Vague and elusive, deep and remote—
Seen but not visible, heard but not audible—
This is the *qi* of the True One.
The *qi* of the True One is supremely numinous yet formless.
The True One Master said:
Non-being is the dragon; being is the tiger.
Non-being is the *qi* of mercury; being is the *qi* of lead.
Non-being, stirred by being, takes form;
Being, moved by non-being, gains numinosity.
Thus the millet pearl hangs in emptiness,
And purple frost gleams in the sunlight.
Those who sit rigidly in meditation, clinging to dust-laden thoughts—
How pitiful they are!

The annotation states: The *Cantong Qi* says: “Being and non-being restrain each other.”
When the upper is closed, it is called being;
When the lower is closed, it is called non-being.
Master Peng’s *Exegesis of the True* divides this into two interpretations,
But the Nameless Master here cites the principle of mutual restraint between being and non-being—
This is the crucial secret of the Great Elixir,
Contained in the meaning of the two words: lead and fire.
Now, examining this poem—
Above, it lists the dim and obscure; below, it summarizes with being and non-being.
Thus, it should follow the meaning of upper and lower closure.
Yet one must not be rigidly bound by the commentary.
Being and non-being restrain each other—
The *Jinbi Shangjing* states: “Take the two non-beings as the school, the one being as the gate.”
The enlightened sage awakens to the Dao—how could it lie in clinging to the text?
If one penetrates deeply, all applications align.

Forty-Five
When the Four Images are complete, the Mysterious Body takes form;
When the Five Agents are whole, the Purple Radiance shines.
Shedding the husk, it enters the mouth—
Divine and sacred beyond measure,
Even the dragon spirits flee in awe.

The annotation states: When dragon and tiger conjoin in union, the Four Images are complete and the Five Agents whole. When the Four Images and Five Agents unite in harmony, the true and singular body coalesces like a millet-grain pearl, its purple radiance shining. Secretly refined within, it is seized and drawn into the mouth—passing through the divine and attaining the sacred without limit. How could the dragon spirits not be struck with awe and reverence?

The commentary explains: The Four Images are the Azure Dragon, White Tiger, Vermilion Bird, and Dark Warrior. The Five Agents are Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth. The great Dao is empty and without form, yet takes the golden elixir as its profound mystery. Though the golden elixir is wondrous, it is nothing more than the gathering and harmonizing of the Five Agents and the union of the Four Images. When the Four Images unite as one, the Mysterious Body is surely formed; when the Five Agents harmonize, the elixir’s radiance naturally shines. This is neither the fire of stored intention nor the water of the kidneys, nor is it the liver as dragon and lungs as tiger. Heaven generates humanity, and humanity generates the numinous treasure—the Five Agents gather here, the Four Images assemble here. If one obtains the Mysterious Mechanism and refines the great medicine, shedding the husk and entering the mouth, one transcends the mundane and enters sagehood. How could the boundless dragon spirits not be filled with awe and reverence?

Forty-Six
After drinking from the Flowery Pond, the moon’s radiance grows clear.
Mounting a golden dragon, I visit the Purple Tenuity.
From this time forth, all immortals know me—
Whether the sea fields shift or the hills and valleys move.

**Annotation states:** The Flowery Pond is the elixir. Once the drinking is complete, the work is perfected, the embryo shed, and the spirit transformed—flesh like ice and snow, graceful as Liezi riding the qi and clouds to roam the eight extremities. Having beheld the dusty world to the full, one lets the seas turn to mulberry fields, the mulberry fields turn to seas, high ridges become valleys, and deep valleys become ridges.

**Forty-Seven**
To know the method of refining, nurturing, and returning the elixir,
One must sow the seed in one’s own garden—
No need for forced breath or straining effort,
For the fruit will ripen naturally, the numinous embryo shed.

**Annotation states:** This thing is none other than what lies within one’s own body, of the same kind. The Dao is most near, never distant from humanity—just as planting in one’s garden yields its own growth. Its nearness is evident. If the seed is not of the same kind, success is difficult; if it is, it is as easy as turning the palm. The *Cantong Qi* says: "When of the same kind, effort is easily applied; when not, skill is hard to achieve." What need is there for straining effort?

**Commentary states:** The previous verse speaks of idly tending the medicine furnace and watching the fire-timer, and also says there is a natural true fire for nurturing. Here, it states there is no need for forced breath or straining effort—all refer to the workings of the inner medicine. It further speaks of setting up the furnace and establishing the tripod, gathering and refining, with the Great One in the furnace—all refer to the workings of the outer medicine. This thing is the Yang elixir. The Yang elixir, being of the same kind as oneself, easily forms the embryo. The *Mud Pill* speaks of "one *mu* within the body as one’s garden." Without a teacher’s transmission, one may rashly guess and speculate. Fortunate is the one who receives the transmission, so that all may easily understand and together ascend to the fruit of immortality. Thus, where the annotation was not fully clear, I have further elucidated its meaning. The poems and words are each distinguished by their kind, yet within what is easily known, there are also things difficult to know, which I dare not lightly commit to bamboo and silk. For those who study immortality and possess the karmic affinity for it, this book—with its annotations and commentaries—offers a clear and unerring path. If one can fully awaken, there will come a day of attaining the great Dao. This text, a treasure of the immortal’s satchel, is guarded by numinous spirits at every turn. How could one not cherish and deeply study it?

**Forty-Eight**
Cease all artifice and forced effort—
Recognize the deathless method of the other household.
Within the alchemical vessel, steadily brew the wine of extended life;
Within the tripod, gather the nectar of returning souls.

**Annotation states:** Many who cultivate the truth cling to methods that are not of the same kind, applying artifice and effort, yet refuse to seek the other household’s deathless method of the same kind. They can gather the Yang elixir of returning souls within the tripod and steadily brew the mercury-fire of extended life within the abdomen. These two things are the supreme treasures of true cultivation. The *Cantong Qi* says: "When of the same kind, effort is easily applied; when not, skill is hard to achieve." This is the proof. The so-called "other household" refers to the white tiger’s *qi*-essence. Later students often mistake their own bodily essence for true lead. If this were so, why would the immortal sages deceive others with talk of the "other household"?

**Commentary states:** The previous verse speaks of sowing the seed in one’s own garden. Wu Mingzi explains: "Refusing to seek the other household’s deathless method of the same kind." The earlier verse refers to oneself, hence "one’s own"; this verse teaches others, hence "the other household." Yet the same kind is one. This "same kind" does not mean one person with another, but the primordial qi in its undifferentiated unity. Using primordial qi to supplement primordial qi is like using boundless qi to replenish finite qi—hence the ease of attaining immortality. The *Cantong Qi* says: "Primal essence flows and spreads, borne by qi to lodge in things." This is the same kind. If one uses human to supplement human, the body is entirely yin; using yin to supplement yin is like a hen hatching its own egg—its form is incomplete. How can it achieve the marvel of yin-yang union? How can it congeal the primordial qi into an elixir? How can it transform the purely yang body into a purely yang immortal?

**Forty-Nine**
The snow mountain’s single flavor—fine *tighu*;
Poured into the Eastern Yang’s crucible of transformation.
If it passes beyond Kunlun to the northwest,
Only Zhang Qian would have seen Ma Gu.

**Annotation:**
The snow mountain’s white color symbolizes the west and the phase of metal—this is the golden elixir. A single grain of golden elixir tastes like fine *tighu*; taking it as medicine, it enters my cinnabar field within the crucible of transformation. Kunlun Mountain lies amid the sea of waters, and thus entering Kunlun is the place where fire is ignited. Atop Kunlun’s summit is a gate called the Mysterious Gate, which is the Gate of Heaven. The Gate of Heaven lies in the northwest, in the *gan* position, hence the immortal elder’s saying: "Plant it in the *gan* household’s chamber of intercourse." Thus, if one passes beyond the northwest, Zhang Qian would see Ma Gu.

Zhang Qian is a man, symbolizing the *Qian* hexagram and yang fire, and also representing true mercury. Ma Gu is a woman, symbolizing the *Kun* hexagram and the yin tally, and also representing true lead. This speaks of passing beyond Kunlun to ignite fire and enter through the Mysterious Gate, whereupon the true mercury within the crucible first meets true lead and undergoes transformation. As true lead inwardly melts with true fire and outwardly connects with the *Kun* symbol, it transforms into the *Qian* symbol and yang fire, driving out the yin tally. The two fires advance in mutual exchange, and lead and mercury congeal—here lies the root of the Dao of immortality. Zhang Qian riding a raft across the Heavenly River to meet the Woman Star is but an allegory for the mutual encounter of yin and yang.

**Exegesis:**
The outer fire is the true qi of heaven and earth; the inner fire is the ancestral qi of the primordial sea. Only when the two fires interflow do mercury and lead congeal, and the sacred embryo may be formed.

**Fifty**
Not knowing yin and yang, nor host and guest—
Who can tell which is distant, which near?
In the chamber, the tail gate is sealed in vain,
How many in Jambudvīpa have been slain!

**Annotation:**
Zhongli Quan said: "The four great elements of the body are all yin—what then is yang essence?" Now, yang essence is the essence of the true One, the qi of utmost yang, called the yang elixir. One’s own true qi is yin and serves as the master of the body, nourishing all its parts. When the yang elixir arrives from without to restrain one’s yin mercury, it becomes the host, while one’s own yin mercury becomes the guest. The two long for each other and congeal into golden sand, naturally neither flying nor fleeing. Then, with the addition of fire, it is refined into the golden liquid returning elixir. Thus, the yang elixir is external and called distant, while one’s own true qi is internal and called near. Reversing this near and distant to establish host and guest, the Dao is accomplished.

Those who lose their way do not grasp this principle and instead practice the bedchamber arts of controlling women, forcibly sealing their essence and qi, calling it "refining the yin elixir." Seeking to prolong life, they instead hasten death—this is like carrying firewood to extinguish a fire. The *Yinfu Jing* says: "Fire is born from wood, and calamity arises—it must be overcome." Can one not be cautious?

**Exegesis:**
When the guest becomes the host and the distant becomes near, this is the marvel of inversion. Those who seal the tail gate mistake it for the art of reversing the Yellow River’s flow—many have lost their lives thus.

**Fifty-One**

All things flourish and return to their root; returning to the root is called repose, and repose is called regaining life’s mandate—thus one abides long. To know the constant and return to the root is difficult to guard against; reckless action invites misfortune—this all have heard.

**Annotation:**
All things flourish and each returns to its root. Returning to the root is called stillness; stillness is called regaining life’s mandate; regaining life’s mandate is called the constant. To know the constant is called illumination—these are the supreme words of the Most High. Before a person is born, they dwell in darkness, without knowing, merged in primordial simplicity. At birth, they receive from yin and yang, inherit from father and mother. The sage reverses this and cultivates it, seizing the qi of precelestial origin as the elixir mother, plundering the true qi of yin and yang as the foundation of transformation. Refining form to reenter formlessness, refining qi to return to primordial simplicity, refining spirit to unite with the Dao in truth—thus returning to the root and regaining life’s mandate is long abiding. Those who can know the constant Dao and return to the root are sages—hence they attain long life. Those who do not know the constant Dao, who return to the root yet act recklessly, are common people—hence they invite misfortune.

**Fifty-Two**
Ouye personally transmitted the sword-casting method:
Mo Ye’s metal and water matched soft and hard,
Once refined, it could discern human intent,
Slaying demons a thousand miles away in a flash of lightning.

**Annotation:**
When Ouye cast the sword, the Heavenly Emperor sent a divine maiden to attend the furnace. He tempered it with metal and water, matched it with soft and hard, and after forging the precious sword, it could slay the fierce and cut down the evil in a flash of lightning—its numinous power was so divine. The making of the returning elixir and the casting of swords are alike: taking heaven and earth as the furnace, using yin and yang as water and fire, matching the Five Phases, controlling with spirit and qi. After refinement, it can bend or straighten, soften or harden, do good or evil, be round or square. When the heart conceives a thought or the mind directs an intention, it already knows human intent and flies into action, slaying and cutting in a flash of lightning—this is the natural spirit-sword. If a cultivator of the elixir lacks this sword, it is like seeking fish and rabbits without a trap or snare. The immortal elder alludes to Ouye’s sword-casting to speak of it, yet in truth it is the intangible image of the dark pearl. The intangible image is the celestial mechanism, the secret formula.

**Exegesis:**
The forged and cast sword is used where it ought to be used; the natural sword is the spirit of the returning elixir, the transformation of returning to essence—just as Ouye’s cast sword possesses numinous power.

**Fifty-Three**
Strike bamboo to summon lead, swallow jade mushrooms;
Beat the zither to call the phoenix, drink the knife’s edge.
Lately, golden light shines through the body,
Yet one speaks not of this to ordinary people.

**Annotation:**
This speaks of the work of firing the elixir. Bamboo is hollow-hearted and without emotion; striking means two things colliding. Playing the zither signifies the harmony of husband and wife. Lead is lead; the phoenix is mercury.
