The *daogui* is the vessel of the yin tally; the jade mushroom is the qi of yang fire. The dragon’s refined qi is called jade mushroom; the tiger’s refined qi is called *daogui*. This speaks of dragon and tiger striking each other to unite as husband and wife, harmonious as the sound of the zither. The phoenix is the Vermilion Bird of the South; lead is the Dark Warrior of the North. This is also the image of Kan and Li intermingling to refine the golden elixir. At that moment, gather and ingest it, returning it to the cinnabar field within the earthen crucible. There, subdue one’s own yin mercury. Then, with an empty heart, harmonize the affection of husband and wife, conjoining yin and yang to move the tally fire. Follow the hexagrams and lines, matching breath with spirit and qi. Use spirit and qi to guide water and fire; with water and fire, refine the embryo breath. The embryo breath roams and chants as Kan and Li intermingle within the central palace of the earthen crucible. Nourish lead and mercury, which day and night consume the qi of the tally fire, thereby generating the substance of golden liquid—this is the golden liquid returning elixir.

**Exegesis:**
According to the *Yi Zhen Lun*: When moving the fire, one may feel something at the coccyx surging straight up through the spine, passing the double gates with a distinct sound, ascending to the mud pill, then descending from the mud pill to strike the upper palate. Droplet by droplet, it enters the mouth, resembling sparrow’s eggs, tasting like frozen butter—fragrant, sweet, soft, and delightful. When this occurs, it is the golden liquid returning elixir. Swallow it slowly into the cinnabar field. If this happens continuously without cease, the five viscera become clear and empty. Closing the eyes to inwardly observe, the organs appear as if illuminated by candlelight. Gradually, myriad golden rays shine brilliantly, radiating from the body like a wheel of fire, clouds and mist swirling around it. Step by step, sacred signs manifest in succession, verifying the transcendence from the ordinary to the sagely—this is no mere metaphor but the true vision. The immortal elder silently bore this marvel, daring not speak of it to others, for it is not a matter seen or heard in the human realm.

**Fifty-Four**
When medicine meets qi and tally, only then does form arise;
The Dao abides in emptiness, uniting with spontaneity.
A single grain of golden elixir swallowed into the belly—
Only then do I know my words do not depend on heaven.

**Annotation:**
There is a thing formlessly formed, born before heaven and earth. The sage thus forcibly names it the Dao, forcibly names it the primordial chaos of the true unity of qi. Invisible when looked upon, inaudible when listened to, unattainable when grasped. The sage, in resonance with the tally of the two eights’ initial qi, communicates and penetrates, descending numinous power to form an image within the empty mystery. A single grain, like a millet seed, ingested into the belly instantly dries the mercury, transforming it into a body of pure yang, enduring as long as heaven and earth. Chaoyuanzi said: “Life and death exhaust the Dao, which depends on heaven and earth; nature and destiny originally belong to mercury and lead. This is not my destiny; it is in me and does not depend on heaven.”

**Fifty-Five**
The radiant red golden elixir forms in a single day—
Ancient immortals’ words are truly worth heeding.
Those who speak of nine years or three years
Are merely delaying and prolonging the allotted time.

**Annotation:**
For the great medicine of the golden elixir, the work of the lower furnace takes no more than half an hour to immediately obtain and ingest. This speaks of “a single day” because the sage condenses a year’s qi into a month, a month’s qi into a day, and a day’s qi into an hour. Generally speaking, this is called “attaining immortality in a single day.” Thus, the immortal elder said: “Exchanging days for hours is the method of divine work.” Once the golden elixir enters the mouth, one immediately ascends to the sacred realm—such swift and clear verification! How could it be a matter of three years or nine years, protracting time and delaying the schedule? The ancient immortal Zhang Guolao wrote:
*The radiant red golden elixir forms in a single day;
The yellow sprout does not leave the cinnabar mine.
Though the work is not yet thrice completed,
Upon opening the furnace, one already sees the radiant light.*
This is the Dao.

**Fifty-Six**
The great Dao’s cultivation may be easy or difficult—
It depends on me, or it depends on heaven.
If one does not accumulate deeds and bestow yin virtue,
Then myriad demons will arise to obstruct the path.

**Annotation:**
Demonic obstructions lie in heaven; cultivation lies in me. Without bestowing yin virtue, obstacles arise at every turn.

**Exegesis:**
The previous poem said: “A single grain of golden elixir swallowed into the belly—only then do I know it depends on me, not on heaven,” greatly praising the efficacy of the golden elixir as most numinous and divine. This poem now says: “It depends on me, or it depends on heaven,” exhorting learners that upon hearing the great Dao, they should accumulate deeds and bestow virtue to seek heavenly assistance. One must not rely solely on the elixir’s numinosity, for there will surely be demonic obstructions to hinder progress.

**Fifty-Seven**
The Three Powers mutually steal and consume in their time—
This is the mechanism of immortals’ Dao and virtue.
When the myriad transformations are at peace, all concerns cease;
The hundred bones are all ordered, verifying non-action.

**Annotation:**
Heaven and earth steal from the myriad things through the four seasons, thus there is flourishing and withering, yet they cannot remain forever flourishing. The myriad things steal from humans through the five flavors, thus there is life and death, yet they cannot remain forever living. Humans steal from the myriad things through the five phases, thus there is completion and decay, yet they cannot remain forever enduring. When the three stealings are fitting, the Three Powers are at peace. Therefore, there is life and death, prosperity and decline, flourishing and fading, day and night, coming and going, birth and killing, rise and fall, things and self, right and wrong—all arising in profusion, cycling endlessly and unfathomably. This is the natural Dao. If one can blend these three stealings into one, reverse their mechanism and act, seize the right time to consume, then the hundred bones will all be ordered, and the myriad transformations will naturally be at peace. When the myriad transformations are at peace, all concerns cease, and the Dao of non-action is naturally verified.

**Fifty-Eight**
The precious characters of the *Yin Fu* exceed three hundred;
The numinous scripture of the *Dao De* stops at five thousand.
Immortals of past and present, without limit in number,
All from this pass through to reach the true transmission.

**Annotation:**
The two scriptures serve as the governing key of all classics and the pivotal hub of the various masters. Immortals and sagely beings of old have, without exception, awakened to the true transmission through these two scriptures and thereby attained the great Dao.

**Fifty-Nine**
Though your wisdom surpasses Yan and Min,
Without a master’s transmission, do not force conjecture.
For the alchemical classics lack oral instructions—
How can you forge the spiritual embryo without guidance?

**Annotation:**
Amidst a thousand classics and ten thousand discourses, only the branches are expounded; the supreme Dao is not complex. It is solely transmitted through the mind-seal. Without encountering a true master, all efforts are in vain. This Dao cannot be forcibly deduced, even by one as wise as Yan or Min.

**Sixty**
When the restless mind-monkey is stilled and the square-inch mechanism tamed,
Three thousand merits align with heaven’s measure.
Naturally, the cauldron refines dragon and tiger—
Yet how can one bear the clinging to home, wife, and child?

**Annotation:**
This verse admonishes those of the present age who fail to turn back. The "square-inch mechanism" refers to the mind of the cultivator, which, before the elixir is refined, must be utterly lucid, unshaken by the restless mind-monkey or galloping intent-horse. As an ancient song says: *"Man’s nature is originally a monkey— / Myriad distractions arise from outward wandering. / If you can subdue and gather the six essences, / The luminous pearl will coalesce by night."*

Master Lü states: *"Before refining the returning elixir, first refine the mind."* The *Western Mountain Record* says: *"True immortals and sagely beings teach people to cultivate the Dao by cultivating the mind, / And to cultivate the mind by cultivating the Dao."* Further: *"Restrain it, and it is upright; / Release it, and it runs wild. / From clarity, the Dao arises; / From turbidity, the spirit is lost."* This is the essential barrier.

The so-called "merits" are the interplay of yin and yang. The Immortal Elder says: *"The great medicine is cultivated with ease or difficulty— / Know that it depends on me, / Not on heaven. / Without accumulated merits and deeds, / Hordes of demons will obstruct the path."*

Master Zhongli Quan says: *"Merits without conduct are like feet missing; / Conduct without merits is like the sun halting. / When merits and conduct are both complete, / The feet are prepared—who says one cannot become an immortal?"* Master Lü says: *"The road to Penglai requires three thousand merits fulfilled— / Then one strides alone into the clouds to return."* When hidden virtues are accumulated, one inevitably encounters a perfected being. Thus it is said: *"Naturally, there is a cauldron to refine dragon and tiger."*

As for "clinging to wife and child," the Immortal Elder’s intent is to caution scholars against straying from the true Dao into deviant practices. To cling to wife and child is to sink forever in the sea of suffering. The scholar must nurture aspirations beyond the mundane.

**Sixty-One**
If you have not yet refined the Returned Elixir, refine it with urgency;
Once refined, you must know when to stop and be content.
Should you cling to fullness without ceasing,
Disgrace and misfortune will one day befall you.

**Annotation says:**
A man’s *tiankui* arrives at sixteen and is exhausted by sixty-four.
When it first arrives, it is full and pure, weighing one catty.
By the time he reaches his prime, one *liang* of mercury has fled;
By thirty, four *liang* have gone;
By sixty, the bed is stripped to the frame—
At sixty-four, the number is complete, the pure *kun* transmission spent.
When crow flies and hare runs, time waits for no man.
Living mercury must borrow lead to capture;
The Returned Elixir must be refined without delay.
Once refined, embrace the One and guard sincerity.
If you do not know contentment, clinging to what is not yours,
You will suffer disgrace and misfortune.

Zhongli Quan says:
When the Elixir is ripe, do not apply further firing;
To continue firing will harm the Elixir.
It is best to preserve and guard it without loss.
Drink when thirsty, eat when hungry, sleep when weary.
If you can further clarify the mind and perceive your nature,
Facing the wall for nine years,
This Dao will grow ever more profound.

**Commentary says:**
Lü Chunyang was sixty-four when he met Zhengyang;
Ge the Immortal was sixty-four when he met Master Zheng;
Ma Ziran was sixty-four when he met Haichan—
All were then cultivating the Golden Elixir’s Way and attained immortality.
Once refined, know contentment:
After ten months of gestation, one should bathe,
And within a year, all will be complete—
No need to wait for the winter solstice to cease work.
*The Four Hundred Words on the Golden Elixir* says:
*"The firing times are not fixed;
The winter solstice is not at midnight.
When it is time to bathe,
Even the hours of mao and you are empty."*
Shi Xinglin says:
*"The winter solstice is not at midnight;
Bathing is not at mao and you."*
Dao Guang says:
*"After shedding the embryo and bathing,
Carry and nurture it to secure long life."*
All three immortals attained the Dao at sixty-four—
What was the Way they cultivated?
May we hear its outline?

**I reply:**
All three immortals, in their prime, aspired to the Dao, upheld precepts, and accumulated talismans.
Only at sixty-four did they receive the true transmission of the Golden Elixir,
Thus attaining the Dao swiftly.
As for worldly men, lust and desire deplete essence;
Anxious thoughts harm the spirit;
Fatigue and toil exhaust *qi*.
Once true yang is lost,
Even if they hear of the Great Dao before sixty-four,
Success will be difficult.
If one can sever desire in youth,
Seek the Dao in one’s prime,
While the body is yet unspoiled and essence undiminished,
And meet a master to receive guidance and begin swift cultivation—
If no master is met, do not dissipate your essence or weary your form.
Accumulate merit and pile up conduct,
Awaiting the encounter.
Then, perhaps, you may hope for the Dao attained by the three immortals.
Their Way is recorded in the classics—its threads may be traced.

Zhengyang showed Chunyang a few grains of Elixir, saying:
*"This is not the five metals or eight stones of the world,
But a wondrous treasure compounded from the world’s rarities.
Though it has substance, it is formless—
Like clouds, like fire, like light, like shadow,
Visible yet intangible.
When consumed, it unites with a person’s soul and consciousness,
Becoming one body—light, empty, and wondrous,
Not an Elixir of tangible form."*

Ge the Immortal’s *"Song of the Flowing Pearl"* says:
*"Flowing Pearl, Flowing Pearl,
You make me toil endlessly,
Wandering the four seas,
Traversing ten thousand books.
Anxious, I forget sleep and meals,
Visiting all my learned friends,
Burning cinnabar and mercury for thirty years,
Sighing daily.
Now at sixty, I grieve over descending the Three Paths.
Fortunately, my master transmitted the primordial *qi* of emptiness and non-being.
First stabilize the golden tripod,
Then secure the jade furnace.
Stir the *li* fire to arouse the *kan* fire.
When the jade liquid moistens the chamber,
The flowing tassels of the Grotto Palace—
The true man’s teaching—
A man of true resolve must keep this in mind.
Remember, remember!"*

Ma Ziran’s *"Song of the Golden Elixir"* says:
*"The sixty-four hexagrams all say ‘cease.’
I met Haichan as my disciple,
Who then told me a single phrase—
All my past efforts were in vain.
It turns out this alone is the Returned Elixir,
Right before my eyes, yet I did not recognize it.
In the year *gengzi*, the month *wuyin*,
I met a perfected being who imparted the oral formula—
Like jade in stone, uncarved.
When carved, it was white as snow,
Within it the Returned Elixir, two times eight *liang*,
Born in the cinnabar field.
If the yellow sprout is obtained and planted in the cinnabar field,
Lifespan will be boundless, beyond reckoning."*

This is the Dao attained by the three immortals,
In accord with the same ultimate principle as the *Wuzhen Pian*.
The Purple Mystery Zhang Zhenren lived to ninety-six.
In the fifth year of *Yuanfeng* (*renxu*), on the fifth day of the third month,
He departed through *shijie*.
From the second year of *Xining* (*jiyou*), when he met his master in Chengdu and received the Dao,
The Zhenren was already eighty-two.
His cultivation occurred after sixty-four—
His preservation and nurturing in ordinary times bore deep merit.

*The Yellow Court Classic* says:
*"At one hundred and twenty, one may still return,
But beyond this, guarding the Dao is most difficult.
Only by relying on the ninefold refined Eight Precious Elixir,
Replenishing essence and contemplating the Seven Origins,
Can this be achieved."*

---

**Sixty-Two**
Simply take the door of death as the door of life;
Do not cling to the gate of life as the gate of death.
If you recognize the turning point and act with insight,
You will see that harm conceals life, and kindness arises.

**Annotation says:**
Yin and yang, the five phases—
Following them brings life; reversing them brings death.
This is the common Way.
Yet who knows there is a life that is not life—
Thus long life?
A compliance that is not compliance—
Thus ultimate compliance?
If you can understand this turning point,
Then harm conceals life, and kindness arises,
And a man may conceive—
This is no lie.
The killing mechanism is the mechanism of theft.

**Commentary says:**
What gives me life is yin and yang, the five phases;
What brings me death is also yin and yang, the five phases.
Taking the door of death as the door of life
Is the ability to reverse the killing mechanism.
If you lightly employ life and follow the common Way,
What gives you life will kill you.
Ordinary people follow yin and yang, the five phases—
Thus death comes.
The perfected reverse yin and yang—
Thus they live.
The immortal steals the mechanism,
Shedding the illusory body.
People see them as dead—
This is not death.
The pure yang true body soars and transforms,
Coextensive with heaven and earth, enduring forever.
Thus, the life that is not life is long life.
Inverting the five phases, reversing creation—
This is non-compliance.
Seizing the essence of heaven and earth,
Returning it to the limitless—
This is compliance.
Thus, the compliance that is not compliance is ultimate compliance.

---

**Sixty-Three**
Fortune and misfortune arise mutually, each leaning on the other,
Like echoes and shadows following one another.
If you can turn this mechanism of life and death,
Disaster becomes blessing in the space between your palms.

**Annotation says:**
Yang governs life and is called fortune;
Yin governs killing and is called misfortune.
When yin wanes, yang waxes;
When yang reaches its peak, yin arises—
Mutually leaning, like echoes and shadows following.
This is the natural principle of the common Way.
If you can follow this mechanism of killing and life in cultivation,
Then disaster becomes blessing in the space between your palms,
And harm conceals life, a man conceives—
This is no lie.

---

**Sixty-Four**
In cultivation, mingle with the world and harmonize your light;
Be round when round is needed, square when square is needed.
Display or conceal as others require—
Let none discern your actions or concealments.

**Annotation says:**
"Clad in coarse cloth yet holding jade within, harmonizing one’s light and merging with the dust, mending the broken fence—
No self, no others, in seclusion or in the open, in accord or in opposition,
How could ordinary folk fathom or measure this?"

**Twelve *Xijiangyue* [Moon Over the West River] (Composed According to the Twelve Months’ Rhythm)**
**[The Immortal Elder’s self-annotation: "West" is the direction of metal; "river" is the body of water; "moon" is the function of the elixir. Wumingzi’s annotation: The Immortal Elder composed this suite to the rhythm of the twelve months to reveal the Great Dao.]**

The inner elixir is akin to the outer elixir,
Inner and outer must both be open and flowing.
The cinnabar head blends and unites—
Their warmth and nurturing serve twofold functions.

Within resides the celestial true fire,
In the crucible, blazing and ever-red.
The outer furnace demands diligent effort in increase and decrease—
Nothing surpasses the wondrous true seed.

**Annotation says:**
The *Pomi Song* of Yimen states:
"The Dao arises within—set up the furnace and tripod without.
The Dao arises without—Kan and Li, lead and mercury lie within."
This clarifies the two elixirs, inner and outer.

Now, the outer elixir is the Golden Elixir,
Wrought in the crucible of the two eights,
Achieved in less than half an hour.
The inner elixir is the Golden Liquor Returning Elixir,
Wrought within one’s own belly,
Requiring ten full months to complete the transformation and transcend the womb.

Observe these two elixirs: though their methods of blending the cinnabar head and their operations may seem roughly alike,
Their workings in fire and timing differ vastly in speed.
When the cultivator begins the work, at the moment the inner elixir blends with the cinnabar head,
Even the slightest deviation will prevent the Great Elixir from forming.
Take heed! Take heed!

Though the inner elixir possesses true fire within the earthen cauldron, blazing and ever-red,
It must rely on the outer furnace’s effort in increase, decrease, withdrawal, and addition,
Lest miscalculation lead to peril.
Yet the endless transformations of inner and outer true fire truly depend on the marvel of true lead—
This substance alone can capture mercury and prevent its flight.

Ye Wenshu, failing to grasp this principle, claimed:
"The inner elixir is refined by true fire,
While the outer elixir requires mundane fire’s increase and decrease."
Such a view, like peering at the sky through a tube, merits but a laugh.
Little does he know that though the two elixirs differ, their essence is one Dao.

The so-called inner and outer elixirs:
Within a single body, one is endowed with the essence of Heaven and Earth,
Born and shaped through the molding of yin and yang.
Thus, within this body, essence, qi, and spirit are sovereign.
Spirit is born of qi, qi of essence—
These three are postcelestial, the most yin substances of Heaven and Earth.

If the cultivator clings to the body alone in practice,
The utmost they can achieve is refining these three—essence, qi, and spirit.
Yet how can these three, being of one nature, entirely postcelestial, purely yin and devoid of yang,
Transform the form into pure yang and emerge beyond Heaven and Earth?

Thus the Immortal Elder said:
"Cultivating a single substance only leads to frailty."
Master Zhongli stated:
"Tears, saliva, semen, fluids, qi, blood, and humor—these seven are all yin."
He also said:
"Cultivating a single substance is solitary yin."
Zhenyizi said:
"Solitary yin cannot generate; solitary yang cannot complete."
The *Cantong Qi* states:
"A hen hatching her chicks cannot succeed."
The sage knows that one’s true qi, being postcelestial, yin in nature, is hard to capture and easy to lose.
Thus, one gathers the precelestial One Qi—true yin and true yang, the substances of the two eights united—
Capturing them within a single hour,
Refining them into a grain of utmost yang elixir, called true lead.
This is wrought externally, hence called the outer elixir.
With this yang elixir, one restrains one’s yin mercury,
Like a cat seizing a rat.
The yang elixir is the mother qi of Heaven and Earth;
One’s mercury is the child qi of Heaven and Earth.
When mother qi subdues child qi, is this not union?

This is wrought internally, hence called the inner elixir.
Thus the Immortal Elder said:
"When the elixir meets the qi’s union, it takes form;
The Dao resides in emptiness, merging with nature."

Zhenyizi said:
"Before Heaven and Earth existed in chaos, true lead, attaining the One, was born first,
Gradually giving rise to Heaven and Earth, yin and yang, the Five Phases, and the myriad things."
The *Cantong Qi* states:
"Born before Heaven and Earth, majestic and exalted."
All these attest to the precelestial One Qi.

With the precelestial yang elixir restraining one’s yin mercury, transforming it into pure yang,
And further employing the fire of yin-yang symbols, applying withdrawal and addition,
After ten months of work, the form transforms into qi, qi into spirit,
Spirit merges with the Dao, becoming formless—
Its transformations unfathomable.
Thus one emerges beyond Heaven and Earth,
Stands beyond the bounds of creation,
Grasps Heaven and Earth, molds yin and yang,
Yet is not molded by yin and yang.
This is the work of the precelestial One Qi—
Such is its marvel.

Hence it is said:
"Nothing surpasses the wondrous true seed."
How could one take the postcelestial, most yin qi-union as the inner elixir?
How could one take postcelestial, mundane cinnabar, mundane mercury, or impure, non-union substances as the outer elixir?

Scholars of the Dao, delve into the root and origin,
Lest you be misled by heterodox teachings and forever fall into the self-inflicted cycle of rebirth.

**Commentary says:**
Even the slightest deviation will prevent the Great Elixir from forming—
As the quatrain says: "A hair’s breadth off, and the elixir fails."
The "two eights" are not a furnace but a metaphor for the furnace.
The furnace is no furnace—such is the furnace.

The outer elixir is congealed into golden cinnabar through the fire of yin-yang ascent and descent; the inner elixir is likewise congealed into the golden liquid reverted cinnabar through the fire of yin-yang ascent and descent. Externally, it is nurtured through symbolic correspondence; internally, it is nurtured through symbolic correspondence. Thus it is said: though the inner elixir differs, its essence is one and the same Dao.

How well put by the Tang immortal in *Attaining the Numinous*:
"People know longevity lies in reverting essence and replenishing qi,
Yet where is cinnabar to be found outside the self?"
This is truly vulgar talk, ignorant of the true realm.
But let me ask: can essence be reverted? Can qi be replenished?
Regulating breath, manipulating the mechanism, exhaling and inhaling—
Is this truly an outward emission and inward absorption?
Where does the return of one’s nature come from, and where does it enter?
Some take exhalation and inhalation as the essence’s flower—
Yet how does this cause the coldness of a broken waist?
Some take the ebb and flow of breath as essence and qi—
Yet how does this lead to the exhaustion of skin and labor?
At the age when one should be in full vigor, one becomes a vessel of decline and decay.
Once the flower of essence is lost, the spirit and soul scatter in four directions—
What then is there to revert?
Those who guard the true qi, long practicing movement to extend their years,
Are but lower-grade earthbound immortals,
Devoid of the power to ascend the void.
Only when one externally refines the fire dragon and internally circulates the golden liquid
Does one truly ascend to the ranks of the loftiest immortals.
Judging by the words of these high immortals,
Cultivating a single element alone will never lead to transcendence.
Now the words are clear, distinguishing inner and outer elixirs,
Yet people still fail to awaken—
Alas, how profoundly distant they are from the Way!

**Second Stanza**
This elixir is most divine, most sagely—
Yet I fear your allotted share is meager and hard to digest.
Harmonizing lead and mercury, the work is not finished by dawn,
But early you shall behold the form of the mysterious pearl.
If a man of resolve can cultivate this,
Why should he not dwell in the marketplace or serve at court?
The practice is easy, the medicine not far—
Yet once revealed, people cannot help but laugh.

**Annotation says:**
Once the golden elixir enters the mouth, one instantly ascends to sagehood—
Is this not the work of the most divine and sagely?
Forged and refined in less than half an hour, the golden elixir’s form appears—
Is this not the simplest and easiest?
Found in every household, unbound by marketplace or court—
Is this not the nearest?
Only because it is most divine, most sagely, most simple, most easy, and most near
Do people, upon hearing it explained, unconsciously laugh.
Those who attain it need only fear their karmic virtue is too shallow to bear the Way—
Scholars, take heed!

**Commentary says:**
The true one’s intent is that the refinement of the golden elixir
Need not be confined to mountains or secluded places—
It can be done amidst the marketplace or the imperial court.
The practice is very easy, the medicine very near.
As long as one finds a place of purity, it can be accomplished.
Thus the poem says:
"Before refining the reverted cinnabar, do not flee to the mountains—
To dwell alone in the deep mountains is futile."
This is because worldly scholars, not understanding the root,
Strive for profit in the marketplace and fame at court,
Yet can still proceed with the work—
Just as one with ten thousand strings of cash can ride a saddle to Shu.
But one must first sever attachment to fame and profit,
Extinguish all cravings,
And enter seclusion for ten months—
Only then can one hope to attain the true.

**Third Stanza**
The White Tiger’s first classic is the supreme treasure;
The Flower Pool’s divine water is true gold.
Thus we know the source of the highest good runs deep—
It is not to be compared with ordinary medicinal substances.
If you wish to refine the nine revolutions,
First refine the self and hold the mind steady.
Follow the seasons in gathering, discerning floating and sinking,
And in advancing the fire, guard against peril.

**Annotation says:**
"First" means the beginning.
The "first classic" refers to the initial menstruation—
Not the celestial water of women.

Do not slander the sacred Dao with the three peaks and twenty-four grades—
The sacred Dao cannot be defiled,
Just as one cannot ascend to heaven by climbing steps.

The true One’s essence:
In heaven, it is called the true One’s water;
In the tiger, it is called the first menstruum’s essence.
Refined in the Flower Pool’s divine water,
This is the supreme treasure, true gold—
All inseparable from the true One’s essence,
Flowing through the myriad barriers under various names.
The *Classic* says, "The highest good is like water,"
For the true One’s water arises before heaven and earth,
Thus called the highest good.
Its source of benefit runs deep and far,
Unlike ordinary post-heaven impure substances.

Nine revolutions are nine years.
After the ten-month embryo is complete and the birth is achieved,
Bodhidharma faced the wall for nine years,
Returning west with a single sandal—
There is indeed a reason for this.
Yet to refine the nine revolutions,
First circulate the fire for ten months,
Gather in accordance with the seasons,
Discern floating and sinking,
Distinguish host and guest,
Guard the feminine without asserting the masculine—
Only then can peril be avoided.
Naturally, form transforms into qi,
Qi transforms into spirit.
Embracing the origin and guarding the One,
After nine years, the work is complete:
Form and spirit are both wondrous,
Merging with the Dao in truth.
The sage forcibly names it the nine-revolution golden liquid,
The great return.

**Fourth Stanza**
If you wish to retain true lead and embrace mercury,
Within the household, do not part from the minister.
Wood and metal are separated—
How can they meet without cause?
You must employ a matchmaker to summon them.
Wood’s nature loves metal’s righteousness,
Metal’s sentiment loves wood’s benevolence.
They swallow and devour each other,
Only then do they become intimate.
Only then does the man realize he is with child.

**Annotation says:**
This speaks of the inner image.
The "household minister" is one’s true qi.
One’s true qi congeals because of the golden elixir,
And the golden elixir’s divine efficacy arises from one’s mercury.
The two substances depend on each other,
Their natures yearning for one another,
Thus enabling transformation and spiritual communion.
Hence it is said, "If you wish to retain true lead and embrace mercury,
Within the household, do not part from the minister."
The elixir pertains to metal and is external,
While one’s mercury pertains to wood and is internal.
The two are separated,
Relying entirely on the Yellow Dame to refine and form the elixir.
Once swallowed into the abdomen,
It unites with one’s mercury—
Again, the Yellow Dame summons them.
The two having harmonized and joined,
Yin and yang align with the fire.
Wood’s nature yearns for metal,
Metal’s sentiment yearns for wood.
They swallow and devour each other,
Uniting as husband and wife,
Nurturing the infant within the abdomen.
Only then does the man realize he is with child.
This Dao is most profound and wondrous—
Without benevolence toward all things
And the accumulation of hidden merits,
How could one attain this in this lifetime?

**Fifth Stanza**
Who is the sixteen-year-old maiden of no family?
Who is the twenty-seven-year-old gentleman who calls himself so?
When wood liquid meets metal essence,
The seven directions enable the three natures.
Then, borrowing Ding Gong’s refining,
Husband and wife begin their joyful union.
The river chariot dares not pause—
It transports them straight to Kunlun’s peak.

**Annotation says:**
Sixteen is the yin number;
The "maiden" is one’s true qi.
It is also called "wood liquid."
Twenty-seven is the yang number;
The "gentleman" is one’s yang elixir.
It is also called "metal essence."
When the two merge in the cinnabar field’s earth cauldron,
They form the three sacrifices.
"Ding Gong" is fire;
"Husband and wife" are lead and mercury,
Joined in the cinnabar field’s earth cauldron.
Daily, they unite in the joyful fire of conjugal love,
Refined in the earth cauldron.
Lead and mercury receive this sign,
Generating the substance of golden liquid.
From the tailbone, it ascends straight to the peak of Mud Pill,
Descending into the mouth,
Slowly swallowed back into the cinnabar field’s earth cauldron.
Thus it circulates endlessly,
Like the river chariot’s ceaseless flow,
Transforming into the golden liquid returning elixir.
Master Zhongli said:
"From the tailbone straight up to the peak of Mud Pill,
The river chariot flows freely hundreds of times."
Master Haichan said:
"If yellow sprouts fill the brain’s blood,
Even after ten thousand years, though old, the body does not die."
This is the evidence.

**Commentary says:**
The *Cantong Qi* states:
"Three things, one household, all return to wu and si.
Take metal, wood, and fire as the three things."
It also says:
"When the three natures merge,
They share the same ancestral origin.
Take metal, wood, and fire as the three natures."
All refer to the external medicine’s symbolic method.
Here, speaking of the three positions,
Wood liquid is the internal medicine,
Metal essence is the external medicine.
When they meet earth, the three natures are complete—
This refers to the symbolic method of internal and external.
Thus, the three natures each follow their use.
Those who err take it as "three surnames,"
Which is even more absurd.
For "nature" is the nature of things,
The nature of humans,
The nature of the elixir,
The nature of the five phases—
How could it be a surname?
A verse says:
"Fire arises from Kunlun,
Yin and yang combine within and without."
Kunlun is also called:
"If you encounter Kunlun, go northwest"—
Referring solely to the inner northwest,
The palace of Qian’s trigram where yin and yang interact.
Here, Kunlun specifically denotes Mud Pill.
Thus, the repeated metaphors in the "Three Natures" and "Kunlun" chapters
Cannot be rigidly adhered to.

**Sixth Stanza**
Seven returns of cinnabar,
Nine returns of golden liquid—
Return to the origin, return to truth.
Do not count the hours of yin and yang,
But observe the five phases’ completion as the standard.
It is but a single taste of mercury,
Circulating through all the celestial stems.
When yin and yang’s numbers are complete,
It naturally communicates with the spirit,
Entering and exiting without leaving the mysterious female.

**Annotation on the Nine Returns and Seven Reversions**
The nine returns and seven reversions do not depart from the generative and completive numbers of Heaven and Earth’s five phases. Heaven’s one generates water, and Earth’s six completes it—water resides in the north, accumulating the qi of Kan’s trigram as true water. Thus, the *Cantong Qi* states: "Six resides [in the north]." Earth’s two generates fire, and Heaven’s seven completes it—fire returns to the south, nurturing the qi of Li’s trigram to produce cinnabar. Hence, "seven reversions: cinnabar returns to its origin." Heaven’s three generates wood, and Earth’s eight completes it—wood resides in the east, guarding the position of Zhen to form mercury. Thus, the *Cantong Qi* states: "Eight returns." Earth’s four generates metal, and Heaven’s nine completes it—metal returns to the west, governing the position of Dui to become gold. Hence, "nine returns: golden liquid returns to truth." Heaven’s five generates earth, and Earth’s ten completes it—two earths unite and dwell in the center, guarding the four images to form the elixir. Thus, the golden elixir is not produced outside the five phases, and so it is said: "Observe only the completion of the five phases as the standard." How can the hours of yin and yang—from *yin* to *shen*—be taken as the seven reversions and nine returns?

Mercury is lead. Lead is the qi of true unity. When the qi of true unity congeals, it forms essence, called the essence of true unity—this is lead essence. The qi of true unity transforms once into water in the north, twice into cinnabar in the south, thrice into mercury in the east, four times into gold in the west, and five times into earth in the center. Thus, the golden elixir is not born without Heaven and Earth, not produced without the sun and moon, not perfected without the four seasons, not accomplished without the five phases, and not completed without the total number. Therefore, circulating through all the celestial stems, when the numbers of yin and yang are complete, it naturally communicates with the spirit and transforms. Yet its wondrous workings of entry and exit never depart from the gate of the Mysterious Female—this is called the root of Heaven and Earth. The principle of the Mysterious Female has already been expounded in *The Gate of the Mysterious Female*, though few in the world understand its annotation.

**Exegesis**
The common view that from *yin* to *shen* constitutes the seven reversions, and from *zi* to *kun* the nine returns, is mistaken. Zhang Ziyang’s annotation of the *Cantong Qi* states: "Water, fire, metal, wood, and earth are the five phases. Water and fire are the sun and moon; metal and wood are the dragon and tiger. Earth corresponds to Heaven and Earth. When refined, they form the golden elixir." Thus, Heaven’s water, six, resides in the north, accumulating Kan as water; Heaven’s wood, eight, resides in the east, guarding Zhen to become cinnabar; Heaven’s fire, seven, returns to the south, belonging to Li as mercury; Heaven’s metal, nine, returns to the west, transforming Dui into gold; Heaven’s earth, five, returns to the center to form the elixir. The qi transforms once into water, twice into cinnabar, thrice into mercury, four times into gold, and five times into the elixir. From this, we know that the elixir is not born without Heaven and Earth, not perfected without the sun and moon, not completed without the four seasons, and not accomplished without the five phases. Refining the body of pure yang into the form of true gold, the meanings of "six resides," "seven reversions," "eight returns," and "nine returns" can then be discerned. This is why the Yellow Emperor, Laozi, the divine immortals, and the sages prized it. Master Wuming’s annotation clarifies the original text: "These celestial stems" refer to the positions of the seventy-two stems, which embody the meaning of the seven reversions and nine returns.

**Seventh Stanza**
Within the male lies the female’s essence,
True yin yet embraces yang’s essence.
When the two harmonize, the medicine is formed—
Transforming the soul and spirit, the sage is realized.
Trust in the golden elixir’s single grain:
A serpent’s swallow transfigures into dragon’s form,
A fowl’s feast becomes the phoenix’s flight,
Soaring into the sacred realm of true yang.

**Annotation**
The male’s inner female is the dragon’s *qi*—mercury. The yin embracing yang is the tiger’s *qi*—lead. When these two substances unite, the numinous elixir is spontaneously born. Swallowed into the abdomen, it transforms the yang soul to dissolve the yin spirit. A single grain, like a millet seed, when a chicken devours a serpent or swallows it whole, becomes a dragon or phoenix, ascending into the sacred realm of true yang. How divine is the medicine’s sanctity!

**Eighth Stanza**
As Heaven and Earth pass through closure and union,
Dawn and dusk must recognize the wheels’ convergence.
Like waters flowing to the sea, the mystery lies in withdrawal and addition.
Attain the One, and ten thousand affairs are complete—
Discern south and north, east and west,
Diminish and diminish again, guarding past merit.
The life-treasure must not be lightly handled.

**Annotation**
The method of firing the elixir begins with effort at *Zhun* and ends with rest at *Pi-Tai*. Day and night, one moves the fire talismans into the crucible, like a wheel’s spokes converging at the hub, or the hundred rivers flowing to the sea. Such is the wondrous work of withdrawal and addition.

The *Daode Jing* states: "Attain the One, and ten thousand affairs are complete." How profound is this saying! The One is the essence of true unity. The qi of true unity generates yin and yang; yin and yang generate the four images; the four images generate the five phases; the five phases generate the myriad things—all do not depart from the transformations of the qi of true unity. Thus, the essence of true unity is the mother of Heaven and Earth, the ancestor of yin and yang, the root of the four images, the foundation of the five phases, and the basis of the myriad things. Attaining this One, the ten thousand affairs are complete. East, west, south, and north may all be forgotten. Diminish and diminish again, guarding past merit, to fully grasp the One’s mystery. For the One has form: it is shaped by the firing of yin and yang’s two fires. Once a single grain is swallowed into the five viscera, as before, one must cautiously apply the yin and yang fire talismans to fully return to the One’s mystery. Beware of peril and danger—do not act lightly, lest the life-treasure’s mysterious pearl be lost. Thus, it is said: "Guard past merit."

**Exegesis**
Effort begins at *Zhun-Meng*, employing the sixty-four hexagrams in a month. Rest concludes at *Pi-Tai*, with bathing at the second and eighth months—this is the inner medicine’s symbolic method. Attaining the One is the outer medicine’s symbolic method. Lü Dongbin’s song states: "The Three Mao Lords are called the One." The *Daode Jing* speaks of "diminishing": now, in the tenth month of practice, one diminishes affairs and extinguishes thoughts, guarding against danger and peril. Not a single hair’s weight of the mind should be attached, lest the life-treasure be lost, like an infant in the womb. Forgetting the self’s existence within the Heaven and Earth crucible, one can perpetually maintain clarity. Heaven and Earth are wholly subsumed, and thus the perfected person repeatedly exhorts: "Diminish and diminish again, guarding past merit."

**Ninth Stanza**
At winter solstice, the first yang returns—
Three decades add one yang line.
In the moon’s mid-reversal, the *Fu* hexagram appears;
From dawn to dusk, cease *Qian* and *Gou*’s signs.
Days alternate in cold and heat—
Yang revives at *Fu*, rising at midnight;
*Gou*’s image at noon, a single yin dawns.
In refining the medicine, know the twilight’s hour.

**Annotation**
The winter solstice gives birth to the first yang, forming the *Fu* hexagram—this is its single yang line. After thirty days, it becomes the *Lin* hexagram, adding a second yang line. After another thirty days, it becomes the *Tai* hexagram, adding a third yang line. After another thirty days, it becomes the *Dazhuang* hexagram, adding a fourth yang line. After another thirty days, it becomes the *Guai* hexagram, adding a fifth yang line. After another thirty days, it becomes the *Qian* hexagram, completing the six yang lines—this is the fullness of the yang fire’s season.

When yang reaches its extreme, yin arises—thus at the summer solstice, the first yin is born, forming the *Gou* hexagram, its single yin line. Just as before, after thirty days, a second yin line is added, forming the *Dun* hexagram; then the *Pi* hexagram; then the *Guan* hexagram; then the *Bo* hexagram; and finally the *Kun* hexagram, completing the six yin lines—this is the fullness of the yin tally’s season. When yin reaches its extreme, yang revives once more, cycling endlessly. These are the great numbers of a year’s qi’s waxing and waning.

The sage transposes this yearly cycle of qi into a single month: the new moon’s dawn is *Fu*, and the full moon is pure yang. Two and a half days correspond to thirty days—this is one month. The full moon is pure *Qian*; by the sixteenth day, *Gou*’s single yin is born. Thus it is said: “At the full moon’s end, *Gou*’s sign appears,” for yin first sprouts as a portent. This is the great number of a month’s qi, the celestial cycle.

The sage further transposes this monthly cycle into a single day, dividing it into the four seasons’ qi of cold, heat, warmth, and coolness. Thus at midnight’s *zi* hour, the first yang is born as the *Fu* hexagram; after noon, the first yin is born as the *Gou* hexagram. In applying the tally fire, the ascent and descent of yin and yang—drawing out, adding, advancing, and retreating—each aligns with heaven and earth’s four seasons and the rise and fall of yin and yang, without the slightest deviation. Thus it is said: “In refining the medicine, know the twilight’s hour.” Twilight is the beginning of yin and yang—this is the great number of a day’s qi, the celestial cycle.

**Commentary:**
A great celestial cycle of one year is the ascent and descent of heaven and earth. Heaven and earth are separated by eighty-four thousand *li*; divided into six nodes, earth’s yin conceals yang. From the summer solstice, the zenith of heaven’s yin qi descends through six nodes to earth, where yin and yang transform and ascend and descend in one cycle—this is one year. The sage models this with the twelve hexagrams’ doubled six lines: the yang fire from *zi* to *si* grows as yin wanes. Thus the outer adheres to yang, the inner to yin, both aligning with the dominant force. Yin’s softness is internal, yang’s hardness external—not the hexagram’s inherent inner and outer. Therefore, *Fu* and *Gou* are the lesser parents, rooted in *Qian* and *Kun*, to clarify the tally fire’s waxing and waning.

A small celestial cycle of one month is the conjunction of the sun and moon’s defenses. The moon receives the sun’s light, becoming full and waning, without mention of the sun, though the sun is implicit. One month is divided into five days as one *hou*, six *hou* as one month—this too is a division of yin and yang into nodes. The moon’s waxing and waning complete one cycle in a month. The sage uses the eight precelestial hexagrams, excluding *Kan* and *Li* as the sun and moon’s bodies, their phases also divided into six *hou* with six hexagrams’ pure three lines as models. The celestial tally is invisible, revealed through the sun and moon: a yang line symbolizes the *hun*’s birth, a yin line the *po*’s birth. The *hun* is born until the full moon, completing *Qian*; the *po* is born until the dark moon, completing *Kun*. Five days make one *hou*; each *hou* advances one line. In the month’s first half, yang lines advance; in the latter half, yin lines advance, aligning with the moon’s waxing and waning. The celestial stems *jia*, *yi*, *bing*, *ding*, *geng*, and *xin* correspond to the moon’s twilight and dawn directions, hence the six hexagrams’ received stems. The empty *ren* is *Li* within *Qian*; the empty *gui* is *Kan* within *Kun*. Yang *ren* and yin *gui* are the northern darkness’s land—hidden in use, obscure and unseen. *Kan*’s *wu* and *Li*’s *si* are the sun and moon’s bodies—*wu* and *si* face the light’s direction, where the sun and moon display benevolence, shining brightly and visibly. Together, the six empties complete the ten stems; the ten stems complete the five phases—this is the Supreme Polarity before division.

Before the new moon, at the *zi* hour, the sun is at *zi* and the moon at *gui*; after the new moon, at the *zi* hour, the moon is at *ren* and the sun at *zi*—hidden in use within *ren* and *gui*. Before the new moon, at the *wu* hour, the sun is at *wu* and the moon at *si*; *si* is received in *ding*. After the new moon, at the *wu* hour, the sun is at *wu* and the moon at *wu*; *wu* is received in *bing*—displaying benevolence in *wu* and *si*. At the new moon’s conjunction, they unite at *zi* and *wu*.

If one further divides the year’s twelve hexagrams into six *hou*, each *hou* contains two hexagrams. At the month’s beginning, it grows from *Kun*’s dark moon to *Tai*—this is the upper *ji*, *Qian* and *Kun*’s *jiji*. At the month’s waning, it declines from *Kun*’s full moon to *Pi*—this is the lower *ji*, *Qian* and *Kun*’s *weiji*. *Qian* and *Kun* come and go, aligning with yin and yang’s advance and retreat. *Pi* and *Tai* ascend and descend, aligning with yin and yang’s equal halves. Thus it is said: “The upper *ji* is half a *jin* of metal; the lower *ji* is half a *jin* of water.”

The sun rises at *jia-mao* and sets at *geng-you*; the moon’s fullness begins at *Zhen*’s *geng* and wanes at *Qian*’s *jia*. At the winter solstice’s *zi*, the day gradually lengthens; at the summer solstice’s *wu*, the day gradually shortens. The moon’s yang retreats: from the new moon’s *zi*, it advances; from the full moon’s *wu*, it retreats. At heaven and earth’s center, the suspended images’ brilliance is unmatched by the sun and moon. The sun and moon are qi—having form but no substance, they interact without obstruction. Yang embraces yin to form the sun; yin embraces yang to form the moon. Thus in a single moment’s mystery or half a year’s duration, all may be taken as models.

Metal and water are each half—this is the initial *ji*’s essence. The initial *ji*’s qi is supremely clear and unclouded—it has qi but no form. Measuring the year by the moon, one month of thirty days corresponds to a year’s three hundred sixty hours, each hour matching one day. Two and a half days—thirty hours—correspond to one month. A small deficiency lacks twelve hours; thus within fifteen days, adjustments are made—this is the month’s compensation for the day’s account.

Therefore, *Qian* and *Kun* are the great parents, employed through *Kan* and *Li* to clarify the tally fire’s advance and retreat. A day’s celestial cycle, a month’s lunar waxing and waning, and a year’s yin-yang ascent and descent—great and small celestial cycles of creation are all the same. Measuring a year by a single hour, one month is evenly divided into two qi. Thus *zi* is the eleventh month; *ren* is *Great Snow*; *zi* is winter—this is rooted in *Qian* and *Kun*, taking the day as the year.

Measuring a month by a single hour, two and a half days—two hours—make one *hou*; six hours make one qi, half a month. Measuring the day by the hour: *mao* corresponds to the eighth day’s upper *ji*; *you* to the twenty-second day’s lower *ji*; *hai* to the dark moon; *zi* to the new moon; *si* to the full moon; *wu* to the waning. This employs *Kan* and *Li*, taking the day as the month, to clarify the tally fire’s waxing and waning, advance and retreat, uniting the year, month, and day’s three celestial cycles as one. Modeling creation with sixty hexagrams, all are the same. Excluding the four *yin* and *yang* hexagrams, heaven and earth, sun and moon envelop the myriad things yet are unused. Combining the sixty-four hexagrams’ three hundred eighty-four lines yields the weight of one *jin*—the two *pian*’s tally, with the four hexagrams’ use contained within.

The Great Celestial Cycle fundamentally arises from *Qian* and *Kun*. Modeling creation with Fu Xi’s hexagram chart, the Small Celestial Cycle’s waxing and waning of *Taiyin* likewise corresponds, with *Kan* and *Li* in accord—this too constitutes the Small Celestial Cycle, employing *Kan* and *Li*. Modeling with King Wen’s hexagram chart, the Great Celestial Cycle’s rhythms of heaven and earth’s ascent and descent, *Qian* and *Kun*’s flowing course, are also in harmony. Thus, the year’s *Fu* is the month’s *Zhen*; the year’s *Gou* is the month’s *Pi*. The day’s *Fu* is the hour’s *zi*; the day’s *Gou* is the hour’s *wu*. From this, it is evident that *Qian*, *Kun*, *Kan*, and *Li* are never without use; the great and small parents are never absent. Fundamentally rooted in *Qian* and *Kun*, *Qian* and *Kun* become the entire body of *Kan* and *Li*; employed through *Kan* and *Li*, *Kan* and *Li* become the central *qi* of *Qian* and *Kun*. Heaven and earth are the sun and moon; the sun and moon are heaven and earth. Heaven conceals *yin* while the sun contains *yang*; earth conceals *yang* while the moon contains *yin*. The forms of heaven, earth, sun, and moon vary in size; the functions of years, months, days, and hours differ in duration. Yet when considered together, all are the unmanifest completion of the Supreme Polarity.

Once divided, from *Zhun* and *Pi* to *Ji Ji*, the sixty hexagrams are employed in pairs to correspond to a single day; the full sixty hexagrams correspond to a month, totaling six hundred *pian* to match a year. In their smallness, even within a single hour, they harmonize with the three hundred sixty. One hour comprises one *miao*; twelve *miao* make one *fen*; thirty *fen* total three hundred sixty *miao* to complete an hour. The wondrous function of this single hour is the immortal’s stolen mechanism, beyond the ken of worldly men. Thus, the greatness of a year, the smallness of a month, the fleeting *miao* of a day, the profound function of an hour—all follow heaven’s Dao, the flourishing of the myriad things, the images of heaven, earth, sun, and moon, their ascent and descent, waxing and waning—none transcend this. How vast is the *Yi*! This is its ultimate.

**[Right: Clarifying Fire Phases]**

Ten—if one cannot distinguish the Five Phases and Four Images, how can one discern cinnabar, mercury, lead, and silver? Before ever hearing of the fire phases in the cultivation of the elixir, one rashly utters grand claims. None pause to reflect on their own errors; instead, they persist in teaching misguided paths, leading others astray and leaving them lost in the eternal ford. How can such deceitful hearts endure without remorse?

**Annotation:** The ten thousand scrolls of elixir classics find their wonder in the *Cantong Qi*. Within it, the chapter "Song of the Tripod and Vessel" is the very marrow of the elixir canon. Yet none among those who study this Way today can fathom it—why do they not ponder this deeply? Let them test this song against my own attainment: if it remains unclear, then my own attainment is not yet perfected. Why, then, do they remain deluded by heterodox schools and false teachings?

Today’s scholars, ignorant of the method of "expelling the old and gathering the new," instead indulge in fantasies of soaring clouds and racing mists. They exalt themselves, imitate others, and, unaware of their own regrets and losses, mislead others into drowning in the ford of delusion—incurable for a lifetime, dying without achievement. How can such deceitful hearts endure without remorse?

**Ye Shu says:** The Nameless Master took the "Song of the Tripod and Vessel" in the *Cantong Qi* as the marrow of the elixir classics, yet many overlook it and fail to investigate deeply. How, then, can they awaken to the great Dao of the true golden elixir?

From the perfected beings I have encountered, I obtained the essentials of two texts, wherein the Five Phases, Four Images, cinnabar, mercury, lead, and silver are used to lure the primordial, undifferentiated qi of true yin and true yang. They do not employ heterodox methods or the conditioned things born of later heaven and earth. Their transformative principles and symbolic patterns are all the same, yet the effects of their fire phases, timings, and the inner and outer elixirs differ.

Through three lifetimes of karmic affinity, I have heard the great Dao. Though I risk celestial punishment by revealing these secrets in writing—first in the *Wuzhen Pian* annotations, then in the *Cantong Qi* commentaries, and now in the *Xuexian Zhengzong*—I do so to dispel confusion for later learners. On the one hand, I clarify the truth of the immortal’s path; on the other, I refute the errors of heterodox schools. May those who study the immortal’s arts, by my words, avoid delusion, trust the immortal’s texts, not stray into heterodoxy, not err in their own cultivation, and not mislead others.

If you encounter a true teacher whose words align with mine, with the *Cantong Qi*, and with the *Wuzhen Pian*, then act swiftly to cultivate together and achieve the great Dao. I do not seek to stand apart to impress the vulgar; I only wish to illuminate the orthodox lineage of the immortal’s path.

The Perfected One, reading the *Cantong Qi*, said: "Do not cling to images or adhere to words." This was spoken for those who have already received the true transmission from a master. Images are set forth as metaphors, words are used to convey meaning—both are but nets and traps, not to be rigidly grasped. As for those who have not met a true teacher or received the true transmission, who wander into heterodox schools and mistake them for the truth, unaware of the great Dao—how can they, in their arrogance, take the Perfected One’s words about not clinging to images as an excuse to avoid seeking profound understanding? If one knows this, one may go a lifetime without hearing the Way spoken of.

Chen Niniu said:
*"If you have not yet met a teacher, study the poems—*
*Within their lines, the secrets lie for steadfast cultivation."*
And again:
*"Without shared language, no bond is formed;*
*Without sufficient effort, no skill is rounded."*
Only when every word is thoroughly examined, when the text is mastered from beginning to end, and when my learning aligns perfectly without a single discrepancy, do I dare not cite heterodox or false teachings as evidence. With diligent effort over time, the numinous will naturally come, and the enlightened heart will spontaneously awaken.

Wei Boyang said: *"After ten thousand recitations, the numinous may be glimpsed;*
*Even if it reveals itself to others, one may still seek meaning in the text."*
Why insist on my humble oral instruction? Through persistent effort over time, my gains from the immortal’s texts have only grown. Thus, I offer this to encourage one another.

Eleven.

Virtue cultivated surpasses eight hundred,
hidden merits accumulated reach three thousand—
only when self and others, kin and foe are equalized
does one fulfill the original vow of the immortals.

Tigers and rhinos, blades and weapons cannot harm;
impermanence’s burning house cannot entangle.
Once the sacred talisman descends,
ascending to heaven is as steady as riding the jade carriage and phoenix palanquin.

*Annotation:* Embracing the One for nine years, merit is perfected and the Dao complete—
when self and others are both forgotten,
how could blades, weapons, tigers, or rhinos bring harm?
The celestial talisman descends, the body soars to the azure vault—
this is the day the true great man emerges from the world.
This speaks of the Golden Elixir’s return:
only when virtue and hidden merits—eight hundred and three thousand—are fully rounded
can one be safeguarded from demonic obstacles.
Cultivating according to the method, one ascends in transcendence,
mounting the jade carriage and phoenix palanquin
to become a perfected immortal, a guest of the Supreme Emperor.

Twelve.

The Cowherd and Weaver Girl’s karmic bond is the Dao’s foundation,
coiled like serpents, endowed by nature.
The toad and crow meet at the new moon [or: the dark of the moon],
uniting in beauty—
the two qi mutually nourish, revolving in motion.
All is the marvelous function of Heaven and Earth:
who comprehends this true essence?
When yin and yang are obstructed, fault arises—
how then can the enduring vastness of heaven and earth be attained?

*Annotation:* The Cowherd and Weaver Girl meet once a year;
the moon’s yin and the sun’s yang unite once a month.
The tortoise and snake, the coiled dragon and serpent, support one another—
all are made so by the two qi of yin and yang.
This is truly the root of the Dao,
the workings of the Great Elixir of Golden Cinnabar—
each step mirrors it.
For the true One’s qi is profound and formless;
only when the initial qi of the two eights—yin and yang—conjoin
can it descend to shape the grain-like form of the elixir.

Once the elixir is ingested,
without the intertwining embrace of the firing process,
how can the transmutation into the Golden Liquid Returned Elixir be achieved?
Alas!

The *Cantong Qi* states:
*"The osprey calls on the river isle—
the fair maiden, the gentleman’s fine match.
The male does not dwell alone,
the female does not abide in solitude.
The dark warrior and coiled serpent support one another,
illustrating how the female and male must invariably rely on each other—
such is the principle’s dwelling.
What doubt remains?"*

Inverting the practice, the cosmos lies within the palm of your hand.
A certain master said:
*"Solitary yin cannot generate,
lone yang cannot complete.
Only by borrowing the union of female and male qi
can the Way of production and transformation arise."*

That Heaven and Earth endure long and abide in permanence
is due to the natural Dao of yin-yang intercourse.
If Heaven did not descend and Earth did not ascend,
the four seasons would not follow their order,
and the myriad things would not come to be.
Thus, the immortal elder repeatedly emphasizes this chapter,
for those who deeply grasp its meaning may unite with it in spirit.

---

Another verse, symbolizing the intercalary month:
The elixir is the supreme treasure of the colored body,
refined to achieve boundless transformation.
Further, on the nature, investigate the true source—
the decisive insight into life and death’s marvelous function.
No need to await another body in a future life:
here and now, attain the Buddha’s divine powers.
Ever since the Dragon Girl accomplished this work,
who has been able to follow in her footsteps?

*Annotation:*
The Golden Elixir can transform the formed into the formless,
thus enabling infinite transmutation—
profound and unfathomable as the dragon’s manifestation.
If one can additionally recognize the mind and see the nature,
dispelling illusory delusions to expand divine powers,
then the Dao of both nature and life becomes doubly perfected,
form and spirit both wondrous.
This path grows ever more refined,
transcending the leakless to become a body of indestructible vajra—
the supreme Great Dao.

Thus, the immortal elder said:
If one realizes the true gold of the wondrously colored body,
one certifies the true gold of compassionate appearance—
majestic and dignified, a teacher of gods and humans,
demonstrating divine powers,
universally manifesting across the Dharma realms,
wielding unimpeded great compassion,
equal wisdom,
and adorned Buddha-lands,
widely proclaiming the wondrous Dharma to universally deliver sentient beings.
Yet this must be coupled with recognizing the mind and seeing the nature
to refine this Dao.

Formerly, the Dragon Girl suddenly awakened to the mind-jewel
and transcended into Buddha-nature—
this is that very Dao.
If, however, a practitioner disdains this illusory form,
unable to cultivate the Golden Elixir,
and instead seeks to directly transcend into the Tathāgata’s true emptiness,
serene and eternally quiescent—
this is the ultimate nirvana of the three times—
then such words, such bodily forms, are not to be adopted.

---

Five quatrains, symbolizing the five phases of lead, mercury, cinnabar, silver, and earth:

*"Though you comprehend the true suchness of nature,
you cannot escape discarding the body only to re-enter it.
If you understand and further refine the Great Elixir,
you instantly transcend the leakless and become a true person."*

*Annotation:*
If one suddenly awakens to the true mind
and directly transcends into the Tathāgata’s true emptiness,
the ocean of pure quiescent nature,
one is ultimately bound to this life and the next,
exiting one body and entering another.
How is this superior to cultivating the Golden Elixir,
refining form into the formless,
achieving unfathomable transformation,
and attaining the responsiveness of a thousand hands and eyes?
Thus, in the Dao of form, spirit, nature, and life,
one perfects them both,
transcends the leakless,
and possesses the majestic and dignified true gold of compassion,
a teacher of gods and humans,
certifying the supreme, utmost truth.

Before the great function manifests,
before the great Dharma is fully illuminated,
even the slightest leakage—
discarding the body to re-enter it—
persists.
If the jewel is fully bright and illuminated,
the treasure refined into the Golden Elixir,
the Dao accomplished in its ten extremities,
one is called a true person.

The deluded of the world,
with their rubbing, swallowing, and exhaling,
their minor arts of aligning oneself with others,
call it the Golden Elixir.
Yet the Golden Elixir arises naturally,
while minor arts arise from contrivance.
The Golden Elixir takes the moon as its root,
emerging from the direction of metal’s seventh branch,
guarded by the origin of water’s kan trigram.
Metal and water unite,
congealing into creation—
this is why it is called the Golden Elixir.

*Exegesis:*
Cultivating both nature and life is called the Dao of one yin and one yang.
If one only awakens to the past but cannot complete life,
one falls into the illness of partial yin or partial yang,
suffering the affliction of discarding the body to re-enter it.

---

**Two: Entering the Womb, Seizing the Dwelling, and Relocating the Old Abode—**
these are called the Four Fruits,
yet how can they compare to subduing the dragon and taming the tiger,
or the true gold erecting a house—when will it ever wither?

*Annotation:*
When has true gold erecting a house ever withered?
The *Scripture on Saving the Dead* says:
*"Even withered bones revive and rise to become people—
how much more so for those who swallow the pearl-like grain of the elixir?"*
Entering the womb, seizing the dwelling—
the Four Fruits are merely the ghosts of yin spirits.
The *Daoguang* says:
*"Entering the womb and seizing the dwelling are the practices of those clinging to emptiness;
subduing the dragon and taming the tiger are the wonders of the Returned Elixir."*

*Exegesis:*
Yin spirits generate consciousness,
enter the mother’s womb to be born into the world.
Seizing the dwelling: another’s consciousness has already entered the womb,
and one seizes it to be born.
Relocating: borrowing the birth-body of a transformed person
and investing one’s consciousness into it.
The old abode: preserving the nature of the yin spirit
to sustain the bodily form without entering extinction—
the Four Fruits all lack the Golden Elixir’s transmutation,
their transformations entirely those of yin spirits.

---

**Three: Mirroring the Form, Closing the Breath, and Contemplating the Spirit—**
a method initially arduous,
later a smooth path.
In an instant, one can roam ten thousand miles,
yet alas—
the house is broken, and one must relocate.

*Annotation:*
Mirroring the form, closing the breath, contemplating the spirit—
these are minor methods of the Hinayana, the arts of yin spirits.
Initially, they are exceedingly difficult,
but with practice, one becomes proficient and unobstructed.
In a flash, one can traverse myriad lands—
such is the marvelous clarity of their numinous spirit.
Yet alas, their form belongs to yin,
the bodily shell difficult to secure, easy to decay,
inevitably leading to entering the womb or seizing the dwelling,
like relocating.

*Exegesis:*
Mirroring the form: suspending a mirror in the chamber,
concentrating the spirit within it to depart.
Closing the breath: sealing the body’s qi
as if one were unborn, in the womb—
placing a goose feather on the nose,
if it remains unmoved for twelve breaths, it is a minor art;
for one hundred and twenty breaths, a major art.
If one can reach a thousand, ascension is near—
as in Bodhidharma’s *Treatise on Embryonic Breathing*,
the *Regulations for Inhalation and Exhalation in the Three Vehicles’ Seated Meditation*,
or exiting through dhyāna.
Contemplating the spirit: concentrating the spirit in one locus—
whether between the brows, atop the head,
the thirty-nine doors of the Great Cavern,
or the inner and outer qi of the Yellow Court—
or cultivating the sixteen contemplations to depart.
All these lack the Golden Elixir’s transmutation,
their transformations entirely those of yin spirits.

---

**Four: The Buddha’s Teachings Guide People to Cultivate the Pure Land—**
only because the Pure Land is the golden realm,
where forms alone are real.
The other two are not true—
why speculate in vain?

*Annotation:*
The Western Pure Land is the direction of metal,
the true land of the Buddha’s body.
The Eastern and Northern Pure Lands are illusory,
not the true Dharma-body’s abode.
Thus, the Buddha taught sentient beings to cultivate the Western Pure Land,
for it alone is the true golden realm.

A Note states: The Western Pure Land of Ultimate Bliss lies in the west—the direction of metal—where only the Golden Elixir, a single grain like a millet seed weighing one catty, is produced. The Buddha consumes it, hence his sixteen-foot golden body and wondrous physical marks, which likewise arise from the Golden Elixir’s transformation. The sixteen-foot measure follows the numerology of two eights; the west is metal. Yet none in the world comprehend this. An ancient immortal once declared:

*"I ask you, who is this Gautama?*
*Dwelling in the Western Land of Ultimate Bliss,*
*where two eights yield the essence of gold—*
*from this, the sixteen-foot golden body is attained.*
*If one can empty this illusory form,*
*directly receiving the true method of the sages,*
*then in an instant, having swallowed the millet-pearl,*
*one transforms into a vajra-body in a moment."*

These words exhaust the matter; beyond this, all other discussions are mere idle speculation.

---

**Five:**
Common sayings often declare: To attain the supreme Dao, one ought to seek it within the subtle workings of the ordinary. By inverting the search within daily life, the dust and sand of the great earth all become treasures.

A Note states: True lead and true mercury are not apart from common speech, everyday affairs, or the intervals of daily life. Cultivating them in inversion, the dust and sand of the great earth all become treasures.

The song on the right says:
*Day after day, only within your household dwelling,*
*moment by moment, following you wherever you go—*
*yet you remain unaware.*

*Central Scroll of the Commentary and Subcommentary on the* Awakening to Reality
*<Subsection: Daoist Works, Category of* Awakening to Reality *Commentary and Subcommentary>*
*Imperially Commissioned* Four Treasuries *Library*
*Commentary and Subcommentary on the* Awakening to Reality, *Lower Scroll*
*Composed by* Zhang Boduan *of the Song*
*Annotated by* Weng Baoguang
*Subcommentary by* Dai Qizong *of the Yuan*

To read the *Zhouyi Cantong Qi*:
The wondrous workings of the Great Elixir follow Qian and Kun.
Qian and Kun move—thus the Five Agents divide;
the Five Agents divide—thus the constant Dao has arising and ceasing.
When the Five Agents reverse, the elixir’s body is ever numinous, ever preserved.
The One first appears from emptiness and nonbeing;
the Two Modes arise from the One, their root unfolds.
The Four Images do not depart from the Two Bodies;
the Eight Trigrams mutually serve as ancestor and descendant.
The myriad things are born through transformation—
fortune and misfortune, regret and remorse are thus distinguished.
The common folk use this daily yet remain unaware;
the sage alone can fathom its source.
Thus the marvelous Dao of the *Yi* exhausts the principles of Qian and Kun,
and so entrusts its images to this text.
When Pi and Tai intermingle, yin and yang now ascend, now descend;
when Zhun and Meng arise, movement and stillness occur at dawn and dusk.
Kan and Li are male and female;
water and fire.
Zhen and Dui are dragon and tiger;
po and hun.
Abiding in the center yields the Yellow Skirt—supreme fortune;
encountering Kang brings positionless honor.
Yet if one fails to attend to the beginning and end of the myriad things,
how can the convergence of the two qi be made manifest?
The waxing and waning of the moon’s crescent respond to the waning and waxing of spirit and essence;
the sun’s rising and setting accord with the cold and warmth of construction and defense.
The root establishes words to clarify images;
once images are grasped, words are forgotten.
It is like setting up images to point to meaning—
once meaning is awakened to, images are discarded.
The enlightened find it ever simpler, ever easier;
the deluded grow ever more confused, ever more entangled.
Thus the superior adept who reads the *Cantong Qi*
does not cling to images or grasp at words.

A Note states:
Qian and Kun are father and mother.
Qian and Kun move—yin and yang qi transform into the Five Agents and give birth to the myriad things.
Thus, following yin and yang and the Five Agents in their molding, one becomes human.
The human body is half yin, half yang because yin and yang take form.
Being half yin and half yang, it is subject to arising and ceasing.
Yang governs arising, yin governs ceasing—
one arises, one ceases; one departs, one arrives.
This is the constant Dao, the natural principle of following the flow.
The sage, reversing this, applies yin and yang in inversion,
establishing Qian and Kun as the cauldron and vessel,
stealing the primordial One Qi to forge the elixir.
Refining form into formlessness, one merges with the Dao and guards the One.
The Dao arises from Non-Ultimate—how could immortality have an end?
Thus it is said: following the constant Dao brings arising and ceasing;
reversing the elixir’s body yields everlasting numinosity and preservation.
Emptiness and nonbeing are the body of the Dao.
The Dao generates the One Qi, which then transforms into yin and yang—
thus yang is Heaven, yin is Earth: these are the Two Modes.
Heaven One generates Water, dwelling in the north—this is winter;
Earth Two generates Fire, dwelling in the south—this is summer;
Heaven Three generates Wood, dwelling in the east—this is spring;
Earth Four generates Metal, dwelling in the west—this is autumn.
These form the four seasons, called the Four Images.
Heaven is Qian, dwelling in Xu and Hai;
Earth is Kun, dwelling in Wei and Shen.
Kun seeks Qian and gives birth to three sons:
the eldest is Zhen, dwelling in Mao;
the middle is Kan, dwelling in Zi;
the youngest is Gen, dwelling in Yin and Chou.
Qian seeks Kun and gives birth to three daughters:
the eldest is Xun, dwelling in Chen and Si;
the middle is Li, dwelling in Wu;
the youngest is Dui, dwelling in You.
Together they form the Eight Trigrams, called the eight directions.
Thus from Zi to Si is the yang realm;
from Wu to Hai is the yin realm.
As yin and yang revolve, the qi of the four seasons cycle through the eight directions,
mutually completing and beginning anew—
hence they are said to serve as ancestor and descendant.
In spring and summer, yang qi arises and grows—
the myriad things receive its power and flourish.
In autumn and winter, yin qi contracts and kills—
the myriad things receive its punishment and wither.
One flourishing, one withering; one fortune, one misfortune—
thus the myriad things are born through transformation,
and fortune and misfortune, regret and remorse are thereby distinguished.
Tracing the origins of fortune and misfortune, regret and remorse—
from the myriad images and Eight Trigrams to the four seasons and yin and yang—
nothing departs from the One Qi or strays from the Great Dao.
Thus the Dao is the One Qi;
yin and yang, the four seasons, the Five Agents, the Eight Trigrams,
the myriad images, fortune and misfortune, regret and remorse—
where are they not present?
Nowhere are they absent.

Wherever one looks—seeing, hearing, speaking, moving, sleeping, waking, every gesture, every contact, whether pure or clamorous, strange or cunning, whether worm-liver or rat-limb, tare or chaff, tile or pebble—there is nowhere the Dao is not. Nowhere is the Dao not, yet the Dao resides within humanity while humanity remains unaware; humanity dwells within the Dao while the Dao does not exclude it. Thus the common people use it daily yet do not know it.

From emptiness and stillness to daily use, they speak of the Dao without knowing it. The sage explores the profound, seeks the hidden, exhausts principle and fulfills nature to reach destiny. Thus they were able to compose the *Yi*, embodying the Dao’s wondrous workings, establishing Qian and Kun as the *Yi*’s gateways. Once Qian and Kun are established, the Dao of the *Yi* moves within them.

Thus Qian and Kun seek each other and form the Eight Trigrams; the Eight Trigrams follow one another and transform into the sixty-four hexagrams. Each hexagram has six lines: yang lines are odd, yin lines are even. Each single yang line, multiplied by four and nine, yields thirty-six *fang*; six yang lines together yield two hundred sixteen *fang*—these are Qian’s *fang*. Each single yin line, multiplied by four and six, yields twenty-four *fang*; six yin lines together yield one hundred forty-four *fang*—these are Kun’s *fang*. Adding the thirty-two *fang* of Qian and Kun’s two hexagrams, three hundred sixty *fang* combine to form the eleven thousand five hundred twenty *fang* of the Great Expansion of the Supreme Polarity. This encompasses the Three Powers and embraces the myriad images. Thus the ultimate of fortune and misfortune, regret and remorse, the omens of life and death, fortune and disaster—none can escape beyond these numbers. Therefore it is said: the wondrous Dao of the *Yi* exhausts the substance and function of creation.

Since the sages rectified the substance and function of creation to expound the *Yi*, the Perfected Wei Boyang, seeing that the Dao of the *Yi* accorded with the Golden Elixir, borrowed the hexagrams to compose the *Cantong qi*, illuminating the *fang* of the Golden Elixir. Yet this was nothing more than borrowed imagery and allegory to speak of the *Cantong qi*.

The essentials of elixir refinement do not exceed the two words *metal* and *fire*. The sages first took the two substances of true yin and true yang as the furnace and crucible, then lured the qi of the Supreme Polarity into the midst of emptiness and nothingness—beyond seeking or fathoming. If one does not use true yin and true yang to lure it, one cannot descend the numinous and form the image. Thus the *Cantong qi* establishes the two hexagrams Qian and Kun as the furnace and crucible, divides the two hexagrams Kan and Li as lead and mercury, and arranges the four hexagrams in the central palace. The remaining hexagrams are distributed within a single month to move the tally of fire. Thus Qian and Kun are dragon and tiger; Zhen and Dui are husband and wife.

The *hun* and *po* are also Kan and Li; Kan and Li are lead and mercury, water and fire, male and female, emotion and nature. If one extends this analogy, the implications are boundless. Yet when one seeks the most fitting expression, nothing surpasses the metaphor of the two substances, true yin and true yang. By conjoining these two substances with qi in the central palace—the Yellow Chamber of the Dao—one forms the elixir. Thus it is said: "Abiding in the center, the yellow skirt brings supreme fortune." This speaks of the external medicine.

Once the elixir is obtained and ingested, without true fire there is no way to nurture the sacred embryo or circulate the primordial yang’s true qi as fire.
