Fire has no fixed position; it flows through the six voids. Thus it is said: "When encountering *Kang*, it has no position yet is revered." This speaks of the internal medicine.

Now, Heaven’s One generates water, which in humans is called *jing*; Earth’s Two generates fire, which in humans is called *shen*. A person’s *jing* and *shen* day and night circulate and guard the body, constantly moving in accord with the qi of Heaven and Earth’s yin and yang without cease. On the day of the winter solstice, within Earth there is a single yang’s qi that ascends, forming the hexagram *Fu*. The human’s primordial qi is likewise. Thus, advancing the yang fire until the first month, when the qi of yin and yang are evenly balanced, they naturally conjoin, forming the hexagram *Tai*. The human’s primordial qi is the same. This is why ceasing fire is called "bathing." On the day of the summer solstice, within Heaven there is a single yin’s qi that descends, forming the hexagram *Gou*. Thus, advancing the yin tally until the seventh month, when the qi of yin and yang are evenly balanced, they naturally conjoin, forming the hexagram *Pi*. The human’s primordial qi is likewise. This is why halting the tally is also called "bathing." Thus it is said: when *Pi* and *Tai* alternate, yin and yang either ascend or descend.

The sages transpose this yearly cycle of qi into the span of a single month—thirty days—where two and a half days and thirty hours correspond to one month’s thirty days. From the day after the new moon, when the moon’s first faint light appears, it is the hexagram *Fu*; by the first quarter, when the moon is half-illuminated and metal and water are evenly balanced, it is *Tai*; by the sixteenth day, when the moon begins to wane, it is *Gou*; by the last quarter, when the moon is half-dark and metal and water are again evenly balanced, it is *Pi*. Thus the waxing and waning of the sun and moon correspond to the flourishing and decline of *jing* and *shen*. This speaks of the month.

Further, they transpose this monthly cycle of qi into the span of a single day—twelve hours. At the *zi* hour, one yang arises, so within the kidneys there is a single yang’s pure *jing* qi that ascends, forming *Fu*, and the yang fire is advanced. At the *wu* hour, one yin arises, so within the heart there is a single yin’s numinous *shen* qi that descends, forming *Gou*, and the yin tally is advanced. Thus it is said: *Fu* and *Gou* illuminate the return and flight of the two qi. This speaks of the day.

The sun’s rising marks day, its setting marks night. The sages move the tally and fire within one day and night, distinguishing the qi of warmth, coolness, cold, and heat, externally aligning with Heaven’s tally and internally harmonizing with the *ying* and *wei* to diminish and augment the body’s refinement, operation, warming, and nurturing of the midnight pearl. Thus it is said: the sun’s rising and setting align with the cold and warmth of *ying* and *wei*. This speaks of the day.

*Zi* is the chief of the six yang, so at dawn the yang fire is advanced, employing the hexagram *Zhun* to govern the matter. *Wu* is the origin of the six yin, so at dusk the yin tally is advanced, employing the hexagram *Meng* to govern the matter. Thus it is said: *Zhun* and *Meng* act, so movement and stillness occur at dawn and dusk.

One day and night govern two hexagrams, *Zhun* and *Meng*, the beginning of the sixty hexagrams. *Jiji* is not the end of the sixty hexagrams; the end returns to the beginning, the beginning returns to the end. Thus it is said: "In *Jiji*, be cautious of the end and beginning of the myriad things." This speaks of the hours.

All the above are Master Wei’s [methods of] employing the great Dao of the golden elixir—most simple, most easy—where no profound secrets can be expounded. Thus he borrowed the images of the *Yijing* to establish meaning and convey teachings, enabling students to observe these hexagrams and awaken to their essentials. If one attains the wondrous subtleties of the golden elixir, then the analogies of Qian and Kun, Kan and Li, dragon and tiger, *hun* and *po*, lead and mercury, water and fire can all be discarded. This speaks of the external borrowing of images.

If one attains the true mechanism of moving fire, then the hexagrams *Zhun*, *Meng*, *Jiji*, *Gou*, *Pi*, and *Tai*, along with their lines and fractions, can all be rendered useless. This speaks of the internal borrowing of images.

This is how the Immortal Elder, fearing that students reading the *Cantong qi* would fail to grasp the profound intent of the True Man and instead cling to images and adhere to words without relinquishing images and forgetting words, composed this piece to instruct like-minded seekers. His benevolence is thus. The *Song of the Elder of Qingcheng* says: "I thank the former sages for their secret formulas—true fish-traps and rabbit-snares—where at the point of attainment, not even a single word remains." From this, one can see its utmost simplicity. Without encountering a true teacher’s oral instructions, it is not easy to tread its profound mysteries—even by one chance in ten thousand.

The commentary says: From "emptiness and nothingness" to "daily use" speaks of the Dao. From "the sages" to "the transformations of creation" speaks of the *Yijing*. From "Master Wei Boyang" to "mere borrowing of images" speaks of the *Cantong qi*. From "the essentials of elixir refinement" to "supreme fortune" speaks of the external medicine. From "once the elixir is obtained" to "has no position yet is revered" speaks of the internal medicine. From "Heaven’s One generates water" to "either ascend or descend" speaks of the year. From "the sages transpose this yearly cycle" to "flourishing and decline" speaks of the month. From "further, they transpose this" to "cold and warmth" speaks of the day. From "*Zi* is the chief of yang" to "end and beginning" speaks of the hours. From "the wondrous subtleties of the golden elixir" onward, where nothing can be said, speaks of the external borrowing of images. From "the true mechanism of moving fire" to "can all be rendered useless" speaks of the internal borrowing of images.

Moreover, the number thirty-two serves as the boundary of Qian and Kun, totaling three hundred sixty. Multiplying thirty-two by two hundred sixteen yields six thousand nine hundred twelve—this is the boundary number of the thirty-two yang hexagrams. Again, multiplying thirty-two by one hundred forty-four yields four thousand six hundred eight—this is the boundary number of the thirty-two yin hexagrams. Together, the two chapters comprise eleven thousand five hundred twenty. Now, taking the seventh month as the pivot between *Pi* (否) and *Tai* (泰), one bathes at their juncture. Yet when the myriad things are full and overflowing at the intersection of *Pi* and *Tai*, one also takes the hexagrams *Pi* and *Tai* to correspond to the spring and autumn equinoxes for bathing, though the application differs. The subtleties of the *Wuzhen* texts possess their own wondrous uses. Thus, the Immortal Elder also states in the *Four Hundred Characters*:

*"As for the bathing method,
Mao and You are likewise empty."*
Master Xinglin remarks:
*"Bathing does not lie in Mao and You."*
Hence, Master Wumingzi simply takes the two hexagrams *Pi* and *Tai*, where yin and yang are evenly balanced, as the two equinoxes of spring and autumn, or as the seventh month, or as the two solstices. Without grasping their subtleties, one will be confounded.

**Song Bestowed upon Daoist Liu of White Dragon Cave**

Jade flees, gold flies—both luminaries hasten.
No sooner does one hear blossoms bloom than autumn frost descends.
Vainly boast Peng’s thousand years of age—
It is but a lightning flash amid the clouds.
A lightning flash—how all too swift!
A hundred years amount to but thirty thousand days.
Within them, cold and heat alternately torment,
Unseen, the youthful visage fades in darkness.
Though children and grandchildren fill the eye,
Affection and attachment only deepen entanglement.
When essence is exhausted and the body withers,
Who can teach you to briefly halt?
Since halting briefly admits no strategy,
Inevitably, the body returns to flowing water.
Yet look upon the sages and worthies of old—
How many have truly mastered remaining in the world?

The Master of Empty Mystery says:
Sun and moon shuttle like a loom, time flies like an arrow—
Few among men reach seventy years.
Cold and heat press upon us, children and grandchildren tug at the heart.
From old age to death, generation after generation it is ever thus—
Yet who turns back to steadfastly seek the Dao and preserve the form in the world?

I deeply sigh: human life is hard to attain, the supreme Dao hard to hear.
Though one dwells in the world, there is a method—
Only that most men lack the capacity,
And instead rush into the mountains to seek herbs and grasses,
To subdue lead and refine mercury in hopes of forging cinnabar and the Elixir of Yang.

Men of the world, seeking the Dao, know not the true path,
But fiercely love the external furnace, hunting rare herbs and grasses,
Smelting common lead and mercury, hoping to transmute them into the Elixir of Yang,
To exchange bones and become immortal treasures.
The immortal elder has a poem that says:
*"Refrain from refining the Three Yellows and Four Spirits;
If you seek among the grasses, you stray further from the truth."*
This warns men of the world: do not let the external furnace and treasures mislead the heart.
When the elixir ripens, gold will naturally fill the house—
Why waste fire and squander wealth?

The forging of the Elixir of Yang is entirely distinct:
One must seek crimson blood within Kan,
Seize it and bring it to Li to refine the essence of yin.
Harmonize and blend them at the proper time—
The proper time requires a matchmaker.
The Golden Elder and the Maiden of Mystery unite in marriage:
The Golden Elder favors the White Tiger,
The Maiden of Mystery ever rides the Crimson Dragon.
The tiger comes to stillness, sitting in autumn mountains;
The dragon stirs, rising from the azure pool.
When the two beasts meet, they battle fiercely—
Waves surge like a boiling cauldron,
The Yellow Dame and Old Ding lend their might,
Shaking heaven and earth, startling gods and spirits.

The subjugation of lead and mercury, the forging of elixir to transmute crimson blood and reshape bones—
All this is but the resource of greed and delusion,
Unknowing of planting virtue, only increasing sin.
What benefit is there to the great matter of life and death?
The forging of the Golden Elixir, the transformation of mortal bones into pure Yang immortals—
This is entirely distinct.
Within Kan, seek crimson blood from the White Tiger to obtain the *qi* of the eighth string—
This is the extraction of essence from black lead.
Within Li, refine the essence of yin from the Azure Dragon to obtain the *qi* of the eighth vessel—
This is the extraction of marrow from red lead.
Kan is black, yet within it one seeks the crimson;
Li is yang, yet within it one refines the yin.
When the two substances unite, gather them on the proper day, at the proper time.
Once the timing is correct and the Yellow Dame serves as matchmaker,
The Golden Elder and White Tiger, the Maiden of Mystery and Crimson Dragon,
Naturally pair as husband and wife, their affections entwined.
The two substances unite, the Yellow Dame as go-between,
The Golden Elder lending might, seizing heaven and earth—
Heaven and earth tremble, gods and spirits submit and flee.
An ancient song says:
*"Subtly they rise and fall, the essence of heaven and earth;
Gathering yin and yang, startling gods and spirits."*
This is not the so-called gold, stone, herbs, and grasses of the world. **[Here refers to external elixirs.]**

Once the battle ends and the clouds and rain disperse,
Plant a mysterious pearl in the mud at the bottom.
From this, the root and sprout gradually grow.
Tend it in due season, embrace true essence—
After ten months, the embryo is shed, swallowed into the mouth.
Unawares, the mortal body now possesses spirit.
When the wild battle of the two beasts concludes,
The Golden Elixir is obtained at once, swallowed into the five viscera.
Plant this mysterious pearl in the earthen crucible at the muddy bottom,
Advance and retreat according to the fire talisman, refine with true fire.
From this, the Golden Liquid and Returned Elixir take root,
The sprout growing day by day, flourishing month by month.
Tend it in due season, nourishing its growth—
After ten months, the sacred embryo is perfected,
Refining form into *qi*, naturally possessing manifold spiritual *qi*.
Refining *qi* into spirit, naturally uniting with the Dao. **[Here refers to internal elixirs.]**

This matter is rare in the world, not known to ordinary men.
If one lacks immortal bones from past lives,
How easily can one encounter it?
If encountered, one should immediately refine—
For the light of life is as urgent as an arrow.
When seeking fish, one must cast a net;
Do not wait by the waterside, sighing in vain.
I hear you have known the medicine for many years—
Why not collect your heart and refine mercury and lead?
Do not let the candle be blown out by the wind.
The six paths of rebirth—do not blame heaven.
The Great Dao of the Golden Elixir is rarely transmitted in the world.
If you have planted immortal bones in past lives and met a true teacher,
Begin cultivation swiftly, though it may already be too late.
The years do not wait for men—do not die in vain.
Since you already know the medicine, hasten to cultivate.
Lead and mercury are not material things of this world,
Nor are they the medicine of subduing lead and mercury to forge the Elixir of Yang.
This urges men to cultivate early.

Nearly all in the world today are deceitful—
Even those clad in plain robes claim to be Daoists.
Ask them what gold and wood are—
They fall silent, mute as if struck dumb,
Then turn to breath retention and fasting,
Pursuing other paths and long roads.
Have you not seen the *Song of Breaking Delusion*?
*"The method of the Great One containing truth is most excellent—*
*Do not blame my words for being wild and coarse,*
*Only that men of the time find it hard to discern."*
Only when your heart aligns with mine
Dare I pour out my thoughts to you.

Vulgar men take the practice of the Dao as their duty,
Yet know not what gold and wood are.
In vain they practice breath retention and fasting,
Minor arts of side paths—
How could they understand the *Song of Breaking Delusion*?
*"How is this the Dao?*
*The Great One containing truth—*
*The five phases move in reverse,*
*The tiger is born in water, Kan and Li inverted,*
*The dragon emerges from fire."*
This is what it means.

Some interpret this song as referring to the ten-month gestation,
The sacred embryo’s entry and exit, its wondrous transformations—
Their words are correct.
Others take a single spiritual elixir, swallowing it into the belly,
Citing the *Cantong Qi*:
*"Golden sand enters the five viscera."*
Later generations doubt this as external elixir—
Their words are not fitting.
They have not grasped the true transmission of *Wuzhen Pian*.
Its essentials state:
*"True lead is the primordial *qi* born from the kidneys;*
*Divine mercury is the true within nature, issuing from the heart.*
*The *qi* within *qi* conceals true water;*
*The true within nature harbors true fire."*
Why not deeply investigate the preface of *Wuzhen Pian*?
It says:
*"Nowadays, scholars take lead and mercury as the two *qi*,
Divide heart and kidneys as Kan and Li—
These are all cases of the sun and moon losing their Dao,
Lead and mercury in separate furnaces.
How can they hope to congeal the Returned Elixir? Is it not far off?"*
This is what *Wuzhen Pian* ridicules.
Yet now, some take this as the essential method—
From this, it is clear they have not grasped the true transmission of *Wuzhen Pian*.

If you meet a true teacher, you will know my words are not false.
I do not dare to denounce them, but only wish to clarify the Dao.

**Song of Stone Bridge**

My home lies north of Stone Bridge,
At the mountain pass that tames the waters,
Where ancient trees stand guard.
Beneath the bridge, the stream flows clear,
From the foot of Kunlun Mountain, a fragrant spring wells forth.
I dwell within these mountains, truly boasting their splendor—
Everywhere, unfading blossoms are planted.
To the north of the mountain, a cave shelters a fierce tiger,
Emerging from its den with a roar that stirs the wind.
To the south, a deep pool harbors a flood dragon,
Rising through clouds to send down rain, shrouding the mountains in mist.
When the two beasts meet and battle,
The dark essence and flood dragon submit—all true auspices.
The scene is wondrous fair; I secretly rejoice,
Pouring my own wine, drinking to drunkenness,
Strumming a tuneless zither.
The notes teach attentiveness—
Alas, in drunkenness, none understand.
Muddled and silent, I seem a fool.
Gazing upward, I observe the workings of creation:
The sun sets in the west, the moon rises in the east—
Heaven is earth, earth is heaven,
Yin and yang reverse and unite naturally.
Once you recognize the inversion of the five phases,
You will ascend in rosy clouds, returning to the grotto-heaven,
A golden house with rafters of white jade,
Jade maidens and golden lads attending before you.
The Southern Asterism and Northern Dipper are arrayed clearly,
The myriad phenomena manifest boundlessly.
Without day or night, ceaselessly,
The fire of the celestial revolution is complete.
If you ask the true place of the Golden Elixir,
Seek the teacher who points out lead in water.
Wood gives birth to fire, metal to water—
Water and fire must distinguish front and rear.
Discern the floating and sinking, know host and guest.
Lead, silver, cinnabar, and mercury—only then can they unite.
There is hardness and softness; do not be careless.
Knowing contentment, always content, return to the root.
The myriad spirits celebrate the era of Great Peace.
Then the nation prospers, the people rejoice—
This matter is excellent to ponder.
Those of the Dao who know this principle,
Later generations who study the true—
They say only of preserving and nurturing, of circulating *qi*,
That it is easy to attain before their eyes.
Those who ingest it achieve wonders beyond compare:
First, they cure illness, then extend their years.
Refining with fire, they transform the yang body.
The cultivator of the Dao ceases thought, puts aside questions of side paths,
Knowing only to deceive men in the moment,
Unawares, their own bodies wither in darkness.
I urge later learners to be resolute—
Do not abandon your home to wander elsewhere.
The wondrous Dao is not apart from your own body—
How could it lie in a thousand mountains or ten thousand streams?
Do not procrastinate, clinging to baseness.
Hasten to seek a teacher, pursue the mysterious method.
While alive, if you do not learn to cultivate,
Who knows what womb you may enter in the next life?
If you have the heart to see it through to the end,
The great matter of human life is only life and death.
If heaven betrays the man of Dao,
It would make me a lower spirit in the three paths.

**Postscript:**
Mediocre men take the practice of the Dao as their duty,
Yet know not what gold and wood are.
In vain they practice breath retention and fasting,
Minor arts of side paths—
How could they understand the *Song of Breaking Delusion*?
*"How is this the Dao?*
*The Great One containing truth—*
*The five phases move in reverse,*
*The tiger is born in water, Kan and Li inverted,*
*The dragon emerges from fire."*
This is what it means.
Some interpret this as the ten-month gestation,
The sacred embryo’s entry and exit, its wondrous transformations—
Their words are correct.
Yet to take a single spiritual elixir and swallow it into the belly,
Citing the *Cantong Qi*: *"Golden sand enters the five viscera,"*
And for later generations to doubt this as external elixir—
This is not fitting.
They have not grasped the true transmission.
Its essentials state:
*"True lead is the primordial *qi* born from the kidneys;*
*Divine mercury is the true within nature, issuing from the heart.*
*The *qi* within *qi* conceals true water;*
*The true within nature harbors true fire."*
Why not deeply investigate the preface of *Wuzhen Pian*?
It says:
*"Nowadays, scholars take lead and mercury as the two *qi*,
Divide heart and kidneys as Kan and Li—
These are all cases of the sun and moon losing their Dao,
Lead and mercury in separate furnaces.
How can they hope to congeal the Returned Elixir? Is it not far off?"*
This is what *Wuzhen Pian* ridicules.
Yet now, some take this as the essential method—
From this, it is clear they have not grasped the true transmission of *Wuzhen Pian*.
If you meet a true teacher, you will know my words are not false.
I do not dare to denounce them, but only wish to clarify the Dao.

Kongxuanzi says: This song is a comprehensive praise of the marvels of the Golden Elixir and a refutation of the errors of heterodox schools. Where it speaks of "Dragon-Tiger, lead-silver, cinnabar-mercury, floating and sinking, host and guest," it refers to the true essence of the two things, yin and yang. Where it says, "The sun sets in the west, the moon rises in the east; heaven is earth, earth is heaven," it illustrates the union of yin and yang and the inversion of the Five Phases. "Lead within water, wood engenders fire, metal engenders water" metaphorically describes the products of yin and yang. The "mysterious pearl" embodies the form of the completed Golden Elixir. "Day and night, drawing and adding" clarify the ten months of practice. "Preserving and nourishing *qi*" refutes the minor techniques of heterodox schools. Its praises of the Golden Elixir’s efficacy and exhortations to cultivate the Dao are evident in its words and require no further explanation.

*Wuzhen Pian Zhushu*, Volume Three
*Imperially Commissioned Siku Quanshu*
*Wuzhen Pian Zhushu Zhizhi Xiangshuo* [Appendix]
*Preface to Wuzhen Pian Zhizhi Xiangshuo*
By Weng Baoguang of the Song Dynasty

Before the manifestation of the primordial chaos, there was emptiness and silence, no name to be ascribed—only forcibly called the Dao. When the Dao descended, it generated the One *Qi*, neither moving nor still, neither turbid nor clear, vast and unfathomable. The sages, speaking with effort, called it the *Hunyuan Zhenyi* (Primordial True One) *Qi*. Once this *qi* divided, it transformed into yin and yang. Yin and yang are heaven and earth, male and female. Heaven and earth intermingle, and the myriad things are transformed and nurtured; male and female unite, and the myriad things are born. Thus, since the existence of heaven and earth, there has not been a single thing that did not attain its form through the union of yin and yang.

Those who seek to refine the elixir, if they take the images of metals, stones, grasses, and woods—naming the myriad different vessels—or even the essence, fluids, *qi*, blood, and humors of the body as the substance of the elixir, all these are post-celestial, turbid substances born of heaven and earth. Turbid substances have form and can be seen; how can they generate the formless and enter into the formless? Moreover, post-celestial things do not transcend the bounds of heaven and earth, and those with form inevitably decay. How can they transform and transcend beyond heaven and earth? If they do not transcend beyond heaven and earth, then those with form have never escaped the cycle of yin and yang, of life and death. Yang governs life, yin governs death; one dies, one lives, one departs, one returns—this is the natural principle. Even if one refines correctly, ingests efficaciously, and lives as long as Peng Zu or the Great Yu, when one’s allotted span is exhausted, there is no escape from death. Like an arrow shot into the sky, when its force is spent, it must fall. This is the principle that things with form inevitably decay.

Therefore, the sages gather the pre-celestial One *Qi* to refine the elixir, returning form to the One *Qi*, refining *qi* to merge with spirit, and refining spirit to unite with the Dao, thereby returning to the formless form. Thus, they transcend beyond heaven and earth, stand beyond creation, grasp yin and yang, and wield heaven and earth without being altered by the cycles of yin and yang, life and death—all through the power of the pre-celestial One *Qi*. Therefore, the elixir body becomes eternally numinous and enduring, neither arising nor ceasing. It is like moving a jar while inside it; to move the jar, one must be outside it. The True One *Qi* existed before heaven and earth, vast and unfathomable. The sages, using things of the same kind, enticed it to form the elixir—just as fire exists within the sun, and using a yang-sui (burning mirror) draws it forth to obtain the fire; or as water exists within the moon, and using a fang-zhu (moon mirror) draws it forth to obtain the water. Thus, refining things of the same kind, they established the furnace and tripod, calling them the True Dragon and True Tiger. As Master Lü’s verses say: "The natural furnace and tripod, the tiger encircling and the dragon coiling."

These things of the same kind are the emotionless emotion, the colorless color—the most numinous and noble among the myriad things, possessing the correct nature and life. If one gathers the initial *qi* of the same kind and employs it, it is called True Lead and True Mercury. The immortal elder said: "People of this age must recognize the true lead and mercury; they are not ordinary cinnabar or quicksilver, but the *qi* of the initial *qi* of lead and mercury." The "initial *qi*" refers to the upper and lower *qi*, the numbers two and eight. The dragon is called eight ounces, the tiger weighs half a catty—hence called the two and eight. This is because the water source is utterly pure, possessing *qi* but no substance. Using this *qi* to entice it, the True One *Qi* descends in numinosity and takes form. The immortal elder said: "The medicine meets the *qi* of the same kind and only then takes form; the Dao resides in emptiness and accords with nature."

To refine this Golden Elixir, first seek a propitious mountain and blessed land, then construct a few rooms for the elixir chamber. Build a three-tiered altar, erect a sword at the four sides, and hang mirrors. Then establish the Dragon and Tiger as the furnace and tripod, set up a water clock as the measure, and regulate the drawing and adding with the rules of water and fire. The operations require assistants and companions. Such matters are not easily expounded and also require worldly wealth to accomplish. Thus, Master Yin Zhenjun said: "To cultivate this Dao, one must have resources; without resources, the Golden Elixir cannot be refined." One also needs three companions—three like-minded friends of one heart and will.

On the night of the fifteenth of the eighth month, when the first yang stirs, the primary practitioner should step with the Yu step onto the altar, seize the Dragon with the left hand and the Tiger with the right, regulate the *qi*, await the proper time, align the stars, match yin and yang, and harmonize the breath with the water clock. Thus, metal and water unite, and the Dragon-Wood nurtures its essence. One sits in the tent, strategizing like a general weaving the warp and weft of the scriptures, ensuring the beginning and end are flawlessly executed, without the slightest error. Thus, the immortal elder said: "It all depends on the power of cultivation; the slightest deviation will fail to produce the elixir." Another secretly observes the water clock’s precision, meticulously adjusting the drawing and adding, preparing the fire work without missing the hexagrams or exceeding the time. If the moment is lost, the elixir will be difficult to complete. Thus, Chaoyuanzi said: "I urge you to exhaust the numbers of the celestial cycle; do not let the time slip by as the hexagrams hasten." The three work in unison, mutually confirming each other. In less than half a day, the True One *Qi* is obtained and returns to the Palace of Mutual Response, congealing into a grain as large as a millet seed, called the Golden Elixir. It resides in the North Sea, radiant and luminous, piercing through the curtains. Immediately, one wields the Moye sword to pursue it, and upon entering the mouth, one instantly ascends to the sacred position. Thus, the immortal elder said: "Swallowing a grain of the Golden Elixir, one then knows that my life is not determined by heaven." Once this grain is settled in the Cinnabar Field and Sea of *Qi*, the essence and fluids of the entire body converge and return to it, immediately forming cinnabar that does not dissipate. Then, one employs the fire to refine it into the Golden Liquid Returned Elixir. This fire is the *qi* of yin and yang.

The yang numbers are odd, the yin numbers even. From *zi* to *si*, the six celestial stems belong to yang, thus called the "yang fire." From *wu* to *hai*, the six celestial stems belong to yin, thus called the "yin tally." The *qiang* of *Qian* totals two hundred and sixteen, the *fang* of *Kun* totals one hundred and forty-four. Within these two hexagrams, one seizes four thousand three hundred and twenty years of primordial *qi*, which returns to my Cinnabar Field, warming and nurturing the "child pearl" until the sacred embryo is formed.

The Old Lord said: "The odd yang arises from *zi*, the even yin emerges from *wu*. Beginning and ending within *Qian* and *Kun*, it is like the gestation of a fetus in the womb. Thus, externally, one harmonizes with the fire of yin and yang, while internally, the essence of the Golden Liquid is born. Without need for added effort, it naturally circulates, ascending from the *Weilü* with a distinct sound, piercing through the twin towers, rising in reverse to the summit of *Niwan*, then descending into the mouth—its form like a sparrow’s egg, fragrant and sweet. This is the Golden Liquid Returned Elixir."

Slowly swallowing it down to the Cinnabar Field, the sacred embryo is formed, and the infant is nurtured. Thus, the immortal elder said: "The infant is one, containing true fluids. After ten months, the embryo is complete, and one enters the foundation of the sacred. Just as the mortal embryo is born after ten months, so too is the sacred embryo. After ten months, the fire is complete, the work is done, and one sheds the embryo to transform into a body of pure yang. Cold, heat, hunger, and thirst can no longer disturb. Only then may one retreat into deep mountains and secluded valleys, or dwell in humble and remote places, facing the wall for nine years to empty the heart. With no self and no others, the mind remains as it was—this is called the immortal embracing the One."

When the true monk gathers the ox, only those who recognize the heart and see their nature can embrace the One, and thus this Dao is perfected. After nine years of work, the nature of non-action is spontaneously perfected, wisdom naturally arises, the body of pure yang is inherently wondrous, and the spirit inherently numinous. Thus, nature and life unite with the Dao, becoming true yet formless.

The formless form manifests according to circumstances: encountering wind, it becomes wind; encountering rain, it becomes rain; encountering water or fire, it becomes water or fire. It transforms unpredictably—now present, now gone—seen ahead, suddenly behind. Thus, it can divide its body into a hundred billion, responding without limit. Like the moon reflecting in ten thousand waters, it is universally present. Therefore, it responds to conditions and answers calls without fail. Yet its true body abides in the realm of utmost stillness, never acting. This is the union of spirit, form, nature, and life with the Dao, returning together to the ultimate source of emptiness and quiescence.

Thus, the sages forcibly name it the "Nine-Turn Golden Liquid Great Returned Elixir," or the "Vajra Indestructible Body," the supreme and most true wondrous Dao. The immortal elder alone perfected this Dao, attaining a body of true gold and wondrous hue, manifesting its majestic and luminous golden compassionate form universally across the Dharma realm to save and deliver sentient beings. To his disciple Liu Fengzhen, he revealed the nature Dao as unborn, entering quiescence, yet later manifested his true body in Wangwu Mountain. He demonstrated the life Dao as indestructible, achieving perfect penetration. In the fifth year of Yuanfeng, on the fifth day of the third month, at the time of his liberation by means of the corpse, he left a gatha:

*"The wondrous function of the one spirit pervades the Dharma realm,
This is not the Dao of nature and life both perfected,
Nor the true union of form and spirit both wondrous—
How could one attain this?"*

He had lived in the world for ninety-six years. In his lifetime, he broadly expounded the profound and subtle, composing verses that refined emotions and nature, his words profound and elegant. He drew in later generations, entitling his work *Awakening to Reality*. "Awakening to Reality" refers to the truth of nature and life.

Yet he reflected that later students knew only the life Dao but not how to exhaust their nature, or knew only the nature Dao but not how to nurture their life. Thus, he composed a verse on awakening to the true suchness and a hymn on the wondrous treasure of the colored body, to enlighten those of superior wisdom and great capacity, enabling them to fully comprehend the Dao of nature and life, attain ultimate perfection and penetration, and transcend the three realms. This was not something achievable by those lacking the great compassion of unimpeded wisdom and perfect illumination.

Though my understanding is dim and obscured, I have received the immortal elder’s secret transmission. Through diligent study of this work, I have revealed eight or nine parts of its true mechanism. Fearing that those of like aspiration might not recognize the source and flow of the Golden Elixir, I trace its origin and essentials, daring to offend heavenly judgment by directly pointing to the broad path of *Awakening to Reality*. If there are those with innate affinity for immortality, they may directly enter the gate of *Awakening to Reality* and seek non-action in the millet-sized pearl. If sought externally, one cannot hope to attain it.

In ancient times, the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning suspended a precious pearl, as large as a millet grain, in the empty void. Innumerable sacred assemblies eagerly entered through the pearl’s opening—this is the single grain of the Golden Elixir. A grain like a millet contains all phenomena, encompassing the three powers. It is boundless in its vastness, infinitesimal in its smallness. From antiquity to the present, countless perfected beings and supreme sages have realized this Dao—who has not attained the supreme great Dao through this single millet grain?

This Dao is most simple and most easy. Without the guidance of a true teacher, none can fathom its profound roots and firm foundation. Even with roots and foundation recognized, without great wealth and power, none can accomplish the work and manifest the affair. Even with work and affair manifested, without clarity of heart and insight into nature, none can attain the wondrousness of embracing the One. Once the One is embraced in wondrousness, the Dao of nature and life is perfected—nothing more can be added.

Thus, the life Dao is invariably transmitted through a teacher’s guidance, then illuminated through cultivation and practice. As for the nature Dao, it is not something that comes from without. If one relies on external perceptions, knowledge, and learning, one falls into the lesser rules and fails to penetrate the utmost clarity of hearing and seeing. Only by self-awakening and self-illumination within one’s own heart can one fully realize the nature Dao and attain what is called the "supreme first vehicle."

Alas! Within the nature Dao, there is no awakening to awaken, no illumination to illuminate—only the absence of awakening and the absence of illumination. There is no exhaustion to exhaust, no attainment to attain—only the absence of exhaustion and the absence of attainment. The "supreme first" is above nothing, the "one" is without oneness. If a student receives the teacher’s transmission, grasps the celestial mechanism, refines the spirit elixir, sheds the embryo and changes the bones, further clarifies the heart and reaches the origin, awakens to true emptiness, and directly transcends to the supreme vehicle, entering the realm of non-action, then form and spirit are both wondrous, nature and life are both perfected. Riding the phoenix and chariot, mounting the dragon and phoenix, they will surely roam together in Penglai and Langfeng.

The art of strengthening the army and securing victory—this is the method of refining the Golden Elixir.

The practice of refining the Golden Elixir always begins at the first movement of yang on the night of the Mid-Autumn Festival, seated in steadfastness upon the altar of the Celestial Dipper, ascending three tiers. To the left, one seizes the Dragon to examine and stabilize the crucible; to the right, one grasps the Tiger to precisely regulate the firing times. Civil and martial forces contend in battle at the Gate of Mystery; departing and returning, they fiercely struggle at the Gate of the Feminine. The breath tally and water clock must correspond to the revolutions of the celestial cycle without the slightest deviation—thus it is called the method of strengthening the army and securing victory. The "army" is the Dragon and Tiger; the "battle" is their union. Within a single two-hour period, six grains of the Golden Elixir are obtained and taken into the mouth—this is the method of securing victory. As the *Scripture of Western Splendor* states: "Strengthening the army and securing victory lies in the work of nurturing the Mystery Pearl." Therefore, the immortal elders first arranged sixteen regulated poems to clarify the respective eights of Dragon and Tiger. A single five-character quatrain signifies that within one period, a single grain of the Golden Elixir is obtained. This is why I have divided it into the upper volume, presenting it to elucidate the method of strengthening the army and securing victory—thus the work of gathering the Golden Elixir shines forth in clarity.

The method of enriching the state and pacifying the people: the practice of circulating the yin-yang tally and firing times.

The Great Dao is formless, giving rise to the primordial qi. This qi, in its chaotic state, divides into yin and yang. The purest yang qi, light and clear, ascends to cover above—this is called Heaven. The purest yin qi, heavy and turbid, descends to bear below—this is called Earth. The accumulation of pure yang qi that soars upward to Heaven becomes the immortal.

The accumulation of pure yin qi that sinks and dissolves into Earth becomes the demon. The body that receives both yin and yang qi, neither ascending nor sinking, dwelling between Heaven and Earth—capable of becoming either immortal or demon—is the human. If one cultivates and refines, stripping away all yin to transform the form into pure yang qi, one ascends as an immortal. If, unaware of cultivation, one daily depletes primordial yang until the body transforms into pure yin qi, one becomes a lower demon. The *Yijing* states: "That which is rooted in Heaven inclines upward; that which is rooted in Earth inclines downward"—each follows its own numerical destiny. Thus, the sage, gazing upward and downward, knows that humans receive the essence of Heaven and Earth, making them the most numinous and noble. Therefore, they borrow the two substances of true yin and true yang to seize the primal qi of Heaven and Earth before their division, forming the elixir to return to the Cinnabar Field and Sea of Qi, thereby governing the postnatal qi of the entire body. Then, the qi of the entire body converges as if the myriad states paying homage to the sovereign or the stars encircling the North Star.

Knowing that humans first arise from the essence of their parents’ union, they thus steal the pure qi of yin and yang as the foundation for transformation, called the "yin tally and yang fire." Circulating within the sixty-four hexagrams, cycling endlessly, revolving the seventy-two seasonal nodes and twenty-four solar terms within a single day and night, they seize the four thousand three hundred and sixty grains of upright qi, converging them within the Cinnabar Field and Sea of Qi to warm and nurture the elixir pearl. The elixir, abiding in the Central Palace, remains quiescent and non-active, thus externally connecting with the yin tally and yang fire while internally generating the true unity of the numinous body. After ten months of gestation, the form transforms into pure yang qi, beyond hunger and thirst, unassailed by cold or heat—hence the method of enriching the state and pacifying the people.

The state is the body; the people are the essence and qi. The people are the root of the state; when the root is firm, the state is secure. Without a ruler, the people have no refuge; without ministers, the people have no governance. Thus, the sage takes the elixir as the ruler and fire as the minister. When elixir and fire mutually support each other, ruler and minister rejoice in harmony, and the world is at peace. When the root is firm, the people are at ease, and the state of the body is enriched. The *Xihua Jing* states: "When essence is complete and qi is sufficient, the state is enriched and the people are pacified"—this is precisely the result of ingesting the Golden Elixir.

Thus, the immortal elder continues with sixty-four quatrains, corresponding to the sixty-four hexagrams of the *Zhouyi*, to elucidate the numerical progression of firing the lines. He further composes twelve *Xijiang Yue* lyrics, symbolizing the twelve months of firing and bathing. This is why I have divided it into the middle volume, to clarify the method of firing and the intent of enriching the state and pacifying the people. The sequence of elixir cultivation should indeed proceed thus.

**The Dao of the Immortal Embracing the One**

The Dao of the immortal embracing the One is the time when the sage’s firing practice reaches completion, and the form transforms into pure yang qi. Then, one retreats to a secluded corner, faces the wall for nine years, and embraces the One to empty the heart. When the heart is settled, the spirit transforms, uniting with the Dao—this is called "embracing the One." Thus it is said: The Dao is the root of nature; nature is the source of the heart. Heart and nature share the same substance, transforming boundlessly. The common people use it daily, calling it "natural." If one can awaken to it, forget images and words, empty the heart and fill the belly, and embrace the One to advance in practice, after nine transformations, one attains immortality—this is its principle.

The nine transformations are nine years—the number nine is the extreme of yang. The One is the potent name for the Dao. Embracing is holding that which cannot be held.

At this moment of attaining immortality, the adept dissolves the limbs, stills the senses, severs worldly dust, equalizes self and other, relinquishes fixation, certainty, grasping, and rejection—heart and realm become one, wandering freely and at ease. Thus, when cosmic serenity stabilizes, the light of Heaven emerges. After nine years of practice, the nature of non-action becomes perfectly rounded, the formless spirit attains wondrous subtlety. When the spirit is wondrous, transformations are boundless, profound and unfathomable; when nature is rounded, wisdom illuminates the ten directions, spirit pervades without obstruction. Hence, the adept may divide the body into a hundred billion, manifesting without limit—yet the essence of utmost reality abides in the realm of perfect stillness, silent and without any agent of action. Here, spirit, form, nature, and life all unite with the Dao in truth. This is called the "Way of Embracing the One."

Of old, after the immortal elder attained the Dao, he demonstrated to his disciple Liu Fengzhen the entry into quiescence through non-arising. Having entered quiescence, he then manifested his form in Wangwu Mountain—this is the very Way. Of old, after the Tathāgata entered nirvāṇa, his golden coffin arose into the sky, and the threefold fire consumed his body. Yet, when his mother’s weeping did not cease, he again manifested his golden form in the sky, speaking half a verse—this, too, is the same Way. Of old, after Bodhidharma faced the wall for nine years and entered extinction, he carried his single sandal west, and Puhua immolated his body in towering flames. Yet the sound of his bell still shook the sky. Such exemplars are not easily encompassed. If nature and life were not both rounded, form and spirit not both wondrous, who could achieve this?

Thus, the immortal elder concluded his scroll by revealing that the Chan school’s teaching of nature and Dao truly elucidates the Way of Embracing the One. Therefore, I have divided this into a lower volume.

The Way of nature is vast, empty, and boundless—dim, obscure, beyond all form and description. Humans and non-humans are all equal, without high or low. Since beginningless time, whether in forms with names or in nameless formlessness, not a single thing fails to be perfectly complete and sufficient, for its original essence is inherently pure and complete. Thus, there has never been anything that could be described or expressed in words. Yet the Great Treasury contains fifty-four hundred and eight scrolls—all these are the sages’ compelled speech, born of humanity’s profound darkness regarding the Dao. They speak so that people may, through words, awaken to the Dao. Once the Dao is awakened, words themselves become non-existent.

Thus, the *Vajracchedikā Sūtra* states: "If one claims the Tathāgata has expounded the Dharma, this is slander of the Buddha." Therefore, all speech is slander. Now, the immortal elder’s songs and verses on nature and Dao are also compelled speech—already superfluous. This is why I do not further interpret them, lest I draw legs on a snake.

I only wish that the ardent and enlightened may not seek externally but awaken directly within their own hearts, illumining uniquely and bearing the transmission without hesitation. Whether in clamor or silence, speech or stillness, taverns or brothels—it is thus. Whether not thus, whether in every place without distinction, harmonizing all the worlds of the ten directions with a single eye, extending a single hand, the wondrous function pervades all directions, covering heaven and earth. Wherever one moves, it is the real; whatever one does, there is nothing it cannot accomplish. Then one knows that here, the original nature is inherently complete, lacking nothing, needing no deliberation. All abilities are forgotten, all questions and responses, thoughts and concerns—even the word "nature" itself is no longer needed.

The Esoteric Essentials of the Three Vehicles: Poetry on the Golden Elixir

**Great indeed is the single millet grain—**
From the Void it descends, from the Origin it flows,
Returning to form at the first hexagram’s dawn.
Two halves of Qian and Kun draw upon creation’s power,
A single catty spun by the pivot of sun and moon.
The subtle count of stellar breaths, the faintest reckoning—
Advance the fire with divine skill, its signs precise.
When the blaze of the half-hour’s civil and martial flames subsides,
The Crimson Dragon yields the luminous night-shining pearl.

**Method of Circulating the Fire**
Once the single pearl is ingested, earth joins heaven,
Rain gathers at the Mysterious Pass, the fire blazes bright.
Sixty hexagrams cycle through dawn and dusk,
Within the ninefold city, mercury burns, lead is drawn.
In adding and withdrawing, guard against peril;
In bathing, halt the talisman to prevent smoke.
When the work is complete and the embryo shed,
After ten months of nurturing within the Void,
A Great Luo Immortal is born.

**Method of Embracing the One**
The elixir is but the trap, the Dao the fish—
Forget the trap to attain the Dao, realize emptiness.
Do not cling fast to embracing non-action.
Shatter the Void, and the One is also none.
Yet wondrous being’s numinous radiance ever blazes,
Encompassing the Dharma Realm with effortless ease.
Following conditions, responding to stimuli, ever pure—
After nine years, the vajra body becomes indestructible.

**Preface**
Now, those who roam the vast clouds and ascend to the golden palaces—
Their words remain in the sacred texts, their deeds transcend the dusty world.
Yet worldly folk cannot deeply believe.
I have observed the *Preface to the Collected Immortals*:
Since ancient times, those who soared aloft number over a hundred thousand,
Those who raised their households to ascend, over eighty families.
Liu Xiang, foremost Confucian of the Han, also composed the *Biographies of the Immortals* to bequeath to later generations.
Thus, the reality of divine transcendents is no fabrication.

Yet why do worldly folk disbelieve?
For no other reason than this:
The celestial mechanism is profoundly mysterious,
The secrets of immortals and sages are hidden.
Worldly learning is shallow, human sincerity fleeting—
No wonder their ears do not grasp it.

The *Classic of Constant Purity and Stillness* begins:
"The Great Dao is formless, yet gives birth to heaven and earth;
The Great Dao is passionless, yet moves the sun and moon,
Nurturing the myriad things, shaping all beings,
Returning at last to the primal, nameless origin."
The profound beneficence of the ancient sages toward humanity is thus.

They further expounded the principles of heaven and earth, male and female, purity and turbidity, movement and stillness,
Elaborating on the wonders of a tranquil mind and few desires,
Ever abiding in profound stillness—
All to reveal the celestial mechanism and secretly point to the Mysterious Barrier.

By the end of the text, those who can awaken may transmit the sagely Dao,
Attaining the ultimate teachings from the immortal Master Ge’s words—
Passed mouth to mouth, never recorded in writing.
Alas! Once the pure wind departed, worldly customs grew shallow,
The dust of immortality became distant, this Dao was lost.
Though heterodox doctrines abound, all return to the same distant source.
Thus, methods of gathering mercury and extracting lead were not inscribed on bamboo or silk,
The wonders of forming the embryo and nurturing the infant were deeply sealed in golden caskets and jade boxes.
Students of immortality, though white-haired from lifelong study,
Could never glimpse even a shadow of it.

In the prosperous Song dynasty, extraordinary figures emerged.
The Purple Mystery Perfected, Master Zhang,
From youth practiced grain avoidance, endowed with numinous bones,
Resolute and diligent, never faltering in hardship,
Attained the Dao from the Elder of Mount Qingcheng,
Mastering all the profound secrets of the Golden Elixir.
He expressed his encounters in songs and poems,
Naming his work the *Awakening to Reality*.
I obtained and read it, pondering deeply,
Consulting various doctrines, yet found no enlightenment.
Some dismissed it as mere furnace techniques,
Others misconstrued it as inner alchemy for sexual practices.
I sighed over the text for years,
Fortunate at last to encounter the Purple Yang Immortal Elder, Master Chen,
Who personally transmitted the *Awakening to Reality*.
The Perfected Sun Wuming elucidated its secrets, secretly imparting them.
After ablutions and purification, I recited it—
Suddenly, like mist dispersing and clouds parting,
The sun shone, the moon brightened.
The oral instructions and essentials of the heart—
Without daring to inquire further, I already knew
The mechanism of generating heaven and earth,
The Dao of moving the sun and moon,
The nurturing of the myriad things, the shaping of all beings—
All arise from true yin and true yang,
The qi of the upper and lower crucibles.
As for their application—adding and withdrawing, guarding against danger—
All became brilliantly clear before my eyes.
If one can encounter a true teacher and attain this wondrous Dao,
Nurturing the immortal embryo, transcending the mundane to enter sageliness—
Surely this life will not have been lived in vain.

Just beginning to grasp it, I leapt with joy,
Reverently following the guidance to inscribe this at the end of the scroll.
Written on the Mid-Autumn Festival of the Jiazi year of the Jiatai era of the Song,
Respectfully by Baiyunzi.

**Origins and Events of the *Awakening to Reality***

**The Origins of Perfected Zhang**
The Purple Yang Perfected was from Yingluo Street in Tiantai.
Originally named Boduan, styled Pingshu, later renamed Yongcheng.
In youth, he studied all texts, wandering like clouds and water.
In later years, he transmitted the Dao of the Primordial Origin,
Yet its subtlest aspects remained incomplete.
Diligently, he sought and inquired, traveling all directions.
During the Xining era, when Lord Lu the Academician governed Chengdu,
He followed him to Shu, serving as a military advisor in the Sichuan Pacification Office.
In the Jiyou year, he encountered an extraordinary figure
Who transmitted the secrets of fire timing—
Thus his Dao was accomplished.
The master admonished him:
"One day, if someone comes to free you from your bonds, accept them."

Later, with each transmission, he suffered calamities,
Deeply repenting and blaming himself.
He withdrew from the world, forgetting words,
Composing the *Awakening to Reality* in eighty-one chapters,
Exhaustively expounding the secrets of the two elixirs.
His discussions were profound, vehemently criticizing
Worldly scholars who clung to sectarian divisions,
Unable to unify the three teachings or fathom
The principle of different paths converging at the same source.
He vigorously corrected and supplemented the Dao,
His work circulated throughout the world.

During the Yuanfeng era, with Liu Fengzhen and his disciples,
He widely propagated Buddhist teachings,
Leaving a verse on non-arising before entering quiescence.
Liu’s disciples cremated his remains,
Obtaining hundreds of relics like chicken-head fruit,
All deep blue in color.
Seven years later, Fengzhen arrived at Mount Wangwu,
Again meeting the Immortal Elder as before—
Further demonstrating his wondrous attainment in both form and spirit,
The perfection of both nature and life.

During the Zhenghe era, he revealed his name to Huang Mianzhong, the Minister,
In Yanping.
Huang had long transmitted the Dao of Rongcheng,
Passionately devoted to furnace techniques,
Though advanced in years.
Their words did not resonate, and he departed.
Later, he sent a letter to Huang,
Narrating extraordinary events.
Huang’s grandson, Quan, saw the letter but kept it secret,
Revealing only to me its general purport:
Pingshu claimed that he and Huang were both celestial officials of the Purple Tenuity,
Numbered among the Nine August Perfected.
Due to reviewing the records of kalpa cycles,
They were banished to the human realm.
Now, only six stars of the Purple Tenuity remain visible,
Three still concealed in obscurity—
Pingshu, Mianzhong, and Master Yu.

Pingshu was the Purple Yang Perfected,
Mianzhong the Purple Origin Perfected,
Master Yu the Purple Florescence Perfected.
All those banished as officials have already returned to the Celestial Capital,
Yet Pingshu alone ascended as an immortal,
While Mianzhong remains mired in the sea of officialdom.
In each human life, he has undergone ten rebirths—
Nine have passed.
If in the next life he again succumbs to delusion and joins the dust,
He will sink into other destinies, with no hope of ascending as an immortal.
Pingshu clearly recounted their immortal pact,
Striving to deliver him,
Yet Huang ultimately failed to resonate and passed away,
Merely styling himself the Purple Origin Elder.
The Nine August are not recorded in the celestial offices—
They are but faint stars.

Beyond the nameless that may yet be named—does this lie within the twelve thousand five hundred?

**The Affairs of Monk Zixian**

Daoguang, surnamed Xue, named Shi, styled Daoyuan, was a native of Jizu Mountain in Shanfu. Originally a monk, his Dharma name was Zixian. Wandering to Chang’an, he stayed at Kaifu Temple, where he sought the elder Xiuyan. Xiuyan asked, "When the golden rooster has yet to crow, how is there no sound?" Later, he studied under the monk Ruhuan, who posed, "What is the discourse that transcends the Buddhas and Patriarchs?" Zixian replied, "A sesame cake, round and full." Upon hearing the creak of a well-sweep, he suddenly awakened. He composed a verse:

*Creak upon creak, the sound arises—*
*Not from another it is gained.*
*Suddenly, the well-sweep reveals*
*The song of no-birth in full.*
*Beware the mud-snake’s dance,*
*The pomegranate branch’s sway.*

The two elders affirmed his insight. From then on, he swiftly grasped the supreme, secret, and perfect essentials of the true Dharma, his wit sharp and his mastery of both Chan discourse and doctrine profound. Years passed thus.

One day, he realized that all the above were but affairs of this shore—that even if his eloquence flowed like a hanging river, it was still but Chan talk and Daoist discourse. Sitting motionless for kalpas on end, he could never nurture life or attain longevity. Even Bodhidharma, though enlightened, had to journey to the Eastern Land to fulfill the Way. The Sixth Patriarch, though awakened to his nature, still sought transmission at Huangmei. How could these two masters have stopped at such things?

Moreover, his refined aspiration turned to the Dao of golden elixir and the cultivation of life. There must be secret wonders therein. He devoted himself to seeking and inquiring. In the winter of the bingxu year of the Chongning era, he lodged in a Buddhist temple in Qing Town, Meixian County, where he attended a lecture. There, he encountered the Daoist Shi Tai, styled Dezhi, of Apricot Grove Post in Fufeng County, Fengxiang Prefecture. Though eighty-five years old, his hair remained black, his complexion ruddy, and his bearing extraordinary. At night, he sewed his own robes. Daoyuan observed him in secret and felt something unusual. One day, he casually recited a poem by Zhang Pingshu. Shi suddenly exclaimed, "Do you know this man?"

"My master!" He then explained the circumstances: "Master Pingshu’s former name was Boduan. Initially, in Chengdu, he lodged at Tianhui Temple, where he encountered an extraordinary person who changed his name to Yongcheng and transmitted to him the oral instructions of the elixir. Later, for leaking and recklessly transmitting them, he incurred punishment. The governor of Fengzhou, enraged, pressed charges against him, and he was sentenced to penal tattooing and exile. Passing through Bin territory, a heavy snowstorm struck, and he drank wine at a village tavern with his escorts. I happened to be in the tavern as well. After exchanging bows, I was invited to join their table. Observing their merriment, I smiled and said to the escort, 'These guests are already merry, but that guest has not yet begun drinking. Why not invite him to join you?' Thus, the escort drank heartily and asked the reason for his journey. When he explained everything, I thought to myself, 'The governor of Bin is an old friend of mine—fond of virtue and indifferent to rank. He would not mind traveling a hundred *li*.' I said to Pingshu, 'If you are willing to detour to visit him, there may be a chance to avoid this journey.' I earnestly pleaded with the escorts, and they agreed. Together, we went to Bin. I went ahead, and upon meeting the governor, Pingshu was pardoned. Grateful, he said, 'To not repay this kindness would be inhuman! You have studied the Dao all your life yet heard nothing of its attainment. Now, I shall transmit the elixir method to you. Follow it in cultivation to achieve the Dao.' I bowed in reverence, received his instructions, and vowed to uphold them.

After hearing Shi Tai’s account, Daoyuan immediately aroused sincere faith, prostrated himself, and took refuge. He requested to become his disciple and ultimately mastered the Great Elixir, receiving all its oral instructions and essentials. Shi Tai warned him, 'This is not something to be lightly shared with those of great wealth or external defenses, for it easily invites slander. Go swiftly to a bustling city and rely on those of virtue and power to carry it out.' Daoyuan then discarded his monastic robes, donned a scholar’s cap and wide-sleeved robe, and came to the capital. Veiling his light and blending with the dust, he mingled among ordinary folk, hoping to complete this endeavor. Yet, among those who study the Daoist path, upon encountering Pingshu’s poems, their interpretations diverged, and their doubts multiplied, leading to confusion and error. Many dared not even attempt cultivation until death. Alas! Was this Master Pingshu’s original intent?

Thus, I was moved to first clarify and expound its principles, unravel its mysteries, and illuminate its subtleties, making it accessible so that cultivators might avoid mistakes and attain the rank of lofty immortals, mastering the wondrous workings of the elixir. Initially, Master Pingshu, having once incurred punishment, vowed never to teach others. Later, he sighed, 'This is self-preservation, not the Way.' The *Supreme Clarity’s Mysterious Statutes* states: 'To meet someone and not transmit is to lose the Heavenly Dao; to recklessly transmit to the unworthy is to leak the Heavenly Treasure. Transmitting to the right person brings merit to oneself; reckless transmission brings calamity to the seven ancestors.' I have been overly secretive, violating the Heavenly Dao. Disaster looms! Reluctantly, I composed these poems to circulate among the world’s extraordinary people, that they might read and awaken to their meaning. Yet the poems’ depths are profound and obscure, difficult to grasp. Daoyuan thus expanded their meaning into annotations, clearly revealing the true essentials and thoroughly elucidating the mysterious subtleties of the method, leaving no hidden depths. Those who obtain this text may study it in detail, resolve their doubts without inquiry, and attain self-realization—thus fulfilling Master Pingshu’s intent.

Yet, having resolved to save the world and transmit this to later generations, Daoyuan must henceforth remain silent. Those who obtain this text should guard it closely. The treasure of Heaven is protected everywhere by divine beings. If there are those of sincere aspiration, who believe in the Dao, understand the truth, and conduct themselves without flaw, then and only then may it be transmitted. It must not be shared among piles of gold and jade, nor even with one’s closest kin. For careless leakage brings misfortune upon oneself, disaster upon one’s household, and inauspiciousness to one’s descendants. Not only this—it will extend calamity to the nine mysteries and seven ancestors, subjecting them to karmic retribution and long servitude in the offices of ghosts, never to be reborn. Bear this in mind and be cautious! Do not be negligent.

Now, this elder, Yuan Zhenyi of Shangqiu, has transcribed the annotations of the *Wuzhen Pian* poems, along with the events of their transmission at the time, and compiled them in detail below. Though the language is unadorned, it is a faithful record, fully presenting the beginning and end.

Recorded on the Mid-Autumn Festival of the *yiwei* year of the Zhenghe era.

---

**Annotations on the *Wuzhen Pian*: Discernment**

In the *dingmao* year of the Taiding era, in Ruiyang, I saw Xue Zixian’s annotations on the *Wuzhen Pian* and read them with regret, having not yet seen the complete edition. In the *jisi* year of the Tianli era, upon returning to Sheng, I obtained the full text and read it repeatedly for years, discerning its patterns. Later, I received several copies from distant Daoist friends, collated them, and found them identical. The annotations cited by other schools sometimes attributed passages to 'the Master' or 'Ye Wenshu'—this was one point of doubt. Recently published editions of the *Wuzhen Pian* include annotations by Xiangchuan Weng and Wumingzi, which, when compared to the annotations I obtained from Zixian, were also identical. Yet the texts were the same while the authors differed—this was another point of doubt.

In the *renxu* year of the Jiatai era, Yuan Gongfu condemned Wenshu’s annotations as chaotic and difficult to verify. Yet Gongfu’s own teachings amounted to nothing more than solitary cultivation of a single substance—why then condemn others? Was Wenshu truly at fault? Why did both Zixian and Gongfu criticize him? This was yet another point of doubt."

Having examined the dates, I found that in the *Fu Ming Pian*, Daoguang wrote in his preface that he received oral instructions from a master in the *gengzi* year of the Xuanhe era. Today, in Shangqiu, Jin Shiweng of the Yuan dynasty and Wang Zhenyi of the Zhenghe *yiwei* year recorded Xue Zixian’s deeds. Ye Wenshu’s annotations date to the thirty-first year of the Shaoxing era, *xinsi*—forty-seven years apart. In the Zhenghe *yiwei* year, Wenshu may not yet have been born or was still a child. How, then, could Zixian have been named and criticized forty-seven years prior? Moreover, all such errors and distortions were Wenshu’s own, not the work of others. This was yet another point of doubt.

Given these several doubts, I suspected the annotations were not Zixian’s, though I had not yet reached a conclusion. Yet his commentary, unlike that of other schools, truly grasped the Perfected One’s subtleties. On the third day of the fifth month in the *xinwei* year of the Zhishun era, I encountered the authentic oral instructions on the elixir’s ingredients, firing times, and true transmission—heaven’s gift. Still, I could not dispel my doubt that these were not Zixian’s annotations, and so I continued my inquiries, seeking answers far and wide.

In the autumn of the *renshen* year of the Zhishun era, an old friend from Wuling transmitted to me Xiangchuan Weng’s *Baoguang Jie*. Overjoyed, I read it for months, and my former doubts dissolved like melting ice. It became clear that the annotations commonly attributed to Zixian were in fact those of Wumingzi. How had the error—mistaking *Baoguang* for *Daoguang*—persisted so long without correction?

How do I know this? The Perfected One transmitted his teachings to Shi Xinglin, and Xinglin to Zixian—this is the third generation, known to all. The Perfected One also transmitted to Guangyizi, and Guangyizi to Wumingzi—this is likewise the third generation, though few know it. Those who sought credibility for their annotations linked Wumingzi’s commentary to the lineage, appending Zixian’s deeds to lend authority. The record states: "Yuan Wang Zhenyi"—but what Yuan surname exists? This was a fabrication to deceive the world.

Some say Zixian was a monk, also named Daoguang or Baoguang—another error, conflating two men into one due to the shared character *guang*. As for the criticism of Ye Wenshu by name: before Wenshu, no one had annotated the *Wuzhen Pian*; after Wenshu, no one had refuted his errors. Wumingzi, fearing the loss of the Perfected One’s subtleties and the misguidance of later generations, risked heavenly retribution in the *yisi* year of the Qiandao era. Following his master’s instructions, he annotated the text with meticulous clarity, lest others stray. His compassion was boundless, yet he fully revealed heaven’s mysteries.

Later generations, excerpting these commentaries without seeing the full text, further distorted the record: misreading *Weng* as a term of respect for the elderly, splitting Xiangchuan Weng and Wumingzi into two people, and erroneously attributing Wumingzi’s annotations to Zixian. Error compounded error, and even the dates and textual meanings could not be verified—how could they hope to grasp the true transmission of the immortal Dao?

Alas, the authentic lineage of the Golden Elixir’s great Dao has long been severed.

Now, as the realm is unified and those who study immortality abound, how few among them have truly heard this Dao! Is it that Zixian’s annotations have not been transmitted to later generations? Or is it that I, in my isolation, have simply not encountered them? Yet the annotations of Wumingzi are exhaustive, leaving no depths unplumbed, while the purported annotations of Zixian, as transmitted, are largely identical and lack nothing—had Zixian truly written them, how could Wumingzi fail to cite his words and instead plagiarize them entirely, seeking to replace his name and pass them off as his own? In explaining the meaning of the full moon, Wumingzi merely quotes two lines from Zixian, which clearly shows that Zixian never composed such annotations. The current misattribution of these notes to Zixian began with the annotations of one Youzuoren, who, when citing *Wu Shi Zi*, wrote *Wu Shi* instead—a corruption of *Wuming*. This further proves that Zixian never wrote such annotations.

Those who study immortality today cannot weigh the relative importance of Zixian’s renown against the obscurity of Wumingzi. Yet the authentic transmission of the immortal Dao from their masters is identical for both—they both received it from the True Man Pingshu. Where such texts exist, divine forces guard and protect them; how could one not treasure these writings and preserve them carefully, selecting the right people to transmit them? Thus, I have appended here the true origins of the True Man and the deeds of Zixian to the annotations of Wumingzi, clarifying all matters so that those who study these commentaries may easily grasp their principles, correct errors, and recognize the truth of my words. I dare not falsify the transmission of these annotations, nor dare I lightly transmit them to the unworthy.

Those who study immortality must have the karmic affinity to do so; through the text, they comprehend its meaning, and through the annotations, they grasp its guidance, avoiding heterodox paths and directly ascending to the great Dao. If heaven deems it fitting, then the great Dao of the Golden Elixir has never truly been severed. Yet another version of this text, circulating separately, bears a preface by Zixuzi dated the ninth month of the first year of the Chunxi era, placed before Chen Ziyang’s preface. This version omits the passage where Wumingzi states he "meticulously followed the immortal elder’s secret instructions," alters the subsequent text, and redistributes the *Three Vehicles’ Secret Essentials* to the beginning of each volume. It further adds annotations claiming that the essentials lie in using virgin boys and girls as yin and yang, dragon and tiger; that male and female qi constitute pre-heaven and post-heaven; that lead and mercury are true water and fire; that the initial flourishing occurs at the age of heavenly water (tiankui); that the generation of *gui* at sixteen marks the completion of the three yang; that the full moon’s light is the perfect golden crucible; that "great and small unharmed" means the two realms are whole; and that pre-heaven qi is the external medicine—truly the perverse teachings of a deviant sect, falsely annotated!

This is the heretical doctrine of Zixuzi, who dared not reveal his true name and instead preemptively dated his preface, falsely attributing it to Wumingzi without stating his own lineage, seeking to deceive the world. Some say Zixuzi is merely another name for Wumingzi, but if this were true, the names would contradict one another. Moreover, the year *guisi* of the Qiandao era was followed by *jiawu*, the first year of the Chunxi era—within a single year, the transmission of the master’s instructions would have diverged so drastically. How can this be explained? In the *jiazi* year of the Jiatai era, Baiyunzi’s preface states that Chen Ziyang first transmitted these annotations, thirty-two years after the original text. The annotations remain entirely consistent, the secret instructions clear and unambiguous, without a single erroneous or adulterated character. From *guisi* to *jiawu*, barely a month passed—had Wumingzi seen such a corrupted version before his ascension, he would surely have condemned it as heretical. How could he have attacked Ye Wenshu while upholding Zixuzi?

Furthermore, why did Zixuzi not seek the guidance of a true master to correct his errors? Had his transmission been authentic, Wumingzi would have amended it—why then would he add to Wumingzi’s unspoken instructions? This confirms the falsity of his annotations. The truth is clear.

Those among the Dao-seeking scholars fortunate enough to obtain the true essence of these annotations should discern it with clarity and treasure it well. In the *bingzi* year of the Zhiyuan era, on the Zhongyuan festival, Kongxuanzi Dai Qizong, styled Zhongtongfu, respectfully presents this postscript.

I have heard that in ancient times, there was the Perfected One Ziyang, who expounded the subtleties of the Great Dao and rescued deluded followers from drowning. On the day of his Dao’s fulfillment, he composed the *Wuzhen Pian* to transmit to the world—all his life’s experiences were distilled therein. Those who study the Dao yet do not follow the teachings of this text are like travelers bound for the rivers and seas who abandon the oars of cinnabar.

Alas, as the ages grow distant and the winds of the Dao weaken, words become tangled, and heterodox paths cling stubbornly, slandering the immortal way. The true principles are deeply obscured, and false interpretations deny the authentic teachings. Thus, the Way of immortals is dismissed as illusory, and alchemical texts as mere absurdities. The *Wuzhen* book and the heart of the Perfected One remain utterly unrecognized in the world.

Then came Wumingzi, who took up the thread of the orthodox transmission. Mindful that the annotations had become corrupted through successive errors, he composed a new commentary for this book, releasing it into the world. Its chapters are divided, its phrases explicated, its fields and furrows delineated, and its distinctions made clear—all the celestial mechanisms are fully revealed within. Through deep reflection and careful thought, one may attain understanding on one’s own.

My great-uncle, from his earliest years, revered the Dao and studied this text for many years. Heaven awakened his heart, allowing him to hear the profound secrets. Drawing from what he learned from his father and teachers, as well as his own insights, he appended annotations to Wumingzi’s commentary, providing a standard for future seekers. Thus, they may avoid falling into illusion or drifting into absurdity.

How vast is this grace!

Wherein lies his heart? From past lives, he bore an affinity, and by good fortune, he obtained this book—truly a cause for celebration. Yet how might one find companions beyond the world’s dust, to tread the famed peaks and dwell in truth, to guard the immortal’s breeze and journey afar? To establish the crucible and furnace, to inhale and exhale the Dragon and Tiger, to invert mercury and lead, gathering them in an instant, gestating them for ten months, and refining them for nine years—then, serene, to ride the flying chariot across the Weak Waters, to mount the sacred turtle, and stand in the shadow of the immortals, hearing the great Dao of the formless and silent, to rescue those drowning in delusion. Such is his aspiration: to study under the Master of Purple Yang.

Written on the Shangsi day of the Dingchou year of the Zhiyuan era by the later student Dai Shun, bowing in reverence at the Great Cavern of Vermilion Lake.

*The Symbolism of the Golden Elixir*
Wumingzi, in his commentary on the *Awakening to Reality*, compiled and assembled the symbolic correspondences of the Golden Elixir—its metaphors and names may be said to be exhaustive. Following the foundational principles, he expanded and gathered the *Can Tong Qi* and the verses and songs of various immortal scriptures. All that he borrowed—from the celestial Dao, the images of the *Book of Changes*, human affairs, principles, and things—serves as metaphors for the Golden Elixir, its yin-yang symbolism divided into seven sections and appended to the commentary on the *Awakening to Reality*. May those who study immortality find it easier to investigate, knowing the distinctions and similarities between inner and outer, the mutual reflections of their symbolism, the sequence of the Five Phases’ transformations, and the difficulty of fixing their names. By clarifying their shared root and the reality they hold in common, and by distinguishing their metaphorical names, the wisdom of the immortal masters may be unified and grasped. Through this, one may forget the snare and attain the truth; through this, one may achieve the immortal’s Way—no small aid indeed.

Preface by Dai Qizong of the Shangyuan day of the Dingchou year of the Zhiyuan era.

True Mercury

At first ingestion, the body becomes light and robust, walking as if flying;
Next, one crosses rivers as if treading level ground;
Finally, one rides a turtle and mounts a phoenix—
Such are the efficacies of the Outer Elixir.
Fools rarely glimpse these alchemical scriptures.

*Awakening to Reality* with annotations and direct explanations elaborates further.
